Sabian Classification and the Error of Confusing Angels and Jinn
Author classifies Sabians and critiques confusion of angels and jinn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Islamic position on angels and jinn from the erroneous views of the Sabians and some theologians, and identify the sources of such confusion as critiqued by Ibn Taymiyya.

Core Idea
Confusing jinn with angels leads to theological error; revelation alone separates them.

Ibn Taymiyya here continues his critique of alternative sources of knowledge by examining the Sabians. He divides them into two types: monotheist Hanifs (who are Muslims) and polytheist Harranians. The Harranians follow a prophet named al-Baba who received revelations from the 'spirituality of Venus' – a planetary spirit. Notably, many Sabians and even some Muslim theologians fail to distinguish between angels and jinn, treating them as one genus. Ibn Taymiyya asserts the correct Islamic view: angels and jinn are distinct, and the spirits that aid polytheists are devils. This distinction is based on the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. Understanding this helps us see why Ibn Taymiyya insists that only revelation, not rationalist speculation, can provide certain knowledge about the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of Sabians
Locate where Ibn Taymiyya divides the Sabians into 'Hanifs' and 'polytheists'. Note that the Hanifs are considered Muslims, while the polytheists are the Harranians. This classification sets up the contrast between true monotheism and polytheistic spirit worship.
The Hanifs are those who follow the pure monotheism of Abraham.
2
Examine the Harranian beliefs
Read the description of the Harranian Sabians: they have a prophet named al-Baba with a scripture predicting future events, some of which came true. Their knowledge comes from the 'spirituality of Venus', a planetary spirit. This illustrates an alternative source of knowledge – one that Ibn Taymiyya argues is unreliable.
The well 'Bir 'Azzun' and the gathering of spirits are also mentioned.
3
Find the confusion between angels and jinn
Ibn Taymiyya points out that some Sabians call these spirits simply 'spirits' or 'spiritualities', while others call them all 'angels'. He notes that some Muslim theologians also treat angels and jinn as one genus, only differentiating by deeds. This confusion is the target of his critique.
The confusion leads to disputes about whether Iblis was an angel or not.
4
Identify the Islamic corrective
Ibn Taymiyya states the correct view: Muslims know that the spirits aiding polytheists are devils (shayatin), and they differentiate between angels and jinn. This is established by the Book (Quran), Sunnah, and consensus. Recognize that this is a revelation-based distinction, not a rational one.
This distinction is crucial for avoiding shirk and maintaining correct 'aqida.
5
Analyze the critique's nature
Ibn Taymiyya's critique here is epistemological and doctrinal: he is rejecting any source of knowledge that conflates jinn with angels or treats them equally. His grounds are scriptural and consensus-based, not philosophical. This reinforces his broader argument that only prophetic revelation gives certain knowledge of the unseen.
The critique targets both Sabian polytheists and Muslim theologians who err on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذكرنا أن الصابئة نوعان - حُنفاء ومشركون. فالحنفاء هم من المسلمين البابا» نبي الصابئة المؤمنين. وأما المشركون كالصابئة الذين بعث الله إليهم الخليل عليه السلام وغيرهم، الحرانيين فهؤلاء يقرون بهذا. والصابئة الحرّانيون لهم نبي على أصلهم يقال له «البابا». وله مصحف يذكر فيه كثيراً من الأخبار المستقبلة. ويذكر أن سيدته يعني رُوحانية الزُّهَرَة / أخبرته بذلك. وكثير منها صحيح، كإخباره بدخول المسلمين بلاد حران وغيرها، وفتحهم البلاد، وإهانتهم لطائفته . وكان بحران بئر يقال لها «بئر عزّون» يعظمونها تعظيماً كثيراً، وكان يذكر أن الأرواح تجتمع إليها ويذكر أنواعاً من هذه الأمور في مصحف له . وهو موجود قد قرأته أنا وغيري . وهذه الأرواح، منهم من يطلق عليها اسم «الأرواح» و «الروحانيات» ولا يفصل التفريق بين ومنهم من يسميها جميعها «الملائكة»، ولا يفرّقون بين الجن والملائكة . لا سيما وطائفة من أهل الكلام وغيرهم يجعلون الجن والملائكة جنساً واحداً وإنما يفرقون بالأعمال الصالحة والفاسدة، كالآدميين. ومن هذا تَنَازَع العلماء في إبليس، هل كان أم لا؟ وقد بسط الكلام عليه في غير هذا الموضع . وأما من يعرف حقيقة الأمر المسلمين فيعلمون أن الأرواح التي تُعِينُ المشركين هي الشياطين، ويفرقون بين الملائكة وبين الجنّ كما هو ثابت بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع.
And we have mentioned that the Sabians are of two types: Hanifs (monotheists) and polytheists. The Hanifs are from the Muslims – 'al-Baba' is the prophet of the believing Sabians. As for the polytheists, such as the Sabians to whom Allah sent al-Khalil (Abraham) peace be upon him and others, the Harranians – these acknowledge this. The Harranian Sabians have a prophet of their own called 'al-Baba'. He has a scripture in which he mentions many future events. He mentions that his lady – meaning the spirituality of Venus – informed him of that. Many of them are true, such as his report of the Muslims' entry into the land of Harran and other lands, their conquest of lands, and their humiliation of his sect. In Harran there was a well called 'Bir 'Azzun' which they greatly venerated, and he used to mention that the spirits gather at it, and he mentions types of these matters in his scripture. It exists, and I and others have read it. Regarding these spirits, some of them call them 'spirits' and 'spiritualities' and do not differentiate between them, and some of them call them all 'angels', and do not differentiate between jinn and angels. Especially a group of theological scholars (ahl al-kalam) and others make jinn and angels one genus, only distinguishing by good and evil deeds, like humans. From this, scholars have disputed about Iblis: was he [an angel] or not? And the discussion on that has been expanded elsewhere. As for those who know the true reality from the Muslims, they know that the spirits that help the polytheists are devils, and they differentiate between angels and jinn as is established by the Book and the Sunnah and consensus.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage provides a classification of the Sabians into two types: monotheist Hanifs (who are considered Muslims) and polytheist Harranians. The author describes the Harranian Sabians' prophet al-Baba and his scripture containing predictions, some correct. The text highlights the confusion among some groups who do not distinguish between angels and jinn, even among theologians. Ibn Taymiyya asserts the correct Islamic position: angels are distinct from jinn, and the spirits that assist polytheists are devils. This is based on Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. The point supports his earlier argument that alternative sources for unseen knowledge exist, but these are often from evil spirits.

الحنفاء
الحرانيون
روحانية الزهرة

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that angels and jinn are distinct creations, and the confusion between them leads to theological error; the correct distinction is known only through revelation.

Ibn Taymiyya's Ninth Proof: Imagination as a Source of Error
Author argues that reports based on connection to celestial powers or spirits are more often false than true

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's ninth proof against the reliability of reports from celestial connection and identify its psychological basis.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya turns the philosophers' own theory of imagination against them: imagination lies more than it truths.

Even if we grant the philosophers' claim that knowledge of the unseen comes from a connection to celestial souls, Ibn Taymiyya argues that the very mechanism they propose – the imagination – is inherently unreliable. In this proof, he uses their own framework to show that error exceeds truth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
What is the philosophers' claim about reports of the unseen that Ibn Taymiyya is attacking?
2
Extract the concessive structure
Ibn Taymiyya says 'even if we assume' – what does he grant for the sake of argument?
He grants the connection of the soul to a celestial psychic power or reports from spirits.
3
Locate the psychological argument
He refers to al-khayal (imagination) and al-hiss al-mushtarak (common sense). How does this support his critique?
Imagination depicts forms to common sense, and it lies more than it tells the truth.
4
Consider the incomplete contrast
The passage begins to mention the Muslim position. What is the implied contrast?
The Muslim position holds that prophetic revelation is immune from such errors, unlike the philosophers' imagined source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسع : إنه بتقدير أن يكون سببُ الإخبارات هو اتصال النفس بالقوة النفسانية الفلكية، أو هو إخبارُ الأرواح كما تقدم، فمعلوم أن الغلط في هذا أكثر من الصواب. أما على أصلهم، فلأن الخيال يصور للحس المشترك ما عَلِمَتْه النفسُ من الصور المناسبة، والخيال يَكْذِب أكثر مما يَصْدُق ؛ وأما على قول المسلمين وغيرهم،
The ninth [proof]: That if it is assumed that the cause of reports [of the unseen] is the connection of the soul to the celestial psychic power, or it is the report of spirits as previously, then it is known that error in this is more than correctness. According to their own [philosophers'] principles, because the imagination (al-khayal) depicts to the common sense (al-hiss al-mushtarak) what the soul knows of appropriate forms, and the imagination lies more than it tells the truth. And according to the statement of the Muslims and others...
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth proof in Ibn Taymiyya's critique. Even if we grant that reports of the unseen come from a connection to celestial soul or spirits, the rate of error is higher than correctness. The reason according to philosophers is that the imagination, which mediates knowledge to the common sense, is prone to falsehood. The author contrasts this with the Muslim position (which likely holds that prophetic revelation is immune from error). The passage is incomplete but establishes the general principle.

Key Terms
الخيال
الحس المشترك

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because philosophers are mistaken.

Key Takeaway
Even if a source of knowledge is granted, its mechanism may introduce error – Ibn Taymiyya exposes this through the philosophers' own psychology.

Ibn Taymiyya on Dreams as a Source of Knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya argues for knowledge through dreams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that true dreams are a valid source of knowledge, using Quranic verses and prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
True dreams are part of prophethood and a valid epistemic source.

Ibn Taymiyya challenges the logicians who dismiss dreams as irrelevant to knowledge. In this passage, he marshals Quranic verses and prophetic hadith to argue that the soul, when separated from the body in sleep, can receive direct knowledge from God. This is not a marginal idea but a foundational principle of prophetic revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being defended
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that the soul acquires knowledge after separation from the body, especially in sleep. This is the epistemological claim he is defending against the logicians.
The claim is that knowledge can be obtained through dreams.
2
Locate the scriptural support
Find the Quranic verse (39:42) and the prophetic supplications that describe God taking souls during sleep and death. These are used as evidence that the soul is temporarily separated from the body during sleep.
The verse is quoted in full: 'Allah takes the souls at the time of their death...'
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Look at the hadith that dreams are part of prophethood and that the Prophet's revelation began with true dreams. These hadith establish that dreams are a legitimate source of divine communication.
The hadith from Aisha and the statement 'The true dream is one of forty-six parts of prophethood'.
4
Understand the criterion for validity
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes between prophetic dreams (infallible revelation) and righteous dreams for believers (glad tidings). Not all dreams are authoritative; only those aligned with revelation are valid.
This criterion shows that Ibn Taymiyya is not endorsing all dream interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : حصول العلم للنفس بعد التجرد من البدن. إذا أوى إلى فراشه: اللهم ! أنت خلقت نفسي، وأنت تَتَوفَّاها ، لك مماتها ومحياها . إن أمسكتها فارحمها، وإن أرسلتها فاحفظها بما تحفظ به عبادك الصالحين. ويقول أيضاً : باسمك ربي وضعتُ جَنْبي، وباسمك أرفعه إن أمسكت نفسي فاغفر لها وارحمها، وإن أرسلتها فاحفظها بما تحفظ به عبادك الصالحين. وكان إذا استيقظ يقول: «الحمد لله الذي أحيانا بعدما أماتنا وإليه النشور». وقد قال الله تعالى : اللهُ يَتَوَفَّى الْأَنْفُسَ حِينَ مَوْتِهَا وَالَّتِي لَمْ تَمُتْ فِي مَنَامِهَا فَيُمْسِكُ الَّتِي قَضَى عَلَيْهَا الْمَوْتَ وَيُرْسِلُ الْأُخْرَى إِلَى أَجَلٍ مُّسَمًّى إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَتَفَكَّرُونَ. فأخبر سبحانه أنه يتوفى الأنفُسَ حين النوم وحين الموتِ، وأن ما يتوفاه حين النوم منه ما يقضي عليه الموتُ في نومه ومنه ما يُرسله وبسبب تجرّدها عن البدن يحصل لها من العلم ما يُلقيه الله إليها، إما بواسطة الملك الذي يُرِيَها ويحدّثها من الرؤيا، وإما بغير ذلك. قال تعالى: ﴿ وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَن يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْيًا أَوْ مِن وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ أَوْ يُرْسِلَ رَسُولًا فَيُوحِيَ بِإِذْنِهِ مَا يَشَاءُ إِنَّهُ عَلِيٌّ حَكِيمٌ ﴾. قال عبادة بن الصَّامِت : رؤيا المؤمن كلام يكلم به الرب عبده في المنام. وقد ثبت في الصحيح عن النبي أنه قال : «لم يبق بعدي من النبوّة إلا المبشرات، وهي الرؤيا الصالحة يراها الرجلُ الصالح أو تُرَى له ». وقال : الرؤيا الصالحة جزء من ستة وأربعين جزءاً من النبوة. وفي الصحيحين عن عائشة قالت : أول ما بدىء به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الوحي الرؤيا الصادقة في النوم، فكان لا يرى رؤيا إلا جاءت مثل فَلَقِ الصُّبح . ثم حُبّب إليه الخلاء، فكان يخلو بغار حِرَاءٍ فيتحنّتُ فيه، وهو التعبدُ، الليالي ذواتِ العَدَد. وقد قال تعالى : ﴿ اللهُ أَعْلَمُ حَيْثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسَالَتَهُ ﴾. فلا ريب أن ما يجعله الله في النفوس وغيرها يجعله بعد إعدادها لذلك وتسويتها لما يُلقى فيها. فهذا ونحوه حق يقول به السلف وجمهور المسلمين. وإنما يُنكر ذلك مَنْ ينكر الحِكم والأسباب من أهل الكلام. والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بدىء أولاً بالرؤيا الصادقة. فإن رؤيا الأنبياء وحي معصوم، كما قال ابن عباس وعُبيد بن عُمير وغيرهما: رؤيا الأنبياء وحي وقرأ قول إبراهيم عليه السلام : ﴿ إِنِّي أَرَى فِي الْمَنَامِ أَنِّي أَذْبَحُكَ ﴾. ثم إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نقل من درجة إلى درجة ، ثم بعد هذا جاءه الملك فخاطبه بالكلام . فأحياناً يأتيه في الباطن فيكلمه، وأحياناً يتمثل له في صورة رجل فيكلمه . ثم عُرج به إلى ربه ليلة الإسراء . فما ادعوه من أن الرؤيا قد يحصل بها معرفةُ المغيبات حق. وهذا يُحتج به على من
The Fourth Station - The Fourteenth Aspect: The acquisition of knowledge for the soul after separation from the body. When he went to his bed: 'O Allah! You created my soul, and You take it away; to You belong its death and its life. If You keep it, have mercy on it; if You send it forth, protect it with what You protect Your righteous servants.' And he also said: 'In Your name, my Lord, I lay my side, and in Your name I raise it; if You keep my soul, forgive it and have mercy on it; if You send it forth, protect it with what You protect Your righteous servants.' And when he woke up he would say: 'Praise be to Allah who gave us life after He caused us to die, and to Him is the resurrection.' And Allah Almighty said: 'Allah takes the souls at the time of their death, and those that do not die during their sleep; He keeps those for which He has decreed death, and sends the others for a specified term. Indeed in that are signs for a people who give thought.' So He, glorified, informed that He takes the souls during sleep and at death, and that what He takes during sleep, some of it He decrees death upon in its sleep and some He sends, and due to its separation from the body, there occurs for it knowledge that Allah casts into it, either by means of the angel who shows it and speaks to it in the dream, or otherwise. Allah Almighty said: 'And it is not for any human being that Allah should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil or by sending a messenger to reveal by His permission what He wills; indeed He is Most High, All-Wise.' Ubada ibn al-Samit said: 'The dream of a believer is speech with which the Lord speaks to His servant in sleep.' And it is confirmed in the Sahih that the Prophet said: 'Nothing remains after me of prophethood except the glad tidings, and they are the righteous dream that the righteous man sees or is seen for him.' And he said: 'The righteous dream is one part of forty-six parts of prophethood.' And in the two Sahihs, Aisha said: 'The first thing that began with the Messenger of Allah from revelation was the true dream in sleep; he would not see a dream except it came like the break of dawn. Then seclusion became beloved to him, so he would go to the cave of Hira and engage in devotion there, which is worship, for many nights.' And Allah said: 'Allah knows best where to place His message.' So there is no doubt that what Allah places in souls and other things, He places it after preparing them for that and making them suitable for what is cast into them. This and the like is true, and it is what the Salaf and the majority of Muslims say. Only those who deny wisdom and causes from the People of Kalam reject that. And the Prophet began first with true dreams. For the dreams of the prophets are infallible revelation, as Ibn Abbas and Ubayd ibn Umayr and others said: 'The dreams of the prophets are revelation' and he recited the saying of Ibrahim, peace be upon him: 'Indeed I saw in a dream that I slaughter you.' Then the Prophet was transferred from one degree to another, then after this the angel came to him and addressed him with speech. Sometimes he would come to him in the inner being and speak to him, and sometimes he would appear to him in the form of a man and speak to him. Then he was ascended to his Lord on the Night of Isra. So what they claim — that knowledge of unseen things may be obtained through dreams — is true. And this is used as evidence against those who...
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the logicians (and those who deny divine wisdom and causes) who reject the acquisition of knowledge through dreams and angelic revelation. Ibn Taymiyya argues that the soul, upon separation from the body in sleep or death, receives knowledge directly from God, either through an angel in a dream or otherwise. He supports this with Qur'anic verses about God taking souls during sleep and death, and with prophetic hadith about sleep supplications. He then cites the famous hadith that nothing remains of prophethood except glad tidings (true dreams), and that the Prophet's revelation began with true dreams. The author emphasizes that this is the position of the Salaf and the majority of Muslims, and only those who deny divine wisdom and secondary causes (the mutakallimun) reject it. He traces the stages of prophethood: first true dreams, then the angel coming in the heart, then in human form, then the ascension. The conclusion is that dreams can give knowledge of the unseen, which is a valid argument against those who deny the angel and prophetic revelation. The passage is a typical example of Ibn Taymiyya's method of using scriptural and traditional evidence to refute philosophical claims.

Key Terms
الرؤيا
التجرد عن البدن
الوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the status of the true dream for a prophet?
A) It is simply a psychological reflection
B) It is infallible revelation (wahy)
C) It is a possibility but not certain
D) It is only for non-prophets

Key Takeaway
True dreams are a valid source of knowledge, especially for prophets, and are part of the prophetic revelation process.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the hadith 'The true dream is part of prophethood' and explain, in two sentences, how Ibn Taymiyya uses it to prove that dreams are a valid source of knowledge.
?
Using Quran 39:42, write a one-paragraph argument that the soul's separation in sleep allows it to receive knowledge from God, as Ibn Taymiyya does.

beginner

The Stages of Prophetic Revelation (according to Ibn Taymiyya)
Ibn Taymiyya outlines the stages of prophetic revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and sequence the stages of revelation as described by Ibn Taymiyya: true dreams, internal angelic speech, angel in human form, and ascension.

Core Idea
Revelation begins with dreams and culminates in direct divine encounter.

Ibn Taymiyya, in the same passage, provides a detailed chronology of how revelation came to Prophet Muhammad. Starting with true dreams, it progressed to angelic communication in the heart, then in visible form, and finally the ascension. This sequence is crucial for understanding how God communicates with prophets.

Guided Path
1
List the stages from the passage
Extract the four stages: 1) true dreams, 2) inner revelation (angel speaking in the heart), 3) angel appearing in human form, 4) ascension to his Lord on the Night of Isra.
The stages are described in chronological order from the beginning of revelation.
2
Find the evidence for each stage
The hadith of Aisha provides the first stage: the revelation began with true dreams. The verse 42:51 describes the types of revelation. The ascension is mentioned explicitly as the final stage.
Ibn Taymiyya also cites Ibrahim's dream as an example from earlier prophets.
3
Observe the hierarchy of closeness
Each stage brings the Prophet closer to direct divine communication. Dreams are the most indirect; the ascension is the most direct. This shows a progression in intensity.
This hierarchy indicates that dreams are not inferior but foundational.
4
Relate this to the critique of logicians
By demonstrating that revelation has stages and that dreams are its first stage, Ibn Taymiyya refutes those who deny revelatory knowledge. The stages prove that God uses multiple means to communicate, including dreams.
The logicians' denial of dream-based knowledge is thus invalidated.

The Philosophers' Theory of Prophecy: Two Powers
Explaining the philosophers' theory of prophecy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two components of the philosophers' theory of prophetic knowledge and explain how they replace Islamic revelation with logical syllogism and celestial abstraction.

Core Idea
Philosophers reduce prophecy to mental abstraction, not divine revelation.

Ibn Taymiyya critiques a fundamental deviation: the claim that prophets acquire knowledge through logical syllogism and connection to the celestial soul. He explains the philosophers' model, which denies angelic revelation and God's knowledge of particulars. In this lesson, we will dissect that model to understand exactly what Ibn Taymiyya is refuting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' denial
Locate in the passage where Ibn Taymiyya states what the philosophers deny: no living angel, no speech of God heard by the angel, and God does not know particulars. Write down these three denials.
These denials form the basis of their alternative theory.
2
Extract the two prophetic powers
Find the two kinds of special characteristics of prophecy according to the philosophers: the scientific power (al-quwwa al-'ilmiyya) and the practical power (al-quwwa al-'amaliyya). Note how each is defined.
The scientific power is further divided into two sub-parts.
3
Analyze the scientific power's sub-parts
Within the scientific power, there are two ways to attain knowledge: by logical syllogism (for universals) and by abstraction similar to sleep until connection to the celestial soul (for particulars). Explain how imagination then produces images and sounds which they call angels and God's speech.
This is the heart of the philosophical theory's mechanism.
4
Compare to Islamic belief
Contrast this model with the orthodox Islamic view: revelation comes from God via angels with real speech, and God knows all particulars. List the key differences.
This comparison clarifies why Ibn Taymiyya considers the theory false.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : فساد جعلهم علوم الأنبياء تحصل بواسطة القياس المنطقي

ينكر هذا الجنس مطلقاً، ولكن لا تجعل النبوة كلها من هذا الجنس . فمن الباطل ما ادعوه في النبوة وفي كيفيتها، حيث زعموا أنه ليس هناك مَلَك حي يأتي بالوحي من الله ، ولا الله كلام يتكلم به يَسْمعه المَلَكُ فينزل به، ولا يعرف الله جزئيات الأمور حتى يكتبها عنده، أو حتى يُخبر بها الملك والملك يخبر بها النبي ، أو يخبر بها النبي ابتداء .

وزعموا أنه ليس الله ما يدبر به أمر السموات والأرض إلا مجرد حركة الفلك . وأثبتوا النبوة كما أثبتها الفلاسفة نبوة حال كثير من أحوال أوساط المسلمين خير منها . فإن كثيراً من أوساط المسلمين له من العلم والعمل أعظم مما أثبته هؤلاء للأنبياء. فإنهم جعلوا خواص النبوة نوعين : القوة العلمية التي ينال بها العلم، إما بواسطة القياس المنطقي، وإما بواسطة التجرد الذي هو كتجرد النائم حتى تتصل بالنفس الفلكية ؛ والثاني القوة العَمَلية، وهو أن تكون نفسه قوية على التصرف في هَيُولى العالم بحيث تحدث عنها عجائب. والنوع الأول يتضمن أمرين: أحدهما معرفة العلوم الكلية بالقياس المنطقي، والثاني معرفة الجزئيات بهذا الاتصال. ثم الخيال يصور المعقولات في الصور المناسبة لها ويَنْقُشُها في الحس المشترك، فيرى الإنسانُ في باطنه صوراً ويسمع أصواتاً. وتلك الصور عندهم ملائكة الله ، وتلك الأصوات كلام الله .

ادعاء بعضهم من كلام صاحب الكتب المَضْنُون بها على غير أهلها وغير ذلك مما يناسب ذلك . فصار بعضهم يرى أن باب النبوّة مفتوح لا يمكن إغلاقه. فيقول كما كان ابن سبعين يقول : لَقَدْ زَرَّبَ ابنُ آمنة حيث قال لا نبي بعدي. أو يرى لكونه أشدّ تعظيماً للشريعة أن باب النبوة قد أُغلق فيدّعي أن الولاية أعظم من النبوة، وأن خاتَمَ الأولياء أعلم بالله من خاتم الأنبياء، وأن خاتم الأنبياء بل وجميع الأنبياء إنما يستفيدون معرفة الله من مشكوة خاتم الأولياء. ويقول: إنه يوافق النبيَّ في معرفة الشريعة العَمَلية لأنه يَرَى الأمر على ما هو عليه فلا بد أن يراه هكذا، وإنه أعلم من النبي بالحقائق العلمية لأنه يأخذ من المَعْدِن الذي يأخذ منه الملك الذي يُوحِي به إلى الرسول .

وهذا بناء على أصول هؤلاء الفلاسفة الكفار الذين هم أكفر من اليهود والنصارى، الذين سلك هؤلاء سبيلهم. ولكن غيروا عباراتهم فأخذوا عبارات الملحدين في عبارات المسلمين الموجودة في كلام الله ورسوله وسلف الأمة وعلمائها وعُبّادها ومَنْ دخل في هؤلاء من الصوفية المتبعين للكتاب والسنة، كالفضيل بن عياض، وأبي سليمان الدَّاراني، ومعروف الكرخي، والسَّرِي السَّقَطي، والجنيد، وسهل بن عبد الله التستري.
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: The corruption of their making the sciences of the prophets acquired by means of logical syllogism.

He denies this category absolutely, but he does not make all prophecy of this category. So false is what they claimed regarding prophecy and its modality, where they asserted that there is no living angel that brings revelation from God, and no speech of God that He speaks which the angel hears and then descends with it, and that God does not know particulars of things so that He writes them with Him, or so that the angel informs the prophet, or the prophet informs [others] initially.

And they claimed that there is no governance of the heavens and earth except the mere motion of the sphere. And they affirmed prophecy as the philosophers affirmed it—a state whose many conditions are exceeded by the conditions of middle-class Muslims. For many middle-class Muslims have knowledge and action greater than what these [philosophers] affirmed for the prophets. For they made the special characteristics of prophecy two kinds: the scientific power by which one attains knowledge, either by means of logical syllogism or by means of abstraction which is like the abstraction of the sleeper until he connects to the celestial soul; and the second is the practical power, which is that his soul is strong in acting upon the matter of the world so that wonders are produced from it. And the first kind includes two matters: one is knowledge of universal sciences by logical syllogism, and the second is knowledge of particulars by this connection. Then the imagination pictures intelligibles in forms appropriate to them and inscribes them in the common sense, so that the human sees images and hears voices within himself. And those images are, according to them, the angels of God, and those voices are the speech of God.

And the claim of some of them from the speech of the author of the books withheld from those not worthy of them, and other things that correspond to that. So some of them came to see that the door of prophecy is open and cannot be closed. So he says, as Ibn Sab'in used to say: 'Indeed the son of Aminah (i.e., the Prophet) has confined [the matter] where he said there is no prophet after me.' Or he sees, because of his greater veneration of the Sharia, that the door of prophecy has been closed, and so he claims that sainthood (wilaya) is greater than prophethood (nubuwwa), and that the Seal of the Saints is more knowledgeable of God than the Seal of the Prophets, and that the Seal of the Prophets, indeed all the prophets, only derive knowledge of God from the niche of the Seal of the Saints. And he says: that he agrees with the prophet in knowledge of the practical Sharia because he sees the matter as it is, so he must see it thus, and that he is more knowledgeable than the prophet of scientific truths because he takes from the mine from which the angel who reveals to the messenger takes.

And this is built upon the foundations of these disbelieving philosophers, who are more disbelieving than Jews and Christians, whose path these people have followed. But they changed their expressions, so they took the expressions of atheists into the expressions of Muslims found in the speech of God and His Messenger, the predecessors of the nation, its scholars, its worshippers, and those among the Sufis who follow the Book and the Sunna, such as al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad, Abu Sulayman al-Darani, Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, al-Sari al-Saqati, al-Junayd, and Sahl ibn 'Abd Allah al-Tustari.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of the philosophical theory of prophecy, specifically the claim that prophets acquire their knowledge through logical syllogism (qiyas mantiqi) and connection to the celestial soul (nafs falakiyya). He begins by denying this category entirely, asserting that prophecy is not of this kind. He then exposes the falsehoods underlying the philosophers' view: they deny the existence of an angel bringing revelation, deny that God speaks in a way that can be heard, and even deny that God knows particulars. They reduce the governance of the heavens and earth to mere celestial motion. According to them, the special characteristics of prophecy are two: a scientific power attained either through logical syllogism or through abstraction until connection to the celestial soul, and a practical power to produce wonders in the world. The first power comprises knowledge of universals via syllogism and knowledge of particulars via that connection. They further claim that imagination then pictures the intelligibles and inscribes them in the common sense, so that the prophet sees images (which they call angels) and hears sounds (which they call God's speech). Ibn Taymiyya then shows the consequences of this deviant view: some people, influenced by this philosophy, claim that the door of prophecy remains open, or more dangerously, that sainthood (wilaya) is greater than prophethood. They assert that the Seal of the Saints knows God better than the Seal of the Prophets, and that all prophets derive their knowledge from the Seal of the Saints. This, Ibn Taymiyya states, is built on the foundations of these disbelieving philosophers who are worse than Jews and Christians. However, he distinguishes between the deviant Sufis who follow these philosophers and the true Sufis who adhere to the Book and Sunna, listing early pious figures like al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad and al-Junayd.

Key Terms
القياس المنطقي
النفس الفلكية
النبوة
القوة العلمية
القوة العملية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers as described by Ibn Taymiyya, how does the prophet know particulars?
A) Through logical syllogism
B) Through connection to the celestial soul
C) Through angelic revelation
D) Through intuition

Key Takeaway
The philosophical theory replaces divine revelation with a natural process of mental abstraction and celestial connection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the method from this lesson, identify the components of the philosophical theory of prophecy as presented by Ibn Taymiyya. Write them in a bullet list: the denial of angel, denial of God's speech, denial of God's knowledge of particulars, the two powers, and the role of imagination.

Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of the Philosophical Prophecy Theory
Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of the philosophical theory of prophecy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of the philosophical theory of prophecy and identify its dangerous consequences for the status of prophethood.

Core Idea
A flawed theory leads to heresy: wilaya elevated above nubuwwa.

Ibn Taymiyya does not merely describe the philosophical theory; he exposes its logical and theological corruption. He then shows how this theory leads some to claim sainthood superior to prophethood—a clear deviation. This lesson will guide you through his refutation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core falsehoods
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what are the main false claims of the philosophers? List them: denial of a living angel, denial of God's speech, denial of God's knowledge of particulars, reduction of cosmic governance to mere celestial motion.
These falsehoods are the foundation of their erroneous theory.
2
Understand the basis of their theory
The philosophers base prophecy on two powers: scientific and practical. The scientific power is attained via logical syllogism or abstraction to connect to the celestial soul. Note how this excludes any supernatural revelation.
This naturalistic framework is what Ibn Taymiyya rejects.
3
Trace the logical consequences
From the premise that prophecy is a natural human attainment, some conclude that the door of prophecy remains open. Worse, to preserve the seal of prophethood, they claim sainthood (wilaya) is greater than prophethood. Show how this follows from their premises.
Ibn Taymiyya highlights this as the ultimate corruption.
4
Assess Ibn Taymiyya's verdict
He calls these philosophers more disbelieving than Jews and Christians. Why? Because they deny fundamental Islamic tenets while using Islamic terminology. Summarize his overall argument.
This verdict shows the severity of the deviation.

Commentary
This passage is a critique by Ibn Taymiyya of the philosophical theory of prophecy, specifically the claim that prophets acquire their knowledge through logical syllogism (qiyas mantiqi) and connection to the celestial soul (nafs falakiyya). He begins by denying this category entirely, asserting that prophecy is not of this kind. He then exposes the falsehoods underlying the philosophers' view: they deny the existence of an angel bringing revelation, deny that God speaks in a way that can be heard, and even deny that God knows particulars. They reduce the governance of the heavens and earth to mere celestial motion. According to them, the special characteristics of prophecy are two: a scientific power attained either through logical syllogism or through abstraction until connection to the celestial soul, and a practical power to produce wonders in the world. The first power comprises knowledge of universals via syllogism and knowledge of particulars via that connection. They further claim that imagination then pictures the intelligibles and inscribes them in the common sense, so that the prophet sees images (which they call angels) and hears sounds (which they call God's speech). Ibn Taymiyya then shows the consequences of this deviant view: some people, influenced by this philosophy, claim that the door of prophecy remains open, or more dangerously, that sainthood (wilaya) is greater than prophethood. They assert that the Seal of the Saints knows God better than the Seal of the Prophets, and that all prophets derive their knowledge from the Seal of the Saints. This, Ibn Taymiyya states, is built on the foundations of these disbelieving philosophers who are worse than Jews and Christians. However, he distinguishes between the deviant Sufis who follow these philosophers and the true Sufis who adhere to the Book and Sunna, listing early pious figures like al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad and al-Junayd.

Checkpoint
What does Ibn Taymiyya say about the status of the philosophers compared to Jews and Christians?
A) They are better
B) They are equal
C) They are more disbelieving
D) They are not discussed

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the philosophical theory by exposing its false premises and showing that it logically leads to the heresy of elevating sainthood above prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the philosophical claim that prophetic knowledge is acquired via syllogism. Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, show how this leads to the denial of angelic revelation. Write a short refutation (3-5 sentences) that identifies the false premise and its dangerous consequence.
?
Find a contemporary claim that elevates sainthood above prophethood (e.g., in some Sufi writings) and show how it derives from the same philosophical principles that Ibn Taymiyya refuted.

Critique of False Sainthood: Demonic Inspiration vs. Prophetic Path
Ibn Taymiyya critiques Ibn Arabi's claim of divine kashf, asserting demonic origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and critique claims of spiritual experience that are not grounded in the Quran and Sunnah, using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria.

Core Idea
Not every spiritual experience is from God; it may be from devils if it contradicts the prophetic path.

Ibn Taymiyya dismantles the claims of those who assert direct knowledge from God without following the Prophet. He warns that such experiences are often demonic in origin, drawing parallels with false prophets and soothsayers. This lesson equips you to discern authentic sainthood from counterfeit spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claimant's Position
Find the claim that Ibn Taymiyya is attacking. Ibn Arabi and others assert that they receive knowledge through kashf (unveiling) and mushahada (witnessing), which they consider higher than rational reflection.
Look for phrases like 'يعظمون طريق الكشف والمشاهدة'.
2
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's Objection
Ibn Taymiyya argues that such kashf is mostly imagination (khayal) and that the source is actually devils, not God or angels. He says that if Ibn Arabi truly received revelations from a spirit, it was a devil, like the ones that inspired Musaylima.
Notice the parallel: 'كما كان مسيلمة الكذاب يلقي إليه شيطان'.
3
Analyze the Evidence and Examples
Ibn Taymiyya provides historical examples: false prophets (Musaylima, al-Aswad al-Ansi), soothsayers of the Arabs, and ascetics of polytheists and Christians. All had familiar spirits from the jinn that gave them supernatural abilities.
He distinguishes true karamat (miracles of saints) from satanic acts (ahwal shaytaniyya).
4
Apply the Criterion of Conformity to Sharia
The key test: any claim to sainthood or spiritual experience must be measured against the Book and Sunnah. Those who depart from prophetic guidance are susceptible to demonic influence, and their jinn correspond to their own level of sin and ignorance.
See the final sentence: 'وإن كانوا فسّاقاً فجتُهم من جنسهم' etc.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : نزول الشياطين على مدعي الولاية. أخذوا معاني أولئك الملاحدة فعبّروا عنها بالعبارات الموجودة في كلام من هو معظم عند المسلمين، فيظن مَنْ سمع ذلك أن أولئك المعظَّمين إنما عنوا بهذه العبارات الموجودة في كلامهم ما أراده هؤلاء الملحدون، كما فعلت ملاحدة الشيعة الإسماعيلية ونحوهم. فمحمد عندهم يأخذ من الملك الذي هو عندهم خيال في نفسه، وذلك الخيال يأخذ عن العقل. فمحمد عندهم يأخذ عن جبريل، وهذا الخيال هو جبريل. وجبريل يأخذ من العقل، وهو المعدن من النفس الفلكية. فزعم ابن عربي عن الذي يأخذ منه جبريل. فإن ابن عربي وهؤلاء يعظمون طريق الكشف والمشاهدة والرياضة والعبادة، ويَذُمُّون طريق النظر والقياس وما يدعونه من الكشف والمشاهدة عامته خيالات في أنفسهم، ويسمونها حقيقة. ولهذا يقول «باب أرض الحقيقة»، وهي أرض الخيال. وقد ادعى أن الفتوحات الملكية ألقاها إليه روح بمكة. وإذا كان صادقاً فقد ألقاها إليه شيطان من الشياطين، كما كان مُسَيْلِمَة الكذَّابُ يُلقي إليه شيطان، وكذلك الأسود العنسي، وكذلك غيرُهما من المتنبئين الكذابين. وكذلك الذين يدعون الولاية بدون متابعة الرسول تَنَزَّلُ عليهم الشياطين، تنزل الشياطين على مدعي الولاية وتُخبرهم بأشياء، وتأمرهم بأشياء. وربما أحضرت لهم طعاماً ونفقة وغير ذلك. وربما حملت أحدهم في الهواء إلى مكان ونحو ذلك. فهم في الأولياء من جنس مُسَيْلمه الكذاب وأمثاله في الأنبياء ولهم أحوال شيطانية يظنونها من كرامات أولياء الله، وإنما أحوال أعداء الله. وهؤلاء من جنس كهان العرب الذين كان يكون لأحدهم رئي من الجن من جنس شيوخ العبّاد الذين للمشركين من الهند والترك، والحبشة، وغيرهم الكفار، أو من جنس شيوخ النصارى. فإن هؤلاء شيوخ المشركين وأهل الكتاب لهم شياطين تقترن بهم. وكذلك للداخل في المَشْيَخة والدين والزهد والعبادة مع الخروج عن الكتاب والسنة ممن يَدَّعي الإسلام. ثم إن كانوا كفاراً منافقين فجتُهم من جنسهم، وإن كانوا فسّاقاً فجتُهم من جنسهم، وإن كانوا أهل جهل وبدعة بلا علم كان جنّهم من جنسهم.
The Fourth Station - The Fourteenth Aspect: The descent of devils upon those who claim sainthood. They took the meanings of those atheists and expressed them using phrases found in the speech of one who is venerated among Muslims, so that whoever hears that thinks that those venerated ones only meant by these phrases found in their speech what these atheists intended, as the atheists of the Ismaili Shia and others did. So, Muhammad according to them takes from the angel who according to them is an imagination in himself, and that imagination takes from the intellect. So Muhammad according to them takes from Gabriel, and this imagination is Gabriel. And Gabriel takes from the intellect, which is the source of the celestial soul. So Ibn Arabi claimed about that from which Gabriel takes. For Ibn Arabi and these people magnify the path of unveiling and witnessing, spiritual exercise and worship, and they blame the path of reflection and analogy, and what they call unveiling and witnessing is mostly imaginations in themselves, and they call it truth. Hence he says 'the chapter of the land of truth', and it is the land of imagination. And he claimed that the Meccan Revelations were cast to him by a spirit in Mecca. If he is truthful, then a devil from among the devils cast it to him, just as the liar Musaylima used to have a devil cast to him, and likewise al-Aswad al-Ansi, and likewise other false prophets. And likewise, those who claim sainthood without following the Messenger have devils descend upon them, devils descend upon the claimants of sainthood and inform them of things, and command them with things. And perhaps they bring them food and expenses and other things. And perhaps they carry one of them in the air to a place and the like. So they among the saints are of the type of the liar Musaylima and his likes among the prophets, and they have satanic states which they think are miracles of the saints of God, but they are states of the enemies of God. And these are of the type of the soothsayers of the Arabs who used to have a familiar spirit from the jinn of the type of the shaykhs of the worshippers of the polytheists of India, Turkey, Abyssinia, and other disbelievers, or of the type of the Christian monks. For these shaykhs of the polytheists and the People of the Book have devils that associate with them. And likewise for those who enter into shaykhdom, religion, asceticism, and worship while departing from the Book and the Sunnah among those who claim Islam. Then if they are disbelieving hypocrites, their jinn are of their type; if they are sinful, their jinn are of their type; if they are people of ignorance and innovation without knowledge, their jinn are of their type.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a critique of those who claim sainthood and direct spiritual knowledge without following the prophetic example. Ibn Taymiyya targets Ibn Arabi and others who exalt mystical unveiling (kashf) over rational inquiry and adherence to revelation. He argues that such individuals have taken the ideas of atheists and dressed them in Islamic terminology to deceive the masses. Specifically, he refutes Ibn Arabi's claim that the 'Meccan Revelations' (al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya) were dictated by a spirit, asserting that if true, it was a devil, not an angel. He draws a parallel with false prophets like Musaylima and al-Aswad al-Ansi, who also received revelations from devils. Those who claim to be saints without following the Prophet are thus subject to demonic influences: devils descend upon them, bring them food, carry them through the air, etc. These phenomena are not true miracles (karamat) but demonic acts (ahwal shaytaniyya). He compares them to the soothsayers of pre-Islamic Arabia and the ascetics of polytheists and Christians, who have familiar spirits from the jinn. The devils that associate with such people correspond to their own state: if they are hypocritical disbelievers, their jinn are of that type; if they are sinners or ignorant innovators, their jinn match them. The lesson is a stern warning against any claim to spiritual authority that diverges from the Book and Sunnah.

Key Terms
الكشف والمشاهدة
الحقيقة
الشياطين
الولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the source of the experiences claimed by those who assert sainthood without following the Prophet?
A) Angels
B) Devils
C) Rational intellect
D) Their own imagination

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya teaches that authentic spirituality is measured by adherence to the Quran and Sunnah, not by subjective experiences which may be demonic in origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a contemporary claim of spiritual experience (e.g., someone claims to receive direct commands from God in dreams). Using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria, determine whether this experience is likely from God or from devils. State which elements of the claim align or conflict with the Quran and Sunnah.
?
Research a historical figure who claimed sainthood outside the framework of the Book and Sunnah (e.g., Musaylima, al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah, or a modern cult leader). Explain how their experiences fit Ibn Taymiyya's description of demonic descent and why they were not true saints.

Angels as Real Beings: Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of Imaginary Forms
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the logicians' claim that angels are imaginary forms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that angels are living, speaking beings and identify the philosophical claims he refutes.

Core Idea
Angels are not mental images; they are real beings known through revelation.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya directly challenges the philosophers and logicians who reduce angels to imaginary forms impressed in the common sense or to abstract intellects. He counters with the certainty of mutawatir prophetic reports that describe angels as living, speaking beings who appear physically to humans. This lesson examines his central refutation and the logical structure of his critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophical claim under attack
Find in the Arabic the description of 'ṣūra khayāliyya' and 'uqūl wa nufūs'. What exactly do the logicians say angels are?
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's counter-claim
What does he assert based on mutawatir reports? Look for key phrases like 'al-malāʾika aḥyāʾ nāṭiqūn'.
3
Analyze the supporting evidence
How does he use the Qur'anic verses and hadith about Jibril to support his claim? Note the specific examples.
4
Evaluate the force of the refutation
Does Ibn Taymiyya's appeal to tawātur invalidate the philosophical view? Why does he consider this decisive?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه العاشر: إنه من المتواتر عن الأنبياء - صلوات الله عليهم - أن الملائكة أحياء ناطقون يأتونهم عن الله بما يخبر به ويأمر به تارة، وينصرونهم ويقاتلون معهم تارة. وكانت الملائكة أحياناً تأتيهم في صورة البشر والحاضرون يرونهم. وقد أخبر الله عن الملائكة في كتابه بأخبار متنوعة. وذلك يناقض ما يزعمونه من أن الملك إنما هو الصورة الخيالية التي ترتسم في الحس المشترك، أو أنها العقول والنفوس.

عظم خلق جبریل

الأخبار المتواترة بمجيء الملائكة في صورة البشر

قال الله تعالى: (مَلَتَهُ شَدِيدُ القوى) (ذُو مِرَّةٍ فَاسْتَوَى) (وَهُوَ بِالْأُفُقِ الْأَعْلَى) (ثُمَّ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى) (فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى) (فَأَوْحَى إِلَى عَبْدِهِ مَا أَوْحَى) (مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى) (أَفَتُمَارُونَهُ عَلَى مَا يَرَى) (وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ نَزْلَةً أُخْرَى) (عِنْدَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنْتَهَى) (عِنْدَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى) (إِذْ يَغْشَى السِّدْرَةَ مَا يَغْشَى) (مَا زَاغَ الْبَصَرُ وَمَا طَغَى) (لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى) [سورة النجم: ١٨-٥].

وفي الصحيحين عن مسروق قال: كنت متكئاً عند عائشة رضي الله عنها، فقالت: يا أبا عائشة ثلاث من تكلم بواحدة منهن فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. قلت: ما هن؟ قالت: من زعم أن محمداً رأى ربه فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. ومن زعم أنه يعلم ما في غدٍ فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. ومن زعم أنه كتم شيئاً مما أوحي إليه فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. قال: وكنت متكئاً فجلست فقلت: يا أم المؤمنين أنظريني، ولا تعجليني. ألم يقل الله تعالى: (وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ بِالْأُفُقِ الْمُبِينِ) [سورة التكوير: ٢٣] (وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ نَزْلَةً أُخْرَى) [سورة النجم: ١٣]؟ فقالت: أنا أول هذه الأمة عن ذلك، رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: إنما هو جبريل، لم أره على صورته التي خلق عليها غير هاتين المرتين رأيته منهبطاً من السماء ساداً عظم خلقه ما بين السماء والأرض. وفي لفظ: فقلت فأين قوله عز وجل: (ثُمَّ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى) (فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى) (فَأَوْحَى إِلَى عَبْدِهِ مَا أَوْحَى) [سورة النجم: ٨-١٠]؟ قالت: إنما ذاك جبريل عليه السلام، كان يأتيه في صورة الرجال وإنه أتاه هذه المرة في صورته التي هي صورته، فسد أفق السماء.

وفي الصحيحين أيضاً عن الشيباني قال: سألت زر بن حبيش عن قول الله: (قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى) قال: أخبرني ابن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى جبريل له ست مئة جناح. وعن ابن مسعود أيضاً قال: (مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى) قال: رأى جبريل له ست مئة جناح. وعنه أيضاً: (لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى) قال: رأى جبريل في صورته له ست مئة جناح. وقال البخاري في بعض طرقه: رأى رفرفاً أخضر قد سد الأفق. وعن عبد الله قال: (لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى) قال: رأى رفرفاً أخضر.
The tenth aspect: It is from the mutawatir (widely transmitted) reports from the prophets - blessings of Allah be upon them - that the angels are living, speaking beings, who come to them from Allah with what He informs and commands sometimes, and they support them and fight with them sometimes. And the angels would sometimes come to them in human form, and those present would see them. And Allah has informed about the angels in His Book with various reports. And that contradicts what they claim, that the angel is only the imaginary form that is impressed in the common sense, or that they are the intellects and souls.

The greatness of the creation of Jibril

The mutawatir reports of the coming of angels in human form

Allah the Exalted said: 'One of mighty power' (53:5-18) ... [Surah An-Najm 5-18].

And in the Two Sahihs from Masruq: I was reclining near Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, and she said: O Abu Aisha, three things - whoever speaks of one of them has fabricated a great lie against Allah. I said: What are they? She said: Whoever claims that Muhammad saw his Lord has fabricated a great lie against Allah. And whoever claims that he knows what is in tomorrow has fabricated a great lie against Allah. And whoever claims that he concealed something that was revealed to him has fabricated a great lie against Allah. He said: I was reclining so I sat up and said: O Mother of the Believers, give me respite and do not hasten me. Did not Allah say: 'And indeed he saw him in the clear horizon' (81:23) and 'And indeed he saw him another time' (53:13)? She said: I am the first of this community to ask the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about that, and he said: 'It is only Jibril. I did not see him in the form in which he was created except on these two occasions. I saw him descending from heaven, his enormous creation filling what is between heaven and earth.' And in another wording: I said: Then where is His saying, Exalted is He: 'Then he drew near and came down' (53:8-10)? She said: That is only Jibril, peace be upon him. He used to come to him in the form of men, and this time he came to him in his [true] form, and he filled the horizon of the sky.

And in the Two Sahihs also from Ash-Shaybani: I asked Zirr ibn Hubaysh about the saying of Allah 'Qaba qawsayni aw adna' (53:9). He said: Ibn Mas'ud informed me that the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw Jibril with six hundred wings. And from Ibn Mas'ud also: 'The heart did not lie about what it saw' (53:11). He said: He saw Jibril with six hundred wings. And from him also: 'Indeed he saw of the greatest signs of his Lord' (53:18). He said: He saw Jibril in his form with six hundred wings. And Al-Bukhari said in some of his chains: He saw a green covering that had filled the horizon. And from Abdullah: 'Indeed he saw of the greatest signs of his Lord' (53:18). He said: He saw a green covering.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the logicians' and philosophers' claim that angels are merely imaginary forms (sura khayaliyya) that impress upon the common sense (hiss mushtarak), or that they are abstract intellects and souls (uqul wa nufus). The author begins by asserting that it is mutawatir (massively transmitted) from the prophets that angels are living, speaking beings. He lists their functions: they bring revelation and commands from Allah, and they support and fight alongside the prophets. Moreover, angels sometimes appeared to people in human form, physically visible to those present. This directly contradicts the philosophical view that they are only mental images.

Then Ibn Taymiyya provides scriptural evidence. He quotes a long passage from Surah An-Najm (53:5-18) describing the Prophet Muhammad's seeing of a mighty being at the Sidrat al-Muntaha. This is followed by a hadith from Masruq, reporting that Aisha denied that the Prophet saw his Lord; rather, the one he saw was Jibril, and he only saw him in his true form on two occasions. The hadith emphasizes that Jibril's true form is enormous, filling the space between heaven and earth.

Further hadiths from Ibn Mas'ud confirm that the Prophet saw Jibril with six hundred wings, and that the 'greatest signs' referred to Jibril himself, not to Allah. Ibn Taymiyya uses these reports to establish that angels have a real, physical existence beyond mere imagination. The argument hinges on the authority of tawatur and the explicit texts of revelation, which the author considers the primary source of knowledge about the unseen.

It is important to note that this is a theological refutation aimed at the logical and philosophical claims of the Mantiqiyyin (followers of Greek logic). Ibn Taymiyya does not engage in formal syllogistic reasoning here; instead, he appeals to revelation and consensus of the prophetic reports as providing certainty (yaqin).

Key Terms
متواتر
صورة خيالية
العقول والنفوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary source of evidence Ibn Taymiyya uses to refute the logicians' view of angels?
A) Rational demonstration
B) Consensus of the companions
C) Mutawatir reports from the prophets
D) Analogical reasoning from human experience

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya bases his refutation on the epistemological certainty of tawatur, which he considers superior to philosophical speculation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a modern philosophical claim about angels (e.g., 'angels are metaphors for psychological forces'). Construct a refutation using the logic of Ibn Taymiyya: i.e., show that this claim contradicts mutawatir reports from the Qur'an and hadith.
?
In a debate with a philosopher who says angels are 'immaterial intelligences', apply Ibn Taymiyya's method: cite the hadith of Jibril with six hundred wings to argue for their physical reality.

The Evidence from the Prophet's Vision of Jibril
Ibn Taymiyya cites hadith on Jibril's appearance to prove angels' real existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite specific hadith and Quranic verses that Ibn Taymiyya uses to prove the physical reality of angels.

Core Idea
The Prophet saw Jibril in his true form with six hundred wings.

Ibn Taymiyya supports his refutation with detailed accounts from the Prophet's encounter with Jibril as recorded in the Sahihayn. These reports describe Jibril's enormous size and his appearance in human form, undermining the notion that he is merely an imaginal form. This lesson examines the hadith evidence and its role in Ibn Taymiyya's argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key hadith about Jibril's form
Read the hadith from Aisha and Ibn Mas'ud. What do they say about the number of wings and the size of Jibril?
2
Understand the interpretive dispute
Why did Aisha correct the interpretation that the Prophet saw his Lord? How does this support Ibn Taymiyya's case?
3
Connect the hadith to the refutation
How does the description of Jibril's physical form contradict the philosophers' claim of 'imaginary form'?
4
Assess the strength of this evidence
Why would mutawatir hadith be considered more reliable than philosophical reasoning?

الوجه العاشر: إنه من المتواتر عن الأنبياء - صلوات الله عليهم - أن الملائكة أحياء ناطقون يأتونهم عن الله بما يخبر به ويأمر به تارة، وينصرونهم ويقاتلون معهم تارة. وكانت الملائكة أحياناً تأتيهم في صورة البشر والحاضرون يرونهم. وقد أخبر الله عن الملائكة في كتابه بأخبار متنوعة. وذلك يناقض ما يزعمونه من أن الملك إنما هو الصورة الخيالية التي ترتسم في الحس المشترك، أو أنها العقول والنفوس.

عظم خلق جبریل

الأخبار المتواترة بمجيء الملائكة في صورة البشر

قال الله تعالى: (مَلَتَهُ شَدِيدُ القوى) (ذُو مِرَّةٍ فَاسْتَوَى) (وَهُوَ بِالْأُفُقِ الْأَعْلَى) (ثُمَّ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى) (فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى) (فَأَوْحَى إِلَى عَبْدِهِ مَا أَوْحَى) (مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى) (أَفَتُمَارُونَهُ عَلَى مَا يَرَى) (وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ نَزْلَةً أُخْرَى) (عِنْدَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنْتَهَى) (عِنْدَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى) (إِذْ يَغْشَى السِّدْرَةَ مَا يَغْشَى) (مَا زَاغَ الْبَصَرُ وَمَا طَغَى) (لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى) [سورة النجم: ١٨-٥].

وفي الصحيحين عن مسروق قال: كنت متكئاً عند عائشة رضي الله عنها، فقالت: يا أبا عائشة ثلاث من تكلم بواحدة منهن فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. قلت: ما هن؟ قالت: من زعم أن محمداً رأى ربه فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. ومن زعم أنه يعلم ما في غدٍ فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. ومن زعم أنه كتم شيئاً مما أوحي إليه فقد أعظم على الله الفرية. قال: وكنت متكئاً فجلست فقلت: يا أم المؤمنين أنظريني، ولا تعجليني. ألم يقل الله تعالى: (وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ بِالْأُفُقِ الْمُبِينِ) [سورة التكوير: ٢٣] (وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ نَزْلَةً أُخْرَى) [سورة النجم: ١٣]؟ فقالت: أنا أول هذه الأمة عن ذلك، رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: إنما هو جبريل، لم أره على صورته التي خلق عليها غير هاتين المرتين رأيته منهبطاً من السماء ساداً عظم خلقه ما بين السماء والأرض. وفي لفظ: فقلت فأين قوله عز وجل: (ثُمَّ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى) (فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى) (فَأَوْحَى إِلَى عَبْدِهِ مَا أَوْحَى) [سورة النجم: ٨-١٠]؟ قالت: إنما ذاك جبريل عليه السلام، كان يأتيه في صورة الرجال وإنه أتاه هذه المرة في صورته التي هي صورته، فسد أفق السماء.

وفي الصحيحين أيضاً عن الشيباني قال: سألت زر بن حبيش عن قول الله: (قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى) قال: أخبرني ابن مسعود أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى جبريل له ست مئة جناح. وعن ابن مسعود أيضاً قال: (مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى) قال: رأى جبريل له ست مئة جناح. وعنه أيضاً: (لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى) قال: رأى جبريل في صورته له ست مئة جناح. وقال البخاري في بعض طرقه: رأى رفرفاً أخضر قد سد الأفق. وعن عبد الله قال: (لَقَدْ رَأَى مِنْ آيَاتِ رَبِّهِ الْكُبْرَى) قال: رأى رفرفاً أخضر.
The tenth aspect: It is from the mutawatir (widely transmitted) reports from the prophets - blessings of Allah be upon them - that the angels are living, speaking beings, who come to them from Allah with what He informs and commands sometimes, and they support them and fight with them sometimes. And the angels would sometimes come to them in human form, and those present would see them. And Allah has informed about the angels in His Book with various reports. And that contradicts what they claim, that the angel is only the imaginary form that is impressed in the common sense, or that they are the intellects and souls.

The greatness of the creation of Jibril

The mutawatir reports of the coming of angels in human form

Allah the Exalted said: 'One of mighty power' (53:5-18) ... [Surah An-Najm 5-18].

And in the Two Sahihs from Masruq: I was reclining near Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, and she said: O Abu Aisha, three things - whoever speaks of one of them has fabricated a great lie against Allah. I said: What are they? She said: Whoever claims that Muhammad saw his Lord has fabricated a great lie against Allah. And whoever claims that he knows what is in tomorrow has fabricated a great lie against Allah. And whoever claims that he concealed something that was revealed to him has fabricated a great lie against Allah. He said: I was reclining so I sat up and said: O Mother of the Believers, give me respite and do not hasten me. Did not Allah say: 'And indeed he saw him in the clear horizon' (81:23) and 'And indeed he saw him another time' (53:13)? She said: I am the first of this community to ask the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about that, and he said: 'It is only Jibril. I did not see him in the form in which he was created except on these two occasions. I saw him descending from heaven, his enormous creation filling what is between heaven and earth.' And in another wording: I said: Then where is His saying, Exalted is He: 'Then he drew near and came down' (53:8-10)? She said: That is only Jibril, peace be upon him. He used to come to him in the form of men, and this time he came to him in his [true] form, and he filled the horizon of the sky.

And in the Two Sahihs also from Ash-Shaybani: I asked Zirr ibn Hubaysh about the saying of Allah 'Qaba qawsayni aw adna' (53:9). He said: Ibn Mas'ud informed me that the Prophet (peace be upon him) saw Jibril with six hundred wings. And from Ibn Mas'ud also: 'The heart did not lie about what it saw' (53:11). He said: He saw Jibril with six hundred wings. And from him also: 'Indeed he saw of the greatest signs of his Lord' (53:18). He said: He saw Jibril in his form with six hundred wings. And Al-Bukhari said in some of his chains: He saw a green covering that had filled the horizon. And from Abdullah: 'Indeed he saw of the greatest signs of his Lord' (53:18). He said: He saw a green covering.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the logicians' and philosophers' claim that angels are merely imaginary forms (sura khayaliyya) that impress upon the common sense (hiss mushtarak), or that they are abstract intellects and souls (uqul wa nufus). The author begins by asserting that it is mutawatir (massively transmitted) from the prophets that angels are living, speaking beings. He lists their functions: they bring revelation and commands from Allah, and they support and fight alongside the prophets. Moreover, angels sometimes appeared to people in human form, physically visible to those present. This directly contradicts the philosophical view that they are only mental images.

Then Ibn Taymiyya provides scriptural evidence. He quotes a long passage from Surah An-Najm (53:5-18) describing the Prophet Muhammad's seeing of a mighty being at the Sidrat al-Muntaha. This is followed by a hadith from Masruq, reporting that Aisha denied that the Prophet saw his Lord; rather, the one he saw was Jibril, and he only saw him in his true form on two occasions. The hadith emphasizes that Jibril's true form is enormous, filling the space between heaven and earth.

Further hadiths from Ibn Mas'ud confirm that the Prophet saw Jibril with six hundred wings, and that the 'greatest signs' referred to Jibril himself, not to Allah. Ibn Taymiyya uses these reports to establish that angels have a real, physical existence beyond mere imagination. The argument hinges on the authority of tawatur and the explicit texts of revelation, which the author considers the primary source of knowledge about the unseen.

It is important to note that this is a theological refutation aimed at the logical and philosophical claims of the Mantiqiyyin (followers of Greek logic). Ibn Taymiyya does not engage in formal syllogistic reasoning here; instead, he appeals to revelation and consensus of the prophetic reports as providing certainty (yaqin).

Key Terms
متواتر
صورة البشر
ستمائة جناح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many wings did Jibril have according to the hadith cited by Ibn Taymiyya?
A) Two
B) One hundred
C) Six hundred
D) One thousand

Key Takeaway
The hadith about Jibril's six hundred wings provides concrete evidence against the philosophers' reduction of angels to abstract intellects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look up the hadith of Jibril's six hundred wings in the Sahihayn. Explain how this hadith functions as a refutation of the philosophers' view that angels are only imaginary forms.

Ibn Taymiyya's Quranic Refutation of the Active Intellect
Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic verses to prove revelation comes from Jibril

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's Quranic argument against the Active Intellect and explain why the attributes in Surah Takwir refute the philosophers' position.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic descriptions of Jibril to show revelation comes from a personal angel, not an abstract intellect.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes on the philosophers who claim that prophets receive revelation from the Active Intellect. Rather than engaging with their philosophical system on its own terms, he turns to the Quran itself and asks: does the description of the messenger match the Active Intellect? The answer, he argues, is a clear no. By citing Surah Takwir, he demonstrates that the attributes of the messenger—power, station near the Throne, being obeyed, and trustworthiness—can only apply to a personal angelic being like Jibril, not an impersonal cosmic intellect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophical claim
The philosophers assert that revelation originates from the Active Intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al) or the imaginative faculty of the soul. Recognize this as the target of Ibn Taymiyya's critique.
Active Intellect is a key term in falsafa.
2
Locate the Quranic verses
Ibn Taymiyya cites Surah Takwir (81:19-25). Read these verses and note that they describe a 'noble messenger' (rasul karim) who brings the Quran.
The verses refer to Jibril according to mainstream tafsir.
3
Extract the key attributes
List the qualities: possessed of power (dhu quwwa), a secure station near the Owner of the Throne (makin), obeyed (muta'), and trustworthy (amin). These are concrete, personal attributes.
Muta' (obeyed) is especially emphasized by Ibn Taymiyya.
4
Compare to the Active Intellect
Ask: Can an abstract, impersonal entity like the Active Intellect be described as 'obeyed'? Being obeyed implies a commander with authority, a personal being. The Active Intellect is not a personal agent and cannot be obeyed in any literal sense.
This is the core logical move: the Quranic attributes are incompatible with the philosophical concept.
5
Conclude the refutation
Therefore, the messenger who brought the Quran is Jibril, not the Active Intellect. Ibn Taymiyya has used the Quran's own language to refute the philosophers' claim without relying on their technical terminology.
This demonstrates the priority of revelation (naql) over speculative reason ('aql) in matters of doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال سبحانه: ﴿ إِنَّهُ لَقَولُ رَسُولٍ كَرِيمٍ ذِى قُوَّةٍ عِندَ ذِي الْعَرْشِ مَكِينٍ مُطَاعٍ ثَمَّ أَمِينٍ وَمَا صَاحِبُكُم بِمَجْنُونٍ وَلَقَدْ رَوَاهُ بِالْأُفُقِ الْمُبِينِ وَمَا هُوَ عَلَى الْغَيْبِ بِضَنِينٍ وَمَا هُوَ بِقَولِ شَيْطَانٍ رَجِيمٍ ﴾ [سورة التكوير: 19-25] فبيّن أن الرسول الذي جاء به إلى محمد رسول كريم، ذو قوة عند ذي العرش مَكِينٌ مُطاعٌ ثَمَّ أمين. وهذه صفة لا تنطبق على ما في النفس من الخيال ولا على العقل الفعّال فإنه أخبر أنه مطاع، والمطاع فوق السموات ليس هذا ولا هذا.
And He, the Exalted, said: 'Indeed, it is the word of a noble messenger, possessed of power, with the Owner of the Throne, secure, obeyed there, and trustworthy. And your companion is not mad. And he certainly saw him in the clear horizon. And he is not withholden of the unseen. And it is not the word of an accursed devil.' So He made clear that the messenger who brought it to Muhammad is a noble messenger, possessed of power, with the Owner of the Throne, secure, obeyed there, trustworthy. And these attributes do not apply to what is in the soul of imagination nor to the active intellect; for He informed that he is obeyed, and the one obeyed above the heavens is not this nor that.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary where Ibn Taymiyya refutes the philosophers who claim that revelation originates from the Active Intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al) or from the imaginative faculty of the soul. He cites Surah Takwir (81:19-25), which describes the 'noble messenger' (rasul karim) who brings the Quran. The attributes listed—power, a high station near the Throne, being obeyed, and trustworthiness—are concrete and apply only to a created angelic being like Jibril, not to an abstract concept like the Active Intellect or a mental image. He emphasizes the word 'obeyed' (muta'), which implies a commander who is obeyed, a characteristic of a personal angel above the heavens, not an impersonal force. By this, Ibn Taymiyya argues that the source of revelation is a real, obedient angel (Jibril), not a metaphysical abstraction.

Key Terms
العقل الفعّال
رسول كريم
مطاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Active Intellect is also obeyed by the lower intellects.
B) Because the term 'obeyed' implies a personal agent with command, not an impersonal cosmic intellect.
C) Because the Active Intellect is imaginary and thus cannot be described.
D) Because the passage is about the Prophet Muhammad, not about revelation.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the Active Intellect doctrine by showing that the Quranic attributes of the revelation-bearing messenger are exclusively personal and incompatible with an impersonal force.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Critique of Logicians' Account of Revelation: Angel Not Active Intellect
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the logicians' identification of the angel with the active intellect or imagination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's specific Qur'anic argument against identifying the angel with the active intellect or imagination.

Core Idea
The angel Jibril is 'obeyed' above the heavens — no mental image or intellect can claim that.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya confronts the philosophers' attempt to reduce the angel of revelation to either the active intellect or a mental image. He anchors his refutation in the precise attributes of Jibril as described in Surah At-Takwir, especially the attribute 'obeyed' (muta'). Understanding how he uses this term to demolish the philosophical model is crucial for grasping his broader epistemological critique of Greek-inspired rationalism.

Guided Path
1
Locate the philosophical claim under attack
Identify what the logicians/philosophers say about the angel: that it is the active intellect or mental imagery.
2
Extract the key Qur'anic verse and its attributes
Read Surah At-Takwir 19-21 and list the attributes: noble messenger, powerful, high rank, obeyed, trustworthy.
Verse: ﴿إِنَّهُ لَقَولُ رَسُولٍ كَرِيم ذِى قُوَّةٍ عِندَ ذِي الْعَرْشِ مَكِينِ مُطَاعِ ثُمَّ أَمِين﴾
3
Focus on the attribute 'obeyed' (muta')
Consider why Ibn Taymiyya singles out this attribute. What does 'obeyed' imply about the angel's status and location?
It implies authority and being above the heavens.
4
Apply the attribute to the philosophers' candidates
Ask: Can the active intellect be 'obeyed'? Can a mental image be 'obeyed above the heavens'? Conclude why the identification fails.
Neither fits — the active intellect is an impersonal principle, and mental imagery is internal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كون جبريل وقد قال سبحانه: ﴿ إِنَّهُ لَقَولُ رَسُولٍ كَرِيم ذِى قُوَّةٍ عِندَ ذِي الْعَرْشِ مَكِينِ مُطَاعِ ثُمَّ أَمِين ﴾ [سورة التكوير : ١٩ - ٢١] فبيّن أن الرسول الذي جاء به إلى محمد رسول كريم، ذو قوة عند ذي العرش مَكِينٌ مُطَاعٌ ثَمَّ ، أمين. وهذه صفة لا تنطبق على ما في النفس من الخيال ولا على العقل الفعّال فإنه أخبر أنه مطاع، والمطاع فوق السموات ليس هذا ولا هذا.
Regarding Jibril, He (Allah) said: 'Indeed it is the speech of a noble messenger, possessed of power, with the Owner of the Throne, secure, obeyed, then trustworthy.' So He made clear that the messenger who brought it to Muhammad is a noble messenger, possessed of power, with the Owner of the Throne, secure, obeyed, then trustworthy. And these attributes do not apply to what is in the soul of imagination, nor to the active intellect, for He informed that he is 'obeyed', and the one obeyed above the heavens is neither this nor that.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument by Ibn Taymiyya against the logicians and philosophers who claim that the angel who brings revelation is either a mental image (al-khayal) or the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al). He cites Qur'anic verses from Surah At-Takwir describing the angel as a noble messenger, possessing power, high rank, being obeyed, and trustworthy. Ibn Taymiyya argues that these attributes—especially 'obeyed' (muta')—cannot be applied to a mental image or the active intellect, because the active intellect is not obeyed, nor is it above the heavens. The angel is a distinct, powerful being above the heavens. Thus, the logicians' reduction of revelation to psychological or intellectual processes is false.

Key Terms

الخيال
مطاع

D) The active intellect is not powerful.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic description of Jibril as 'obeyed above the heavens' cannot be reconciled with the philosopher's identification of the angel as an active intellect or mental image.
