Ibn Taymiyya's Use of Quranic Angel Reports Against Logicians
Ibn Taymiyya cites Quranic accounts of angels to support his critique of rationalist epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Ibn Taymiyya uses Quranic reports of angels as mutawatir evidence to challenge the logicians' epistemology and evaluate the strength of his argument.

Core Idea
Mutawatir reports of angels are as certain as rational proofs.

Ibn Taymiyya launches a powerful critique against the logicians who claim that only rational syllogisms yield certainty. He counters by presenting a series of Quranic reports about angels descending and interacting with humans. By showing that these reports are mutawatir (massively transmitted), he argues that they provide epistemic certainty equal to—or greater than—rational proofs. This passage is a key part of his broader refutation of Greek-influenced epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' target claim
The logicians assert that only demonstrative syllogisms (qiyas burhani) produce certain knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya attacks this by defending the epistemic value of transmitted reports (khabar).
2
List the Quranic examples provided
Ibn Taymiyya cites: the angel Gabriel appearing to Maryam, angels at Badr, Uhud, Khandaq, Hunayn, the Hijra, and the dialogue about Adam. These are multiple, independent reports.
3
Explain the concept of tawatur
Each report comes through multiple chains, making it mutawatir—knowledge that cannot be rationally doubted. Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes their collective certainty.
In usul al-fiqh, mutawatir reports are accepted as certain.
4
Analyze the epistemological challenge
If logicians reject these reports, they must explain why rational proofs trump sensory testimony. If they accept them, their exclusive reliance on syllogism collapses.
Ibn Taymiyya forces a dilemma: either accept mutawatir reports as valid knowledge or reject a core of Islamic revelation.
5
Evaluate the strength of the critique
The critique is strong because it grounds certainty in multiple independent testimonies, appealing to both Quranic authority and human epistemology. However, a logician might argue that miracles are not subject to ordinary rational standards.
Ibn Taymiyya anticipates this by noting that these reports are foundational to the religion itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : أخبار نزول الملائكة لنصر الأنبياء وتأييدهم تمثل الملك لمريم بشراً وأخبر الله تعالى أنه أرسل إلى مريم العذراء البتول ملكاً في صورة بشر. فقال تعالى : ( وَاذْكُرْ فِي الْكِتَابِ مَرْيَمَ إِذِ انْتَبَذَتْ مِنْ أَهْلِهَا مَكَانًا شَرْقِيًّا فَاتَّخَذَتْ مِنْ دُونِهِمْ حِجَابًا فَأَرْسَلْنَا إِلَيْهَا رُوحَنَا فَتَمَثَّلَ لَهَا بَشَرًا سَوِيًّا قَالَتْ إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِالرَّحْمَٰنِ مِنْكَ إِنْ كُنْتَ تَقِيًّا قَالَ إِنَّمَا أَنَا رَسُولُ رَبِّكِ لِأَهَبَ لَكِ غُلَامًا زَكِيًّا قَالَتْ أَنَّىٰ يَكُونُ لِي غُلَامٌ وَلَمْ يَمْسَسْنِي بَشَرٌ وَلَمْ أَكُ بَغِيًّا قَالَ كَذَٰلِكِ قَالَ رَبُّكِ هُوَ عَلَيَّ هَيِّنٌ وَلِنَجْعَلَهُ آيَةً لِلنَّاسِ وَرَحْمَةً مِنَّا وَكَانَ أَمْرًا مَقْضِيًّا فَحَمَلَتْهُ فَانْتَبَذَتْ بِهِ مَكَانًا قَصِيًّا فَأَجَاءَهَا الْمَخَاضُ إِلَىٰ جِذْعِ النَّخْلَةِ قَالَتْ يَا لَيْتَنِي مِتُّ قَبْلَ هَٰذَا وَكُنْتُ نَسْيًا مَنْسِيًّا فَنَادَاهَا مِنْ تَحْتِهَا أَلَّا تَحْزَنِي قَدْ جَعَلَ رَبُّكِ تَحْتَكِ سَرِيًّا وَهُزِّي إِلَيْكِ بِجِذْعِ النَّخْلَةِ تُسَاقِطْ عَلَيْكِ رُطَبًا جَنِيًّا فَكُلِي وَاشْرَبِي وَقَرِّي عَيْنًا فَإِمَّا تَرَيِنَّ مِنَ الْبَشَرِ أَحَدًا فَقُولِي إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ لِلرَّحْمَٰنِ صَوْمًا فَلَنْ أُكَلِّمَ الْيَوْمَ إِنْسِيًّا فَأَتَتْ بِهِ قَوْمَهَا تَحْمِلُهُ قَالُوا يَا مَرْيَمُ لَقَدْ جِئْتِ شَيْئًا فَرِيًّا يَا أُخْتَ هَارُونَ مَا كَانَ أَبُوكِ امْرَأَ سَوْءٍ وَمَا كَانَتْ أُمُّكِ بَغِيًّا فَأَشَارَتْ إِلَيْهِ قَالُوا كَيْفَ نُكَلِّمُ مَنْ كَانَ فِي الْمَهْدِ صَبِيًّا قَالَ إِنِّي عَبْدُ اللَّهِ آتَانِيَ الْكِتَابَ وَجَعَلَنِي نَبِيًّا وَجَعَلَنِي مُبَارَكًا أَيْنَ مَا كُنْتُ وَأَوْصَانِي بِالصَّلَاةِ وَالزَّكَاةِ مَا دُمْتُ حَيًّا وَبَرًّا بِوَالِدَتِي وَلَمْ يَجْعَلْنِي جَبَّارًا شَقِيًّا وَالسَّلَامُ عَلَيَّ يَوْمَ وُلِدْتُ وَيَوْمَ أَمُوتُ وَيَوْمَ أُبْعَثُ حَيًّا ذَٰلِكَ عِيسَى ابْنُ مَرْيَمَ قَوْلَ الْحَقِّ الَّذِي فِيهِ يَمْتَرُونَ مَا كَانَ لِلَّهِ أَنْ يَتَّخِذَ مِنْ وَلَدٍ سُبْحَانَهُ إِذَا قَضَىٰ أَمْرًا فَإِنَّمَا يَقُولُ لَهُ كُنْ فَيَكُونُ وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ رَبِّي وَرَبُّكُمْ فَاعْبُدُوهُ هَٰذَا صِرَاطٌ مُسْتَقِيمٌ ) [سورة مريم: 16-36]. وقد ذكر الله النفخ في فرجها من هذا الروح في موضعين آخرين من القرآن. فهذه الأخبار المتواترة من مجيء الملائكة في صورة البشر. أخبار نزول الملائكة لنصرة الأنبياء وتأييدهم وأما نزولهم لنصر الأنبياء وتأييدهم فقد ذكره الله في غير موضع من كتابه في قصة يوم بدر: ﴿ إِذْ تَسْتَغِيثُونَ رَبَّكُمْ فَاسْتَجَابَ لَكُمْ أَنِّي مُمِدُّكُمْ بِأَلْفٍ مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ مُرْدِفِينَ وَمَا جَعَلَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَّا بُشْرَىٰ وَلِتَطْمَئِنَّ بِهِ قُلُوبُكُمْ وَمَا النَّصْرُ إِلَّا مِنْ عِنْدِ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ ) إلى قوله: ﴿ إِذْ يُوحِي رَبُّكَ إِلَى الْمَلَائِكَةِ أَنِّي مَعَكُمْ فَثَبِّتُوا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ﴾ [سورة الأنفال: 9-12]. وقوله: ( وَلَوْ تَرَىٰ إِذْ يَتَوَفَّى الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا الْمَلَائِكَةُ يَضْرِبُونَ وُجُوهَهُمْ وَأَدْبَارَهُمْ وَذُوقُوا عَذَابَ الْحَرِيقِ ) [سورة الأنفال: 50]. وقوله تعالى في يوم أحد: ﴿ إِذْ تَقُولُ لِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَلَنْ يَكْفِيَكُمْ أَنْ يُمِدَّكُمْ رَبُّكُمْ بِثَلَاثَةِ آلَافٍ مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ مُنَزَّلِينَ بَلَىٰ إِنْ تَصْبِرُوا وَتَتَّقُوا وَيَأْتُوكُمْ مِنْ فَوْرِهِمْ هَٰذَا يُمْدِدْكُمْ رَبُّكُمْ بِخَمْسَةِ آلَافٍ مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ مُسَوِّمِينَ وَمَا جَعَلَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَّا بُشْرَىٰ لَكُمْ وَلِتَطْمَئِنَّ قُلُوبُكُمْ بِهِ وَمَا النَّصْرُ إِلَّا مِنْ عِنْدِ اللَّهِ ) [سورة آل عمران: 124-126]. (سقطت آية 125 في أصلنا، وقال «مسومين» بدل «منزلين».) وقال تعالى في يوم الخندق: ﴿ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اذْكُرُوا نِعْمَةَ اللَّهِ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذْ جَاءَتْكُمْ جُنُودٌ فَأَرْسَلْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ رِيحًا وَجُنُودًا لَمْ تَرَوْهَا وَكَانَ اللَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرًا ﴾ [سورة الأحزاب: 9]، وقال تعالى: ( وَيَوْمَ حُنَيْنٍ إِذْ أَعْجَبَتْكُمْ كَثْرَتُكُمْ فَلَمْ تُغْنِ عَنْكُمْ شَيْئًا وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْكُمُ الْأَرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ ثُمَّ وَلَّيْتُمْ مُدْبِرِينَ ثُمَّ أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ سَكِينَتَهُ عَلَىٰ رَسُولِهِ وَعَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَأَنْزَلَ جُنُودًا لَمْ تَرَوْهَا وَعَذَّبَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا وَذَٰلِكَ جَزَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ ثُمَّ يَتُوبُ اللَّهُ مِنْ بَعْدِ ذَٰلِكَ عَلَىٰ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ) [سورة التوبة: 25-27]. وقال عند خروجه للهجرة: ﴿ إِلَّا تَنْصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللَّهُ إِذْ أَخْرَجَهُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا ثَانِيَ اثْنَيْنِ إِذْ هُمَا فِي الْغَارِ إِذْ يَقُولُ لِصَاحِبِهِ لَا تَحْزَنْ إِنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَنَا فَأَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ سَكِينَتَهُ عَلَيْهِ وَأَيَّدَهُ بِجُنُودٍ لَمْ تَرَوْهَا وَجَعَلَ كَلِمَةَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا السُّفْلَىٰ وَكَلِمَةُ اللَّهِ هِيَ الْعُلْيَا وَاللَّهُ عَزِيزٌ حَكِيمٌ ) [سورة التوبة: 40]. أنواع أخر من أخبار الملائكة وقد أخبر سبحانه عن الملائكة بقوله: ﴿ إِنِّي جَاعِلٌ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةً قَالُوا أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَنْ يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ وَنَحْنُ نُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِكَ وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ قَالَ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ الْأَسْمَاءَ كُلَّهَا ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى الْمَلَائِكَةِ فَقَالَ أَنْبِئُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَٰؤُلَاءِ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ صَادِقِينَ قَالُوا سُبْحَانَكَ لَا عِلْمَ لَنَا إِلَّا مَا عَلَّمْتَنَا إِنَّكَ أَنْتَ الْعَلِيمُ الْحَكِيمُ قَالَ يَا آدَمُ أَنْبِئْهُمْ بِأَسْمَائِهِمْ ﴾ [سورة البقرة: 30-33].
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: Reports of the descent of angels to support and strengthen the prophets. The angel taking the form of a human for Mary. And Allah Almighty informed that He sent to Mary the virgin, the chaste, an angel in the form of a human. So He said: 'And mention in the Book Mary when she withdrew from her family to an eastern place and took a screen apart from them; then We sent to her Our Spirit, and he appeared to her as a well-proportioned man. She said, "I seek refuge in the Most Merciful from you, if you should be fearing Allah." He said, "I am only the messenger of your Lord to give you a pure boy." She said, "How can I have a boy while no man has touched me and I have not been unchaste?" He said, "Thus your Lord has said: It is easy for Me, and that We may make him a sign to the people and a mercy from Us, and it is a matter decreed." So she conceived him and withdrew with him to a remote place. And the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of a palm tree. She said, "Oh, I wish I had died before this and was a thing forgotten." Then he called her from beneath her: "Do not grieve; your Lord has provided beneath you a stream. And shake toward yourself the trunk of the palm tree; it will drop upon you fresh, ripe dates. So eat and drink and be contented. And if you see from among humanity anyone, say, 'Indeed, I have vowed to the Most Merciful abstention, so I will not speak today to any human.'" Then she brought him to her people, carrying him. They said, "O Mary, you have done a thing unprecedented. O sister of Aaron, your father was not a man of evil, nor was your mother unchaste." So she pointed to him. They said, "How can we speak to one who is in the cradle, a child?" He said, "Indeed, I am the servant of Allah. He has given me the Scripture and made me a prophet. And He has made me blessed wherever I am and has enjoined upon me prayer and zakah as long as I remain alive, and [to be] dutiful to my mother, and He has not made me a wretched tyrant. And peace is on me the day I was born and the day I die and the day I am raised alive." That is Jesus, son of Mary, the word of truth about which they are in doubt. It is not for Allah to take a son; exalted is He! When He decrees a matter, He only says to it, "Be," and it is. Indeed, Allah is my Lord and your Lord, so worship Him. This is a straight path.' [Surah Maryam: 16-36]. And Allah mentioned the blowing into her womb from this spirit in two other places in the Quran. These are the mutawatir reports of the coming of angels in human form. Reports of the descent of angels to support and strengthen the prophets. As for their descent to support and strengthen the prophets, Allah mentioned it in more than one place in His Book in the story of the day of Badr: 'When you were asking help of your Lord, and He answered you, "Indeed, I will reinforce you with a thousand from the angels, following one another." And Allah made it not but good tidings and that your hearts might be assured thereby. And victory is not except from Allah. Indeed, Allah is Exalted in Might and Wise.' Up to His saying: 'When your Lord inspired to the angels, "I am with you, so make firm those who have believed."' [Surah al-Anfal: 9-12]. And His saying: 'And if you could see when the angels take the souls of those who disbelieve, striking their faces and their backs and [saying], "Taste the punishment of the Burning Fire."' [Surah al-Anfal: 50]. And His saying concerning the day of Uhud: 'When you said to the believers, "Is it not sufficient for you that your Lord should reinforce you with three thousand angels sent down? Yes, if you remain patient and conscious of Allah and they come upon you in haste, your Lord will reinforce you with five thousand angels having marks [of identity]." And Allah made it not but good tidings for you and that your hearts might be assured thereby. And victory is not except from Allah.' [Surah Al Imran: 124-126]. (Verse 125 was missing in our source, and it said 'musawwimeen' instead of 'munazzaleen'.) And He said concerning the day of the Trench: 'O you who have believed, remember the favor of Allah upon you when armies came to you and We sent upon them a wind and armies you did not see. And ever is Allah, of what you do, Seeing.' [Surah al-Ahzab: 9]. And He said: 'And on the day of Hunayn, when your great number pleased you, but it did not avail you at all, and the earth was confining for you with its vastness; then you turned back, fleeing. Then Allah sent down His tranquility upon His Messenger and upon the believers and sent down soldiers you did not see and punished those who disbelieved. And that is the recompense of the disbelievers. Then Allah will accept repentance after that for whom He wills.' [Surah al-Tawbah: 25-27]. And He said at his emigration: 'If you do not support him, Allah has already supported him when those who disbelieved drove him out as the second of two, when they were in the cave, when he said to his companion, "Do not grieve; indeed Allah is with us." And Allah sent down His tranquility upon him and supported him with soldiers you did not see and made the word of those who disbelieved the lowest, while the word of Allah is the highest. And Allah is Exalted in Might and Wise.' [Surah al-Tawbah: 40]. Other types of reports about the angels. And He, glorified, informed about the angels in His saying: 'Indeed, I will make upon the earth a successive authority.' They said, 'Will You place upon it one who causes corruption therein and sheds blood, while we exalt You with praise and declare Your perfection?' He said, 'Indeed, I know that which you do not know.' And He taught Adam the names – all of them. Then He presented them to the angels and said, 'Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful.' They said, 'Exalted are You; we have no knowledge except what You have taught us. Indeed, it is You who is the Knowing, the Wise.' He said, 'O Adam, inform them of their names.' [Surah al-Baqarah: 30-33].
Source pages p. 539

Commentary
This passage is part of Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of the logicians. He presents a series of Quranic reports (akhbar) that describe angels descending and interacting with humans. His aim is to demonstrate that such reports, being mutawatir (massively transmitted), constitute a valid source of knowledge that cannot be dismissed by rational arguments. He begins with the story of Maryam, where the angel Gabriel appears in the form of a man. This shows that angels can take human form, challenging any claim that such reports are impossible. Then he cites the battles of Badr, Uhud, Khandaq, Hunayn, and the Hijra, where angels were sent to support the believers. Finally, he mentions the dialogue between Allah and the angels about the creation of Adam. By listing these examples, Ibn Taymiyya builds a cumulative argument: the consistent and widespread testimony of the Quran proves the reality of angelic intervention. This is a direct attack on the logicians' insistence on purely rational or syllogistic proofs, as he upholds the epistemic value of transmitted reports (khabar).

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT cited by Ibn Taymiyya in this passage as an example of angelic intervention?
A) The battle of Badr
B) The birth of Jesus
C) The battle of Tabuk
D) The day of Hunayn

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses mutawatir Quranic reports of angels to argue that transmitted knowledge can be as certain as rational proofs, challenging the logicians' exclusive reliance on syllogisms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify another example of a mutawatir report from Islamic history (e.g., the number of rak'ahs in prayer) and explain how it meets the criteria of tawatur. Then, argue how a logician might challenge it and how Ibn Taymiyya's approach would counter that challenge.
?
Using the passage, construct a brief jadal (dialectical) exchange: one person takes the position that only syllogisms yield certainty; the other responds using Ibn Taymiyya's angel reports as evidence. Ensure the response follows the rules of munazara by citing a specific Quranic example.

8 min
Ibn Taymiyya's Scriptural Refutation of the Philosophers' Deification of Intellects
Ibn Taymiyya refutes philosophers' deification of intellects using Quranic descriptions of angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' claim that the first intellect is a lord, and identify the scriptural basis he uses.

Core Idea
Angels are servants, not lords: Ibn Taymiyya uses Quran to dismantle the philosophical hierarchy.

Ibn Taymiyya does not engage with the philosophers' logical proofs directly; instead, he confronts their doctrine with the Quranic portrayal of angels as humble servants. In this passage, he systematically cites verses describing angels' obedience, intercession only by permission, and their roles as mere creatures. By contrasting this with the philosophers' elevation of intellects to lordship, Ibn Taymiyya exposes a fundamental theological error.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim
The philosophers assert that the first intellect (al-'aql al-awwal) is the lord of all worlds, and the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al) is the lord of the sublunar realm. Locate the sentence where Ibn Taymiyya states this.
2
List the Quranic verses and angelic characteristics
Ibn Taymiyya quotes verses describing angels: they are not too proud to worship, they obey commands, they intercede only by permission, etc. Extract at least three characteristics from these verses.
3
Compare with philosophical attributes
Note the contrast: angels are servants; philosophers claim intellects are lords. What does Ibn Taymiyya imply by asking 'Where is this description from the saying of these philosophers?'
4
Identify the type of evidence used
Ibn Taymiyya relies entirely on revealed texts (Quran and Hadith) rather than rational arguments. This is a key feature of his critique: he measures philosophical claims against scriptural truth.
5
Evaluate the critique's effectiveness
Consider whether the philosophers would accept scriptural authority. Ibn Taymiyya's method assumes the primacy of revelation over reason in matters of divinity.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر كونهم لا يستكبرون عن عبادة الله عباداً مطيعين اسْمَاهِمْ فَلَمَّا أَنْبَأَهُم بِأَسْمَاتِهِمْ قَالَ أَلَمْ أَقُل لَكُمْ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ غَيْبَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَأَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا كُنتُمْ تَكْتُمُونَ ﴾ [سورة البقرة : ٣٠ - ٣٣]. وأخبر عنهم سبحانه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَقَالُوا اتَّخَذَ الرَّحْمَنُ وَلَدًا سُبْحَنَه بَلْ عِباد وصفهم بكونهم تُكْرَمُونَ لَا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بِالْقَوْلِ وَهُم بِأَمْرِهِ، يَعْمَلُونَ يَعْلَمُ مَا بَيْنَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَمَا خَلْفَهُمْ ا ولا يشفعونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَى وَهُم مِّنْ خَشْيَتِهِ مُشْفِقُونَ وَمَن يَقُل مِنْهُمْ إِنّى إِلَهُ مِن دُونِهِ. * فَذَلِكَ نَجْزِيهِ جَهَنَّمُ﴾ [سورة الأنبياء : ۲٦ - ۲۹] . فأين هذا النعت من قول هؤلاء المتفلسفة الذين يدعون أن العقل الأول ربُّ جميع العالمين - العُلوي والسفلي وكذلك كل عقل حتى ينتهي إلى «الفعّال»، فيزعمون أنه ربّ لما تحت فلك القمر؟ وقد قال سبحانه : وَكَم مِّن مَّلَكٍ فِي السَّمَوَاتِ لَا تُغْنِي شَفَعَتُهُمْ شَيْئًا إِلَّا مِنْ بَعْدِ أَن يَأْذَنَ اللهُ لِمَن يَشَاءُ وَيَرْضَى [سورة النجم : ٢٦] . وقال تعالى: ﴿فَإِنِ اسْتَكْبَرُوا فَالَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ يُسَبِّحُونَ لَهُ بِاليْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَهُمْ لَا يَسْتَمُونَ ) [سورة فصلت : ۳۸] وقال تعالى : وَلَهُ مَن فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَنْ عِندَهُ لَا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، وَلَا يَسْتَحْسِرُونَ يُسَبِّحُونَ الَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ لَا يَفْتُرُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأنبياء : ۱۹ - ۲۰] وقال: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ لَا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ، وَيُسَبِّحُونَهُ وَلَهُمْ يَسْجُدُونَ [سورة الأعراف : ٢٠٦]. وفي الصحيحين عن النبي أنه قال: «ألا تَصُفّون كما تصف الملائكة عند ربها؟ قالوا: وكيف تَصُفُّ الملائكة عند ربها ؟ قال : «يسدُّون الأوّل، فالأول، ويَتَراصُون في الصف». وهذا موافق لقوله تعالى : ( وَالصَّفَاتِ صَفًّا فَالرَّجِرَاتِ زَجْرًا ) فَالتَلِيتِ ذِكْرًا ﴾ [سورة الصافات : ١ - ٣] . ولقوله عنهم : ﴿ وَمَا مِنَّا إِلَّا لَهُ مَقَامٌ مَّعْلُومُ الله وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الصَّافُونَ وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الْمُسَبِّحُونَ ﴾ [سورة الصافات: ١٦٤ - ١٦٦] . وقال تعالى : ( الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ، وَيَسْتَغْفِرُونَ لِلَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا رَبَّنَا وَسِعْتَ كُلَّ شَيْ ءٍ رَحْمَةً وَعِلْمًا فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ وَفِهِمْ عَذَابَ الجميم ) [سورة غافر : ٧] . وقال تعالى : ( قُوا أَنفُسَكُمْ وَأَهْلِيكُمْ نَارًا وَقُودُهَا النَّاسُ وَالْحِجَارَةُ عَلَيْهَا مَلَيْكَةٌ غِلَاظٌ شِدَادٌ لا يَعْصُونَ اللَّهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ ﴾ [سورة التحريم : ٦]. وقال تعالى في صفة أهل النار : ﴿ سَأُصْلِيهِ سَفَرَ وَمَا أَدْرَيكَ مَا سَقَرُ لَا تُبقِي وَلَا نَذَرُ لَوَاحَةٌ لِلْبَشَرِ عَلَيْهَا تِسْعَةَ عشر ( وَمَا جَعَلْنَا أَصْحَبُ النَّارِ إِلَّا مَلَيْكَةً وَمَا جَعَلْنَا عِدَّتَهُمْ إِلَّا فِتْنَةً لِلَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا لِيَسْتَيْقِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَبَ وَمَزْدَادَ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِيمَنَا وَلَا بَرْتَابَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ وَالْمُؤْمِنُونَ وَلِيَقُولَ الَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوهِم مَّرَضٌ وَالْكَفَفِرُونَ مَاذَا أَرَادَ اللَّهُ بِهَذَا مثلاً كَذَلِكَ يُضِلُّ اللَّهُ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِى مَن يَشَاء وَمَا يَعْلَمُ جُنُودَ رَبِّكَ إِلَّا هُوَ وَمَا هِيَ إِلَّا ذِكْرَى لِلْبَشَرِ ﴾ [سورة المدثر : ٢٦ - ٣١]. وقال تعالى: ﴿ فَيَدْعُ نَادِيَهُ لا سَنَدْعُ الزَّبَانية ﴾ [سورة العلق : ۱۷ - ۱۸] . قال غير واحد من الصحابة والتابعين كأبي هريرة وعبد الله بن الحارث، وعطاء : هم الملائكة وقال قتادة : الزبانية في كلام العرب، الشرط. وقال مقاتل: هم خزنة جهنم. قال أهل اللغة كابن قتيبة وغيره : هو مأخوذ من «الزَّبْن» وهو الدفع، كأنهم يدفعون أهل النار إليها قال ابن دُرَيْد : الزَّبن ، الدفع، يقال «ناقة زبون» إذا زَبَنَتْ حالتها ودفعته برجلها ؛ و تزابن) القومُ تدارَأوا ؛ واشتقاق «الزبانية» من الزبن . وأيضاً في الصحاح من غير وجه عن النبي أنه أخبر ليلة المعراج بما رآه من الملائكة والجنة والنار، وأخبر عن البيت المعمور أنه يدخله كل يوم سبعون ألف ملك لا يعودون آخر ما عليهم
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: That they (angels) are not too proud to worship Allah, obedient servants. ... Then where is this description from the saying of these philosophers who claim that the first intellect is the lord of all worlds - the upper and the lower - and likewise every intellect until ending with the 'active intellect', and they claim that it is the lord of what is under the sphere of the moon? ... And in the two Sahihs from the Prophet that he said: 'Do you not form rows as the angels form rows before their Lord?' They said: 'How do the angels form rows before their Lord?' He said: 'They complete the first rows, then the next, and they stand close together in the row.' ... And also in the Sahih from the Prophet that he informed on the night of the Mi'raj of what he saw of angels, Paradise, and Hell, and he informed about the al-Bayt al-Ma'mur that seventy thousand angels enter it every day, never to return to it again.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the philosophers' doctrine that the first intellect (al-'aql al-awwal) and subsequent intellects, including the active intellect (al-'aql al-fa''al), are lords of the worlds. Ibn Taymiyya opens by citing several Quranic verses that describe the angels as obedient servants who do not precede Allah in speech and who act by His command. He then directly contrasts this with the philosophers' claim, asking rhetorically: 'Where is this description from the saying of these philosophers who claim that the first intellect is the lord of all worlds?' He emphasizes that the philosophers even claim that the active intellect is lord of the sublunar realm, attributing lordship to created beings. The author then continues to quote verses about angels not being too proud to worship Allah, about their row formation in prayer, and about their duties as described in the Quran. Finally, he cites the description of the angels of hell (zabaniya) and the hadith about the angels entering the al-Bayt al-Ma'mur. Throughout, Ibn Taymiyya uses scriptural evidence to establish that angels are created servants, not deities or lords, thereby refuting the philosophical hierarchy of intellects. The passage exemplifies his method of critiquing Greek-derived philosophy by appealing to the Quran and hadith as the primary sources of knowledge.

Key Terms
الملائكة
العقل الأول
الفعّال
الزبانية

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in this passage, what is the main error of the philosophers regarding the first intellect?
A) They deny the existence of angels altogether.
B) They claim the first intellect is a lord and creator, while angels are described in the Quran as servants.
C) They say the first intellect is from the jinn.
D) They believe the first intellect is the Prophet Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique demonstrates that scriptural descriptions of creation can serve as a powerful refutation of philosophical doctrines that elevate created beings to divine status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Subjectivist View of Prophethood
Ibn Taymiyya refutes philosophers' claim that prophets only experienced imaginative visions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's tawatur-based refutation of the philosophical claim that prophetic experiences are merely subjective.

Core Idea
Prophetic reports are corroborated by mass transmission, not subjective fantasies.

Ibn Taymiyya confronts the philosophical claim that prophetic experiences are merely internal imaginings. He does not simply reject it; he provides a rational argument based on the principle of tawatur, showing that the prophets' reports are independently verified across time and place. This lesson unpacks his critique and its epistemological foundation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Find the precise philosophical statement about prophets that Ibn Taymiyya is attacking: 'What they saw is only what they imagined in themselves, and what they heard is only what they heard in their souls.'
This reduces prophecy to subjective hallucination.
2
Distinguish two interpretations
Ibn Taymiyya considers whether the philosophers mean the prophets intentionally reported subjective experiences, or whether they are simply denying the objective reality of prophetic visions. He shows that both are false.
The first is a lie about the prophets' intent; the second is outright denial.
3
Examine the tawatur argument
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the prophets, though separated in time and place, gave concordant reports. Their agreement, combined with their known truthfulness and intellect, creates certain knowledge through mass transmission.
This argument does not require meeting: even without contact, the reports corroborate.
4
Analyze the analogy
He gives examples: many reports of black people establish their existence; epileptics' reports of seeing jinn are accepted. Similarly, prophetic reports about angels and the unseen are confirmed by tawatur.
This shows that tawatur yields necessary knowledge even for unseen matters.
5
Evaluate the critique's force
The critique does not rest on mere authority; it uses a rational principle (tawatur) to establish certainty. The philosophers' skepticism is thus shown to be contrary to necessary knowledge.
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that rejecting prophetic reports leads to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : بيان كذبهم على الأنبياء ، وأن النبوة ليست كما يدعونه . وما في القرآن والأحاديث وكلام السلف من ذكر الملائكة وأحوالهم يفوق الإحصاء. وكذلك عند أهل التوراة والإنجيل ونبوات سائر الأنبياء . وما أخبر به الأنبياء يناقض قول من قال عن الأنبياء: «إن الذي رأوه من إنما هو ما يخيل في أنفسهم، وأن الذي سمعوه إنما هو ما سمعوه في نفوسهم». فإن كان مقصوده أنهم أرادوا بما أخبروا به هذا، فهذا كذب صريح عليهم لا حيلة فيه . وإن كان مكذِّباً لهم، يقول إنهم لم يروا شيئاً» أو «إنهم غلطوا فيما أخبروا به من ذلك»، فهذا ليس مَقامَ من يفسّر كلامهم ويبين مرادهم، كما يزعمه هؤلاء المتفلسفة الذين يتكلمون على النبوة بما يدعون أنه تفسير لها. والمقصود هنا بيان كذبهم على الأنبياء، وأن النبوة ليست كما يدعونه . وأما الكذب للأنبياء فلخطابه مقام آخر، مع أن هذا من أجهل أهل الأرض إيطال القول وأكفرهم. وذلك أن الأنبياء عدد كثيرون وهم بإجماع العقلاء في غاية صفات الكمال من العقل، والعلم والعدل، والصدق والأخلاق الحسنة وكل منهم لم ير الآخر ولم يستمع منه، لا سيما محمد ، فإنه لم يكن بمكة على عهده أحد يعرف شيئاً من كتب الأنبياء ألبتة. وكل منهم يخبر عما رأى وسمع أخباراً يصدقُ بعضها بعضاً. فلو لم تثبت عصمة الأنبياء وصدقهم، بل كان المخبر بمثل هذا مجهولاً، لوجب تواتر جنس ما رأوه . كما أن العدد الكثير إذا أخبر كلُّ منهم أنه رأى أسود تواتر وجودُ السُّودان عند من لم يرهم. ولهذا لما أخبر كثير من المصروعين عن وجود الصرع ثبت بهذا وجوده في الجملة، ولم يكن تكذيب المصروعين فيما يخبرون به مما يُعاينونه، بل عامة العقلاء يعلم أنهم رأوا الجنَّ الأحياء الناطقين. وهذا معلوم عند جمهور العقلاء علماً ضرورياً لا يمكنهم النزاع فيه .
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: An exposition of their lying against the prophets, and that prophethood is not as they claim. What is in the Quran, hadiths, and speech of the Salaf regarding the mention of angels and their states is beyond enumeration. Similarly with the people of the Torah, the Gospel, and the prophecies of the rest of the prophets. What the prophets have informed contradicts the saying of those who said about the prophets: 'What they saw is only what they imagined in themselves, and what they heard is only what they heard in their souls.' If his intention is that the prophets meant by their reports this, then this is a clear lie against them with no trick in it. And if he is denying them, saying they did not see anything or they erred in what they reported of that, then this is not the position of one interpreting their speech and clarifying their intent, as these philosophers claim who speak about prophethood with what they pretend is an interpretation of it. The purpose here is to expose their lying against the prophets, and that prophethood is not as they claim. As for the lying to the prophets, it has another place of discussion, though this person is among the most ignorant of the people of the earth in voiding speech and most disbelieving. That is because the prophets are numerous and they are, by consensus of the rational people, at the utmost degree of perfection in intellect, knowledge, justice, truthfulness, and good character. None of them saw the other nor heard from him, especially Muhammad, for there was no one in Mecca at his time who knew anything from the books of the prophets at all. And each of them informs about what he saw and heard, reports that verify each other. So if the infallibility and truthfulness of the prophets were not established, even if the reporter of such was unknown, the genus of what they saw would necessarily be transmitted by tawatur (mass transmission). Just as when a large number of people each reports that he saw black people, the existence of blacks is transmitted by tawatur to those who have not seen them. For this reason, when many epileptics reported about the existence of epilepsy, its existence in general was thereby established, and the epileptics were not denied in what they reported of what they witnessed; rather, the generality of rational people know that they saw living, speaking jinn. And this is known to the majority of rational people as necessary knowledge, in which they cannot dispute.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the philosophers' claim that prophetic experiences are merely subjective imaginings or sounds heard within themselves. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating the station: exposing the philosophers' lie against the prophets and showing that prophethood is not as they claim. He points out that the abundance of reports about angels in the Quran, hadith, and words of the Salaf is beyond enumeration, and similarly in previous scriptures. Then he presents the philosophers' statement: 'What they saw is only what they imagined in themselves...' He argues that if the philosophers mean that the prophets intended their reports to refer to these subjective experiences, that is a clear lie. If, instead, they are denying the prophets altogether or claiming they erred, that is not interpretation but outright denial. Ibn Taymiyya then provides a rational argument: the prophets, numerous and of perfect intellect, truthfulness, etc., each independently reported what they saw and heard, and their reports corroborate each other, even though they did not meet or learn from one another (especially Muhammad, who had no access to previous scriptures). This mutual corroboration, he argues, establishes the truth of their reports through tawatur (mass transmission). He gives the analogy of multiple people reporting the existence of black people or epileptics reporting seeing jinn; such reports are generally accepted as true. Thus, the philosophers' skepticism is baseless and contradicts necessary knowledge.

Key Terms
النبوة
تواتر
متفلسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what proves the truth of the prophets' reports about the unseen despite their lack of contact with each other?
A) Each prophet performed miracles
B) The reports are transmitted by tawatur and mutually corroborate
C) The philosophers confirmed them
D) They were all kings

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the subjectivist view of prophethood by demonstrating that prophetic reports meet the epistemological standard of tawatur, yielding certain knowledge that cannot be dismissed as mere imagination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Use the tawatur principle to evaluate the following claim: 'The Prophet Muhammad split the moon.' Identify whether the transmission of this report meets the conditions of tawatur or is merely ahad, and explain how this affects its epistemological status.
?
Construct a brief argument similar to Ibn Taymiyya's: Show that the reports of the Prophet's miracles (e.g., water flowing from his fingers) are corroborated by multiple independent witnesses, and thus cannot be dismissed as subjective imagination.

Ibn Taymiyya's Linguistic Refutation of Philosophers' Prophecy
Ibn Taymiyya explains the linguistic meaning of 'malak' and concludes that philosophers' views contradict revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the philosophers' conception of prophecy contradicts the revealed meaning of 'malak' and that their logical epistemology excludes prophetic knowledge.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya uses the etymology of 'malak' to demolish the philosophers' claim that prophecy comes from syllogism.

Ibn Taymiyya begins with a linguistic point: the word 'malak' (angel) is derived from the root meaning 'messenger'. This is not mere philology; it establishes that angels are essentially messengers, and prophethood involves revelation from God. He then contrasts this with the philosophers' theory that prophets gain knowledge through logical syllogism or celestial souls. By showing that this contradicts the clear meaning of scripture and basic Islamic beliefs, Ibn Taymiyya invalidates the philosophers' entire epistemology as inadequate for true knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic claim
Ibn Taymiyya states that 'malak' means 'messenger', derived from the root meaning 'message' (risala). The original form is 'ma'lak' and the hamza shifts. Understand that this is a standard Arabic etymology.
The root is 'alif-lam-kaf' meaning 'message'.
2
Connect to revelation
Since angels are messengers, revelation comes through them. This is obvious from the Qur'an and Sunnah. Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes that this is known by necessity in the religion.
3
Contrast with philosophers' view
The philosophers claim that prophets gain knowledge either by logical syllogism (qiyas mantiqi) or by the connection of their soul to the celestial soul. This contradicts the simple meaning of 'malak' and revelation.
Ibn Taymiyya calls this 'among the most invalid of speech'.
4
Analyze the critique of epistemology
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' confinement of knowledge to 'matter and form' (i.e., syllogistic form and empirical matter) excludes the greatest truth: prophetic knowledge. Thus their logic is corrupt.
This is the core of his refutation of Aristotelian epistemology.
5
Assess the broader implication
The philosophers' system cannot account for divine revelation. Therefore, any claim that prophesy is based on their logic is false. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that their logical framework is incomplete.
This serves his overall goal: to show that Greek logic is not the sole path to knowledge.

و «الملك معناه الرسول، وأصله «مَلأَك» على وزن مَفْعَل ولكن ألقيت الهمزة على الساكن قبلها وحُذفت. وهذه المادة معناها «الرسالة» سواء تقدمت اللام على الهمزة كما في صيغة الملك»، أو تقدمت الهمزة على اللام. وهذه الأمور لبسطها موضع آخر . وإنما المقصود أن نعرف أن ما يفسرون به الملائكة والوحي مما يُعلم بالاضطرار من دين الرسول أنه مُناقض لما جاء به. فعلم أن ما يثبتونه من النبوة لا حقيقة له ؛ وأن ادعاءهم أن علم الأنبياء إنما يحصل بالقياس المنطقي وإما باتصال نفسه بالنفس الفلكية من أبطل الكلام. وذلك مما يبين فساد ما ذكروه في المنطق من حَصْرِ طرق العلم مادة وصورة، وهو المطلوب في هذا الموضع ؛ ويبين أنهم أخرجوا من العلوم الصادقة أجلَّ حقيقة له . (وزاد في تفسير المعوذتين: و «ملاك» مأخوذ من المألك» و «الملاك» بتقديم الهمزة على اللام واللام على الهمزة، وهو «الرسالة». وكذلك الألوكة) بتقديم الهمزة على اللام . قال الشاعر : أبلغ النعمان عن مـالكـــــاً عنــــــي أنه قد طال حبسي وانتظاري . وهذا بتقديم الهمزة. لكن الملك هو بتقديم اللام على الهمزة، وهذا أجود ، إلخ.)
And 'al-malak' (the angel) means 'the messenger'; its origin is 'ma'lak' on the pattern of 'maf'al', but the hamza was thrown onto the preceding silent letter and deleted. This root carries the meaning of 'message', whether the lam precedes the hamza as in the form 'al-malak', or the hamza precedes the lam. These matters have another place for their elaboration. Rather, the purpose is to know that what they interpret regarding angels and revelation is known by necessity from the religion of the Messenger to be contradictory to what he brought. Thus it is known that what they affirm of prophethood has no reality; and that their claim that the knowledge of the prophets is obtained either by logical syllogism or by the connection of their soul to the celestial soul is among the most invalid of speech. And that shows the corruption of what they mentioned in logic regarding confining the paths of knowledge in matter and form, and that is what is sought in this place; and it shows that they have excluded from the truthful sciences the most magnificent truth. (And in Tafsir al-Mu'awwidhatayn: 'And 'mala'k' is derived from 'al-ma'lak' and 'al-malak' with the hamza preceding the lam and the lam preceding the hamza, meaning 'the message'. Similarly 'al-uluka' with the hamza preceding the lam. The poet said: Inform al-Nu'man from Malik that my imprisonment and waiting have become long. And this is with the hamza preceding. But 'al-malak' is with the lam preceding the hamza, and this is more excellent, etc.)
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic and theological refutation. Ibn Taymiyya first explains the etymology of 'malak' (angel): it derives from the root meaning 'message' or 'messenger', confirming that angels are messengers of God. He then states that the philosophers' interpretation of angels and revelation is contrary to what is known by necessity from the Prophet's religion. Therefore, their concept of prophethood is baseless. Specifically, their claim that prophetic knowledge comes via logical syllogism or connection to the celestial soul is invalid. This in turn shows the corruption of their logical framework that confines the paths of knowledge to form and matter (i.e., their Aristotelian epistemology). Ibn Taymiyya argues that they have excluded the greatest truth (i.e., prophetic knowledge) from the sciences. The passage ends his overall argument: the philosophers' logic fails because it cannot account for genuine prophetic knowledge, which is the goal of this section.

Key Terms
الملك (al-malak): Angel; etymologically means 'messenger'. Ibn Taymiyya emphasizes the linguistic connection to 'risala' (message) to counter philosophical reinterpretations. [Note: Linguistic derivation is standard; Ibn Taymiyya uses it to support his theological argument.]
القياس المنطقي (al-qiyās al-manṭiqī): Logical syllogism; the philosophers' claimed method for prophets to gain knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya rejects this. [Note: Ibn Taymiyya critiques the Aristotelian syllogism as insufficient for all knowledge.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The rules of logic

D) The scientific method

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' epistemology, which limits knowledge to syllogism and celestial emanation, cannot account for the highest form of knowledge: prophecy, which is known by necessity from revelation.

Classifying Motion: Natural, Coerced, and Voluntary
Classification of motion types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given motion as natural, coerced, or voluntary according to Ibn Taymiyya’s criteria.

Core Idea
All motion reduces to voluntary motion: only will-powered movement is original.

Ibn Taymiyya opens his proof for angels by dividing motion into three types based on the source of the moving power. Understanding this classification is essential to following his logical argument that all motion traces back to voluntary agents. Let's unpack the three categories and their defining features.

Guided Path
1
Identify the threefold classification
Find in the Arabic the list of three motion types: طبيعية (natural), قسرية (coerced), and إرادية (voluntary). Note that the author derives them from the principle that motion comes from a power either inside or outside the moving body.
The term قسرية may appear as قشرية in OCR; correct it mentally.
2
Define each type of motion
For natural motion (حركة طبيعية): occurs when a body seeks its natural place after being displaced, e.g., dust falling to earth. For coerced motion (حركة قسرية): imposed by an external force, e.g., a stone thrown. For voluntary motion (حركة إرادية): caused by a living being with will and perception.
Notice that both natural and coerced depend on an external initiator; voluntary is the only self-starting type.
3
Examine the relation between types
Ibn Taymiyya states that coerced motion depends on a coercer (قاسِر), and natural motion only occurs when a body is moved from its place. This implies that neither occurs without an initial voluntary mover.
This sets up the next step in the proof: all motion requires a voluntary origin.
4
Apply the classification to a new example
Test your understanding: classify the motion of a bird flying (voluntary), a rock falling (natural), a boat pushed by wind (coerced). Check if your classification matches Ibn Taymiyya’s definitions.
Be careful: the bird's flight is voluntary because it has will, even if affected by air resistance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً، فالأدلة العقلية تدل على أن الملائكة بهم يدبر الله أمر السماء والأرض، كما قد بسط الكلام على هذا في غير موضعه. وبين فيه أن الحركات ثلاثة : طبيعية، وقسرية، وإرادية. لأن المتحرك إنما يتحرك بقوة فيه أو خارجة عنه؛ والثاني هو حركة إرادية المقسور المتحرك قسراً، والأول إن لم يكن له شعور فهي الحركة الطبيعية، وإن كان له شعور فهي الإرادية والقسرية تابعة للقاسِر ، فلولا هو لم يتحرك المقسور . والطبيعية إنما يكون إذا خرج الجسم الطبيعي عن محله فيطلب بطبعه العود إلى محله؛ فإذا عاد سكن، كالتراب إذا سقط على الأرض والماء إذا وصل إلى مقره، ونحو ذلك . فلم يبق هنا متحرّك ابتداءً إلا المتحرك بالحركة الإرادية. فعلم أن جميع الحركات مبدأها حركة إرادية . ومعلوم أن الآدميين لا يحركون الهواء والسحاب وغير ذلك من الأجسام. فالمحرك لها أحياء يحركون لها بالإرادة، وهؤلاء هم الملائكة .
And also, rational proofs indicate that the angels, through them, God manages the affairs of the heavens and the earth, as the discourse on this has been expanded elsewhere. And he explained therein that motions are three: natural, coerced, and voluntary. Because the moving thing only moves by a power within it or outside it; the second is voluntary motion, the coerced moving thing moves by force, and the first if it has no perception then it is natural motion, and if it has perception then it is voluntary. And the coerced is dependent on the coercer, for were it not for him the coerced would not move. And the natural only occurs when a natural body leaves its place, then by its nature it seeks to return to its place; so when it returns it becomes still, like dust when it falls to the ground and water when it reaches its resting place, and similar to that. So here there remains no moving thing initially except the mover by voluntary motion. So it is known that all motions have their origin in voluntary motion. And it is known that human beings do not move the air and clouds and other such bodies. So the mover of them are living beings that move them voluntarily, and these are the angels.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the existence of angels based on the classification of motion. The author (Ibn Taymiyya) states that rational proofs indicate that God manages the affairs of the heavens and the earth through angels. He then explains that motion is of three types: natural, coerced, and voluntary. The classification is based on the source of the moving power: either within the moving thing or external. Coerced motion depends on an external coercer, while natural motion occurs when a body seeks its natural place. The key point is that all motion ultimately traces back to voluntary motion, because the only original mover is that which moves voluntarily. Since humans do not cause large-scale motions like those of air and clouds, the agents must be other voluntary movers, i.e., angels. This argument is reminiscent of the Aristotelian unmoved mover but adapted to an Islamic framework.

Key Terms
حركة طبيعية
حركة قسرية
حركة إرادية

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Coerced motion involves will, natural motion does not.
C) Natural motion is always upward, coerced motion is always downward.
D) Coerced motion is permanent, natural motion is temporary.

Key Takeaway
All motion is either natural, coerced, or voluntary; only voluntary motion is self-starting, making it the ultimate source of all movement.

Tracing All Motion Back to Voluntary Agents: A Compound Syllogism
Compound syllogistic proof for angels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's compound argument for the existence of angels as voluntary movers, identifying each syllogistic step.

Core Idea
A chain of reasoning from motion types to the necessity of voluntary agents like angels.

Ibn Taymiyya uses the classification of motion to build a multi-step proof. He shows that all motion originates from voluntary motion, then argues that humans cannot be the movers of cosmic bodies, concluding that angels must be the agents. Let's break down this compound syllogism step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first syllogism: motion types and their origins
Locate the premise that all motion is either natural, coerced, or voluntary. Then note the sub-premise: natural and coerced motions depend on a prior mover (coercer or displacer). Conclude: only voluntary motion is an original mover. This is a disjunctive syllogism eliminating natural and coerced as original.
Ibn Taymiyya states: 'So here there remains no moving thing initially except the mover by voluntary motion.'
2
Extract the second syllogism: from voluntary motion to angels
The second step: All original motions are voluntary. Cosmic motions (air, clouds, etc.) are not caused by humans. Therefore, they must be caused by other voluntary beings. He concludes these are angels.
The unstated premise: every voluntary motion requires a living being with will.
3
Formalize as a compound syllogism
Combine the two syllogisms. Syllogism 1 (categorical): Original motion is only voluntary. All natural/coerced motion is not original. So original motion is voluntary. Syllogism 2 (categorical): All voluntary motion requires a voluntary agent. Cosmic motions are voluntary. So cosmic motions require a voluntary agent. And that agent is not human, so it must be angels.
This is a sorites: a chain of categorical syllogisms.
4
Evaluate the logical validity
Check each step. The first part is valid if the classification is exhaustive. The second requires that cosmic motions are indeed voluntary. Ibn Taymiyya assumes this because they cannot be natural (they involve direction changes) nor coerced (no external physical cause visible). The argument is strong within his framework.
We are not judging the truth of premises, only logical flow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Ibn Taymiyya's Disjunctive Refutation of Celestial Causes
Ibn Taymiyya disproves celestial causation of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's disjunctive argument against celestial causation of prophetic knowledge and identify the empirical refutation he provides.

Core Idea
Prophetic knowledge requires a personal cause, not a uniform celestial motion.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya targets the philosophical claim that prophetic knowledge arises from celestial souls or intellects. He constructs a two-pronged argument: first, a logical disjunction showing that angelic causation is at least possible; second, an empirical argument that celestial motions cannot account for the diversity of human inspirations. Understanding this argument equips you to critically evaluate causal theories in Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that knowledge in prophets' hearts comes from angels, not celestial causes. His goal is to disprove the philosophers' theory.
2
Extract the disjunctive premise
He poses a dichotomy: either prophetic knowledge has a cause or it does not. If it has no cause, the philosophers' claim that it comes from intellect/soul is false.
3
Examine the consequence for the cause branch
If it has a cause, it could be angels or jinn. The philosophers have no proof to deny angelic causation, given their own theories (emanation or mover).
4
Follow to the conclusion
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that since the celestial soul theory is invalid, the cause must be angels. This is the sought conclusion.
5
Analyze the empirical refutation
He adds an empirical argument: celestial motions are uniform for all on a given day, yet human inspirations vary greatly. Therefore, celestial motions cannot be the cause of diverse inspirations.
This strengthens the conclusion that angels are the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : كون حصول العلم في قلوب الأنبياء من الملائكة. ومما يبين ذلك أن يقال : ما يحصل في قلوب الأنبياء وغيرهم من العلم بأمور معينة إما أن يكون له سبب يقتضي حصول ذلك العلم، أو يحصل بلا سبب كما يقول من أهل الكلام من ينكر الأسباب في الوجود فإن لم يكن له سبب بطل قولهم : إن ذلك من العقل والنفس. وإن كان له سبب أمكن أن يكون ذلك هو ملائكة تعلّمهم بذلك، أو جن تعلّم بعض الناس. وهم ليس لهم حجة أصلاً على نفي ذلك بتقدير ما يقولونه من قدم الأفلاك وصدورها عن علة مستلزمة لها كما يقوله ابن سينا، أو أن العلة تحرّكها تحريك القدوة للمقتدى به على قول أرسطو وأتباعه. فعلى قول أرسطو وأتباعه وعلى كل قول ليس في العقل حجة تنفي ذلك. وإذا أمكن كون ذلك من بطل قولهم . بل نقول : يجب أن يكون ذلك من الملائكة إذا كان له سبب . فإن كون ذلك من النفس الفلكية قد ظهر بطلانه ، فوجب أن يكون ذلك من الملائكة . وهو المطلوب. وقد أثبت طائفة من نظار المسلمين والفلاسفة وجود الملائكة والجن بهذه الطريق. وقالوا نحن نجد أموراً تحدث في نفوسنا بغير قصد منا من العلوم والإرادات، وما هو من جنس العلوم والإرادات من الخواطر - خواطر الشبهات والشهوات . فلا بد بهذه الطريق من فاعل يحدثها في قلوبنا والله سبحانه وتعالى هو خالق كل شيء، لكن لم يخلق شيئاً إلا لسبب كما دل على ذلك استقراء خلقه للموجودات، ولا يحدث حادثاً إلا بسبب حادث والإنسان يكون قلبه خالياً من اعتقاد الضدين ومن إرادة الضدين، فيحدث أحدهما في قلبه، فلا بد لذلك من سبب حادث أوجب ذلك. ولا يجوز إضافة ذلك إلى مجرد الحركات الفلكية فإن نسبة الحركة الفلكية في اليوم المعين إلى الأشخاص نسبة واحدة والناس مختلفون في هذه الخواطر اختلافاً لا مزيد عليه. والشخص الواحد يختلف حاله فتارة يكون مؤمناً وتارة يكون كافراً، وتارة برا وتارة فاجراً، وتارة عالماً وتارة جاهلاً وتارة ناسياً وتارة ذاكراً، بدون حدوث سبب فلكي يرجح أحد هذين الحالين على الآخر. وأهل الأرض الواحدة، والبلد الواحد، والإقليم الواحد، تختلف أحوالهم في ذلك مع أن طالع البلد لم يختلف، ومع أن المتجدد من الأشكال الفلكية قد يكون متشابه الأحوال وأحوالهم مع هذا تختلف. وهذا لبسطه موضع آخر. فإن ظن هؤلاء أن الحوادث التي تحت الفلك ليس سببها إلا تغير أشكال الفلك واتصالات الكواكب من أفسد الأقوال ولهذا كان أصحاب هذا القول من أكثر الناس جهلاً، وكذباً، وتناقضاً، وحيرة.
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: The occurrence of knowledge in the hearts of prophets from angels. And what clarifies that is to say: What occurs in the hearts of prophets and others of knowledge of specific matters either has a cause necessitating the occurrence of that knowledge, or occurs without a cause, as those among the theologians who deny causes in existence say. For if it has no cause, their statement that it is from the intellect and the soul becomes invalid. And if it has a cause, it is possible that it is angels teaching them that, or jinn teaching some people. And they have absolutely no proof to deny that, given what they say about the pre-eternity of the spheres and their emanation from a cause that necessarily entails them as Ibn Sina says, or that the cause moves them with the movement of the exemplar to the one imitating as Aristotle and his followers say. So according to Aristotle and his followers and according to every statement, there is no rational proof to deny that. And if it is possible that it is from [angels], their statement is invalid. Rather we say: It must be from angels if it has a cause. For the fact that it is from the celestial soul has been shown to be false, so it must be from angels. That is what is sought. And a group of Muslim theologians and philosophers have affirmed the existence of angels and jinn by this method. They said: We find matters occurring in our souls without our intention, of knowledges and volitions, and that which is of the same kind as knowledges and volitions from inspirations - inspirations of doubts and desires. So by this method there must be an agent that produces them in our hearts. And Allah, exalted, is the Creator of everything, but He did not create anything except for a cause, as is indicated by induction of His creation of existents, and He does not bring about an event except through an event. And a person's heart is empty of belief in both opposites and of willing both opposites, then one of them occurs in his heart, so there must be an event that necessitates that. And it is not permissible to attribute that to mere celestial motions, for the proportion of the celestial motion on a given day to individuals is one and the same, while people differ in these inspirations to the utmost degree. And the same person's state differs: sometimes he is a believer, sometimes a disbeliever, sometimes pious, sometimes immoral, sometimes knowledgeable, sometimes ignorant, sometimes forgetful, sometimes mindful, without the occurrence of a celestial cause that preponderates one of these two states over the other. And the people of one land, one city, one region differ in their states with respect to that, while the ascendant of the land has not changed, and while the renewed celestial configurations may be similar in states, yet their states differ despite this. This is elaborated elsewhere. For the assumption of these people that the events under the sphere have no cause except the change of celestial configurations and planetary conjunctions is among the most corrupt statements, and therefore the adherents of this statement are among the most ignorant, lying, contradictory, and perplexed of people.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument by Ibn Taymiyya against the philosophers' claim that prophetic knowledge comes from celestial causes. He begins by stating the thesis: knowledge in prophets' hearts comes from angels. He then presents a disjunctive argument: either such knowledge has a cause or it does not. If it has no cause, then the philosophers' claim that it comes from intellect and soul is false. If it has a cause, it could be angels or jinn. The philosophers have no proof to deny angelic cause, given their own theories (Ibn Sina's emanation or Aristotle's mover). So Ibn Taymiyya concludes that it must be angels, since the celestial soul theory is invalid. Then he mentions an additional proof by Muslim theologians and philosophers: we find thoughts and inspirations arising in ourselves without our intention, which must have an agent; that agent cannot be merely celestial motions because celestial motions are uniform while human states vary greatly. Therefore, the cause must be angels (or jinn). He strongly criticizes astrological causation as among the most corrupt statements.

Key Terms
ملائكة
نفس فلكية
سبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya's argument, why can prophetic knowledge not be caused by celestial motions?
A) Because celestial motions are eternal and cannot produce temporal events.
B) Because celestial motions are uniform while human states vary greatly, so they cannot explain the diversity of inspirations.
C) Because prophets reject any form of causation.
D) Because angels have no connection to the celestial sphere.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses a combination of logical disjunction and empirical observation to argue that prophetic knowledge must come from personal spiritual agents (angels) rather than impersonal celestial motions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument in your own words, using a disjunctive syllogism format (either A or B; if A then not C; if B then D; therefore D). Then write a brief evaluation of its strength.

Find a contemporary claim that attributes human behavior to astrological influences. Apply Ibn Taymiyya's empirical refutation by showing the diversity of human responses under identical celestial conditions.

Refuting Astrological Causation with the Kaaba's Inviolability
Ibn Taymiyya points out the astrologers' inability to explain the Kaaba's veneration through celestial causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Ibn Taymiyya uses a historical counterexample to refute astrological determinism.

Core Idea
The Kaaba's inviolability refutes astrologers' claim that celestial configurations govern events.

Ibn Taymiyya often refutes false doctrines by pointing to empirical evidence from Islamic history. In this passage, he takes on the astrologers' claim that the Kaaba's honor must be due to a favorable astrological ascendant (tali'). He observes that astrologers are 'confused' (حاروا) because they cannot explain through their own system why Mecca has been perpetually honored and protected. This is a classic use of a counterexample to undermine a causal claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Astrologers claim that the Kaaba's veneration is due to a favorable ascendant (tali') at its construction. This is a causal claim linking celestial configurations to historical outcomes.
Ibn Taymiyya phrases it as 'according to their claim' (على زعمتهم).
2
Find the empirical counterexample
Ibn Taymiyya points to the Kaaba's historical protection from enemies (e.g., the Year of the Elephant) and the fact that even the tyrant al-Hajjaj did not harm it. This is a case where no known ascendant explains the outcome.
The Companions of the Elephant (أصحاب الفيل) refer to the Abyssinian attack in 570 CE.
3
Analyze the refutation strategy
Ibn Taymiyya uses a direct counterexample: if astrologers cannot find any special ascendant for the Kaaba, their universal claim that celestial causes determine honor is false. The Kaaba's status comes from divine will.
This is a form of reductio ad absurdum from an empirical perspective.
4
Evaluate the strength of the refutation
The refutation is logically valid because it presents a specific case that contradicts the universal claim. It does not require a full alternative theory, only the demonstration of inconsistency.
Ibn Taymiyya does not need to prove that celestial causation is impossible in all cases; one clear counterexample suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا حاروا في مكة - شرفها الله - وأي شيء هو الطالع الذي بنيت عليه على زعمتهم حتى رزقت هذه السعادة العظيمة وهذا البناء العظيم مع طول الأزمان مع أنه بسوء إلا انتقم الله منه كما فعل بأصحاب الفيل، ولم يعل عليها عدو لم يقصدها أحد قط. لم يكن الحجاج بن يوسف عدوًا لها، ولا أراد هدمها ولا أذاها بوجه من الوجوه.
And therefore they are confused about Mecca - may Allah honor it - and what ascendant it was built upon according to their claim, that it was granted this great happiness and this great structure over long periods, while any evil intended against it, Allah took revenge upon it as He did with the Companions of the Elephant. And no enemy ever overcame it; no one ever intended it harm. Al-Hajjaj ibn Yusuf was not an enemy to it, nor did he intend to demolish it or harm it in any way.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
Ibn Taymiyya uses the example of Mecca and the Kaaba to refute astrologers' claim that celestial configurations determine events. Astrologers cannot explain how Mecca, built without any special ascendant, has been honored throughout history, protected from enemies, and even the tyrant al-Hajjaj did not dare harm it. This shows the invalidity of astrological causation.

Key Terms
طالع
كعبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To prove that the Kaaba has a special astrological ascendant.
B) To show that astrologers cannot explain the Kaaba's honor through celestial causes, thereby refuting their theory.
C) To argue that all celestial causation is impossible in any form.
D) To praise al-Hajjaj for protecting the Kaaba.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses the Kaaba's inviolability as an empirical counterexample to refute astrologers' claim that celestial configurations determine events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify another historical event from Islamic history that could serve as a counterexample to a false causal claim (e.g., the preservation of the Quran despite attempts to distort it). Explain why it disproves the claim that human effort alone preserves texts.

Refutation of Astrologers' Claims About the Ka'ba
Ibn Taymiyya refutes astrologers' false claims about a cave and talismans under the Ka'ba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's method of refuting unsubstantiated magical claims by combining empirical falsification with theological explanation.

Core Idea
Perplexity leads to false explanations; Ibn Taymiyya's refutation restores rational and theological clarity.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya confronts astrologers who, baffled by the universal veneration of the Ka'ba despite Mecca's lack of natural attractions, invented magical explanations involving talismans and fumigation. He dismantles these claims by showing their factual falsehood, then provides a sound theological alternative grounded in the Qur'an. This lesson will walk you through his critical methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phenomenon that perplexed the astrologers
Notice the contrast: people from all over endure great hardships to visit the Ka'ba, yet Mecca has no gardens or rivers. This perplexed the astrologers.
This sets up the irrationality of their explanation.
2
Extract the false claims
The astrologers claimed a cave with talismans under the Ka'ba, and fumigation in Rajab to turn people's faces toward it. List these claims.
These are the targets of refutation.
3
Analyze Ibn Taymiyya's factual refutation
He states that no one has ever descended below the Ka'ba, and there is no cave. Also, Muslims do not use fumigation as worship—it is like perfume. Polytheists use it as worship.
Empirical and practice-based evidence.
4
Recognize the alternative theological explanation
Ibn Taymiyya cites the Qur'an (5:97): Allah made the Ka'ba a support for people. The true cause is Allah's will and power, not magic.
Replaces false cause with sound theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصار هؤلاء الفلكيون حائرين في أمرها لما جعل الله لها من العز والمهابة والتعظيم مع المحبة، ومع كون الناس من مشارق الأرض ومغاربها يأتونها بمحبة ورغبة وذُلّ مع المشاق العظيمة التي تزيد على مشقة عامة الأسفار من الجوع والعطش والخوف والتعب، وأنه ليس بمكة بساتين ولا أنهار ولا غير ذلك مما تطلبه النفوس. حتى ألجأ بعضهم الحيرة إلى أن زعم أن تحتها مغارة فيها طلاسم موجهة إلى الجهات جميع، وأنها تبخر في شهر رجب أو غيره لتصرف وجوه الناس إليها، ونحو هذه الأقوال المكذوبة التي يعلم كل من له علم بمكة أنها كذب مختلق وأنه لا ينزل أحد قط إلى أسفل الكعبة، ولا مغارة تحتها. ونفس التبخير لا يفعله المسلمون عبادة وقربانا، كما كان يفعل ذلك من قبلهم، بل هو عندهم من جنس الطيب فتقصد رائحته. ومن كان قبل المسلمين من أهل الكتاب كانوا يقربون القرابين فتنزل النار تأكله، وقد يدخنون بدخن. وأما المشركون من عباد الكواكب والأصنام فالتدخين عندهم من أصول العبادات. بل وجود مكة مما يدل على القادر المختار وأنه يخلق بمشيئته وقدرته وعلمه، جعل الكعبة قياما للناس كما قال تعالى: ﴿جَعَلَ اللهُ الْكَعْبَةَ الْبَيْتَ الْحَرَامَ قِيَامًا لِلنَّاسِ﴾ [سورة المائدة: 97].
So these astrologers became perplexed about its affair because Allah has given it honor, awe, and veneration along with love, and because people from the east of the earth and its west come to it with love and desire and humility amidst great hardships that exceed the hardship of ordinary travels—hunger, thirst, fear, and fatigue—and that there are no gardens in Mecca nor rivers nor anything else that souls desire. Until their perplexity drove some of them to claim that there is a cave beneath it containing talismans directed to all directions, and that it is fumigated in Rajab or other months to turn people's faces towards it, and similar false statements which everyone who has knowledge of Mecca knows are fabricated lies, and that no one ever descends to the bottom of the Ka'ba, nor is there a cave beneath it. As for fumigation itself, Muslims do not do it as worship and offering, as those before them used to do; rather, it is for them of the kind of perfume, so its scent is sought. And those before the Muslims among the People of the Book used to offer sacrifices, and fire would descend and consume them, and they would smoke with incense. As for the polytheists who worship celestial bodies and idols, fumigation is among the fundamentals of their worship. Rather, the existence of Mecca itself indicates the powerful, free-choosing Creator, and that He creates by His will, power, and knowledge; He made the Ka'ba a support for people, as He said: 'Allah has made the Ka'ba, the Sacred House, a support for people' [Surah al-Ma'idah: 97].
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of astrologers (al-falakiyyun) who, bewildered by the unique veneration of the Ka'ba, invented baseless explanations. Ibn Taymiyya first describes the Ka'ba's unmatched honor: people from all over the world endure extreme hardships to visit it, although Mecca lacks gardens, rivers, or other worldly attractions. This perplexed the astrologers, leading some to claim that beneath the Ka'ba lies a cave with talismans directed to the four directions, and that the Ka'ba is fumigated in Rajab to attract people. Ibn Taymiyya dismisses these as lies known to anyone familiar with Mecca—no one has ever descended below the Ka'ba, and there is no cave. He then addresses fumigation: Muslims do not use it as worship; they only use pleasant scents as perfume. The People of the Book offered sacrifices consumed by heavenly fire, and they used incense in worship. Polytheists (worshippers of planets and idols) consider fumigation a foundation of their rites. Finally, Ibn Taymiyya offers the true cause: Mecca itself points to the Creator who, by His will and power, made the Ka'ba a support for humanity, citing Qur'an 5:97. The refutation follows a pattern: describe the false claim, show its factual impossibility, then replace it with a sound theological explanation.

فلكيون
طلاسم
تبخير

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because fumigation is only done in Rajab.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refutes astrologers' magical claims by first proving their factual impossibility, then providing a sound theological explanation from the Qur'an.

Refuting the Philosophers: Proof of Angels and Jinn from Internal Experiences
Author proves angels and jinn from internal mental events

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that mental events indicate the existence of unseen beings, and identify how he refutes the philosophers' naturalistic causation.

Core Idea
Mental experiences cannot be explained purely by celestial motion; they reveal the activity of angels and jinn.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya challenges the Aristotelian view that all sublunar events are caused by the movement of the celestial spheres. He argues that the internal phenomena of inspiration and whisperings are evidence for the existence of angels and jinn. This lesson dissects his argument and its critique of purely naturalistic causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim
The philosophers attribute all events in the sublunar world to the movement of the celestial sphere (harakat al-falak). Ibn Taymiyya rejects this as insufficient.
This is the target of his critique.
2
Locate Ibn Taymiyya's premise
He states that what occurs in souls (al-nufus) is not caused solely by celestial motion. This is his key empirical observation.
He implies that there must be another cause.
3
Extract the conclusion
From the negation of celestial causation, he concludes that the existence of angels and jinn is indicated (dalla dhalika 'ala wujud al-mala'ika wa al-jinn).
The argument is a conditional: if not purely celestial, then unseen agents exist.
4
Examine the textual support
Ibn Taymiyya supports his conclusion with Ibn Mas'ud's statement about lamma (inspirations from angel and devil) and the hadith about qarin (companion from angels and jinn).
This links the empirical observation to revealed knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمقصود هنا أنه إذا عُلم ما يحدث في النفوس ليس سببه مجرد حركة الفلك دلّ ذلك على وجود الملائكة والجن. وهذا قول سلف الأمة والتابعين لهم بإحسان وأئمة المسلمين فإنهم يقولون : إن الشياطين توسوس في نفوس بني آدم كالعقائد الفاسدة والأمر باتباع الهوى، وإن الملائكة بالعكس إنما تقذف في القلوب الصدق والعدل . قال ابن مسعود: إن للملك لَمَّةٌ وللشيطان لَمَّةٌ، فلمة الملك إيعاد بالخير وتصديق بالحق، ولمة الشيطان إيعاد بالشر وتكذيب بالحق. وفي الصحيح عن النبي أنه قال: «ما منكم من أحد إلا وقد وُكِّلَ به قرينه من الملائكة ومن الجن». قالوا: «وإياك ، يا رسول الله؟ قال: «وإياي ، إلا أن الله أعانني عليه فأسْلَمُ - وفي لفظ «فلا يأمُرُني إلا بخير ).
The intended point here is that if it is known that what occurs in souls is not caused merely by the movement of the celestial sphere, then that indicates the existence of angels and jinn. This is the statement of the predecessors of the ummah, the followers, and the imams of the Muslims, for they say: Indeed, the devils whisper into the souls of the children of Adam, like corrupt beliefs and commanding to follow whims, and the angels, on the contrary, cast into the hearts truth and justice. Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Indeed, the angel has an inspiration (lamma) and the devil has an inspiration. The inspiration of the angel is a promise of good and affirmation of truth, and the inspiration of the devil is a promise of evil and denial of truth.' And in the authentic [hadith] from the Prophet (s) that he said: 'There is none of you but has been appointed a companion from the angels and from the jinn.' They said: 'Even you, O Messenger of God?' He said: 'Even me, except that God helped me against him so he submitted' - and in another wording: 'he does not command me except to good.'
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is an argument demonstrating the existence of angels and jinn based on internal human experiences. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that if we recognise that the events occurring in our souls are not solely caused by the movement of the celestial sphere (a reference to the Aristotelian theory of causation), then this points to the existence of angels and jinn. He attributes this view to the Salaf and the imams of the Muslims. He then quotes Ibn Mas'ud to illustrate the distinction between the inspirations of angels and devils. The hadith from the Prophet confirms that every person has a companion from both angels and jinn, with the exception of the Prophet, whose devil companion submitted to God. This argumentation rejects the purely naturalistic explanation of mental phenomena and establishes the role of unseen agents.

حركة الفلك
وسوسة
لَمَّة
قرين
