Angels and Devils as Sources of Knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya on angelic and satanic causation of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Salaf position on the causation of knowledge with three alternative theories and explain the roles of angelic inspiration (tasdid) and satanic whispers (ilqāʾ al-shayṭān) in correct and erroneous judgments.

Core Idea
Correct knowledge is a divine gift via angels; error stems from Satan, but the sincere mujtahid is excused.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya addresses a fundamental epistemological question: what is the true source of the knowledge that arises in the heart after reflection and reasoning? He surveys three prominent views—philosophical emanation, Mu'tazili generation, and Ash'ari direct creation—and then presents the Salaf position that God uses angels as intermediaries to grant correct knowledge, while Satan casts errors. This lesson walks you through his comparative analysis and its implications for the reliability of human reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rival theories
Read the opening lines where Ibn Taymiyya lists the philosophers (emanation from Active Intellect), Mu'tazila (generation/tawallud), and Ash'ari (direct act of God without cause). Note how each denies secondary causation.
These theories are not just academic; they affect how one understands the role of effort and divine grace in attaining truth.
2
Extract the Salaf position
Ibn Taymiyya states that the Salaf and Imams affirm that God has established causes and wisdoms for events, and that knowledge, strength, and support occur through angelic agency. Identify the key term 'tasdid' (divine guidance via an angel).
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
He cites Quranic verses (al-Anfal 12, al-Mujadila 22) and a hadith about sending an angel to guide aright. How does each support the idea that angels are intermediaries for correct knowledge?
Also note the examples of non-prophetic inspiration (mother of Moses, disciples) as ilhām through an angel.
4
Understand the satanic origin of error
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that mistakes in opinion come from satanic casting (ilqāʾ al-shayṭān). Yet a mujtahid who errs is excused. Look at the report from Abu Bakr and Ibn Mas'ud acknowledging that error is from Satan.
This shows that even sincere effort does not guarantee freedom from satanic influence, but the person is not sinful if involuntary.
5
Recognise the boundary of accountability
He adds that what comes from Satan that a person cannot repel (like dreams or nocturnal emissions) is not sinful; the pen is lifted. This refines the doctrine of personal responsibility in epistemology.
This nuance prevents despair: not every wrong thought is culpable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : حصول التثبيت والتأييد بواسطة الملائكة. وقد تنازع الناس في العلم الحاصل في القلب عقيب النظر والاستدلال على أقوال. فهؤلاء المتفلسفة يقولون : إن ذلك من فيض العقل الفعّال عند استعداد النفس . والمعتزلة يقولون : هو حاصل على سبيل التولّد والأشعري وغيره يقولون : هو حاصل بفعل الله تعالى كما تحصل سائر الحوادث عندهم - لا يجعلون لشيء من الحوادث سبباً ولا حكمة . والذي عليه السلف والأئمة أن الله جعل للحوادث أسباباً وحكماً، وهذه الحوادث حصول قد تحدث بأسباب من الملائكة أو من الجن وأن ما يحصل في القلب من العلم والقوة والتأييد ونحو ذلك قد يجعله الله بواسطة فعل الملائكة كما قال تعالى: ﴿ إِذْ يُوحى رَبُّكَ إِلَى الْمَلَكَةِ إِنِّي مَعَكُمْ فَتَبِتُوا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا ﴾ [سورة الأنفال: ۱۲]. وقال تعالى: (لَا تَجِدُ قَوْمًا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ يُوَادُّونَ مَنْ حَادَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَلَوْ كَانُوا مَابَاءَهُمْ أَوْ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ أَوْ إِخْوَانَهُمْ أَوْ عَشِيرَتَهُمْ أُولَيْكَ كَتَبَ فِي قُلُوبِهِمُ الإِيمَنَ وَأَيَّدَهُم بِرُوحِ مِنْةٌ ﴾ [سورة المجادلة : ۲۲] . وكما قال النبي : من سأل القضاء واستعان عليه وكل إليه، ومن لم يسأل القضاء ولم يستعن عليه أنزل الله إليه ملكاً يُسدّده» (۱). والتسديد هو إلقاه القول السَّدَاد في قلبه. وقال تعالى : ( وَأَوْحَيْنَا إِلَى أُمِّ مُوسَى أَنْ أَرْضِعِيهِ ﴾ [سورة القصص : ٧] . وقال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِذْ أَوْحَيْتُ إِلَى الْحَوَارِينَ أَنْ وَامِنُوا بِي وَبِرَسُولِي قَالُوا ءَامَنَّا [سورة المائدة : ١١١]. وهؤلاء لم يكونوا أنبياء. بل ذلك إلهام، وقد يكون بتوسط الملك ، [٥٠٤] كما كون الرأي قال تعالى : ( وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَن يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْيا أَوْ مِن وَرَايِ حِجَابٍ أَوْ يُرْسِلَ رَسُولًا فَيُوحِيَ بِإِذْنِهِ مَا يَشَاءُ) [سورة الشورى : ٥١] . والآراء والخطأ في الرأى من إلقاء الشيطان، ولو كان صاحبها مجتهداً معذوراً، كما قال غير واحد من الصحابة كأبي بكر، وابن مسعود في بعض المسائل: «أقول فيها برأيي، فإن يكن صواباً فمن الله ، وإن يكن خطأ فمني ومن الشيطان، والله ورسوله بريء منه ) . و ما يكون من الشيطان إذا لم يَقْدِر الإنسان على دفعه لا يأثم به ، كما يراه النائم من تجاوز الله عن أضغاث الشيطان وكاحتلامه في المنام، فإنه وإن كان من الشيطان فقد رفع القلم عن النائم حتى يستيقظ.
The Fourth Station - The Fourteenth Aspect: The attainment of confirmation and support through the angels. And the people have disputed concerning the knowledge that occurs in the heart after reflection and inference, [holding] various opinions. The philosophers say: that is from the emanation of the Active Intellect when the soul is prepared. The Mu'tazila say: it occurs by way of generation. Al-Ash'ari and others say: it occurs by the act of God Almighty, just as all other events occur according to them—they do not assign any cause or wisdom to any events. And the position held by the Salaf and the Imams is that God has made for events causes and wisdoms, and these events may occur by means of angels or jinn, and that what occurs in the heart of knowledge, strength, support, and the like, God may make it happen through the agency of the angels, as He said: [Then your Lord inspired to the angels, 'Indeed, I am with you, so strengthen those who have believed.' (Surah al-Anfal: 12)]. And He said: [You will not find a people who believe in Allah and the Last Day having affection for those who oppose Allah and His Messenger, even if they were their fathers or their sons or their brothers or their kindred. Those – He has decreed faith in their hearts and supported them with a spirit from Him. (Surah al-Mujadila: 22)]. And as the Prophet said: 'Whoever asks for judgment and seeks help in it will be entrusted to it, and whoever does not ask for judgment nor seek help in it, Allah will send down to him an angel to guide him aright.' Guidance (tasdid) is the casting of correct speech into his heart. And He said: [And We inspired to the mother of Moses, 'Suckle him...' (Surah al-Qasas: 7)]. And He said: [And when I inspired to the disciples, 'Believe in Me and in My Messenger,' they said, 'We have believed.' (Surah al-Ma'ida: 111)]. And these were not prophets. Rather that is inspiration (ilham), and it may be through the intermediation of an angel, just as opinion occurs. He said: [And it is not for any human being that Allah should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a partition or that He send a messenger to reveal, by His permission, what He wills. (Surah al-Shura: 51)]. And opinions and error in opinion are from the casting of Satan, even if its possessor is a mujtahid and excused, as more than one of the Companions, such as Abu Bakr and Ibn Mas'ud, said concerning some issues: 'I say concerning it my opinion; if it is correct, it is from God, and if it is wrong, it is from me and from Satan, and God and His Messenger are innocent of it.' And what comes from Satan when a person is unable to repel it, he is not sinning thereby, such as what the sleeper sees—God overlooks the confused dreams of Satan and like nocturnal emission in sleep, for even if it is from Satan, the pen is lifted from the sleeper until he awakens.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological argument by Ibn Taymiyya about the source of correct and erroneous knowledge after reasoning. He begins by noting that people have disputed the nature of knowledge that arises in the heart after reflection and inference (al-ʿilm al-ḥāṣil fī al-qalb ʿuqayb al-naẓar wa al-istidlāl). He summarizes three positions: the philosophers (al-mutafalsifa) claim it is an emanation from the Active Intellect; the Muʿtazila say it occurs by way of generation (tawallud); and al-Ashʿarī and others attribute it directly to God's act without secondary causes or wisdom. Ibn Taymiyya then presents the view of the Salaf and the Imams: that God has established causes and wisdoms for events, and that knowledge, strength, and support in the heart may occur through angelic agency. He supports this with Quranic verses and hadith. For example, in Surah al-Anfal, God inspired the angels to strengthen the believers; in Surah al-Mujadila, He supported the believers with a spirit from Him. The Prophet's hadith about seeking judgment indicates that God sends an angel to guide aright (yusaddiduhu) those who do not seek worldly authority, which involves casting correct speech (al-qawl al-sadād) into the heart. Other verses show inspiration (īḥāʾ) to non-prophets like the mother of Moses and the disciples, indicating this is a form of ilhām that may occur through an angel. Ibn Taymiyya then turns to error: opinions and mistakes in opinion come from satanic casting (ilqāʾ al-shayṭān). Even a mujtahid who errs is excused but still acknowledges his opinion may be wrong and from Satan, as reported from the Companions like Abu Bakr and Ibn Masʿūd. Finally, he clarifies that what comes from Satan that a person cannot repel—such as dreams or nocturnal emissions—is not sinful; the pen is lifted from the sleeper. Thus, correct certainty is a divine gift via angels, while error has a satanic origin, but the person may be forgiven if involuntarily affected.

Key Terms
التثبيت والتأييد
إلهام
إلقاء الشيطان
التسديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Salaf view presented by Ibn Taymiyya, what is the source of correct knowledge after reasoning?
A) Emanation from the Active Intellect
B) Generation (tawallud) from previous actions
C) Direct creation by God without cause
D) Divine act through the agency of angels

Key Takeaway
Correct knowledge after reasoning is a divine gift mediated by angels, while error originates from Satan, but the sincere mujtahid is not held accountable for involuntary mistakes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of Knowledge Without Prophets
Author refutes the claim that spiritual exercise can replace prophetic revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique against the claim that spiritual exercise can replace prophetic revelation and identify the corrupt principle underlying it.

Core Idea
Spiritual purification cannot substitute for prophetic revelation.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya targets a claim made by various esoteric groups: that through spiritual exercise one can attain the very knowledge brought by prophets without needing their reports. He deconstructs this claim, tracing it to a corrupt philosophical principle imported from Hellenistic thought. We will dissect his argument step by step to understand how he defends the necessity of prophetic mediation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimants
Locate the groups Ibn Taymiyya mentions in the text: the Batini Shia (e.g., Brethren of Purity), Batini Sufis (e.g., Ibn Sab'in, Ibn Arabi), and even Abu Hamid al-Ghazali. These are the ones advocating for knowledge without prophets.
‘Batini’ refers to those who prioritize esoteric meanings over apparent revelation.
2
Extract their claim
What exactly do they assert? That through spiritual exercise (riyāḍa), purification of the heart, and moral self-cleansing, one can know the realities of faith in God, angels, books, prophets, the Last Day, jinn, and devils—all without needing the prophets' reports.
This is a strong epistemic claim: direct access to revealed truths.
3
Identify the corrupt principle
Ibn Taymiyya says this claim is built on a corrupt principle (al-aṣl al-fāsid): the idea that when the soul is purified, such knowledge descends upon the heart from the Active Intellect (al-ʿaql al-faʿʿāl) or some similar source. This principle originates from Greek philosophy, not from Islam.
The Active Intellect is a Neoplatonic concept, rejected by Ibn Taymiyya as a valid source of knowledge.
4
Assess the grounds of his critique
Determine whether Ibn Taymiyya's objection is epistemological, revelational, or both. He argues that the claimed source (Active Intellect) is not endorsed by revelation, and that the entire notion undermines the necessity of prophetic intermediation, which is a core Islamic belief.
His critique is both revelation-based (Quran and Sunnah affirm the need for prophets) and epistemological (the Active Intellect is an unproven philosophical construct).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول بمعرفة الغيب بدون توسط الأنبياء. وما يذكره طوائفُ من الباطنية - باطنية الشيعة كأصحاب رسائل إخوان الصفا، وباطنية الصوفية كابن سبعين وابن عربي وغيرهما - وما يوجد في كلام أبي حامد وغيره من أن أهل الرياضة وتصفية القلب وتزكية النفس بالأخلاق المحمودة قد يعلمون حقائق ما أخبرت به الأنبياء من أمر الإيمان بالله والملائكة والكتاب والنبيين واليوم الآخر ومعرفة الجن والشياطين، بدون توسط خبر الأنبياء هو بناء على هذا الأصل الفاسد. وهو أنهم إذا صفوا نفوسهم نزل على قلوبهم ذلك، إما من جهة العقل الفعال (۲) أو غيره (٢).
Refuting the claim of knowing the unseen without the intermediary of the prophets. And what groups of the Batinis mention - the Batini Shia like the authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity, and the Batini Sufis like Ibn Sab'in and Ibn Arabi and others - and what appears in the speech of Abu Hamid [al-Ghazali] and others, that the people of spiritual exercise, purification of the heart, and self-cleansing with praiseworthy morals may know the realities of what the prophets informed about concerning belief in God, the angels, the Book, the prophets, the Last Day, and knowledge of jinn and devils, without the intermediary of the prophets' report, is built upon this corrupt principle. That is, that if they purify their souls, that will descend upon their hearts, either from the 'Active Intellect' or other than it.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a direct refutation (ibṭāl) of the claim that one can attain knowledge of the unseen (al-ghayb) without the intermediary of prophets. Ibn Taymiyya identifies the groups that promote this view: Batini Shia (e.g., authors of the Epistles of the Brethren of Purity), Batini Sufis (e.g., Ibn Sab'in and Ibn Arabi), and even Abu Hamid al-Ghazali. Their claim is that through spiritual exercise (riyāḍa), purification of the heart (taṣfiyat al-qalb), and self-cleansing (tazkiyat al-nafs) with praiseworthy morals, one can come to know the very realities that prophets brought—such as faith in God, angels, scriptures, prophets, the Last Day, and knowledge of jinn and devils—without needing the prophets' reports. Ibn Taymiyya declares this is based on a corrupt principle (al-aṣl al-fāsid), namely that if one purifies the soul, these truths descend on the heart from the 'Active Intellect' (al-ʿaql al-faʿʿāl) or some other source, a concept borrowed from Hellenistic philosophy.

Key Terms
الباطنية
الرياضة
العقل الفعال

B) The Active Intellect

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the claim of gaining prophetic knowledge without prophets rests on a corrupt philosophical principle, not on Islamic sources.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Ghazali on Kashf and Prophetic Authority
Critique of Ghazali's use of kashf to override prophetic reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the core of Ibn Taymiyya's critique against al-Ghazali's reliance on spiritual unveiling and explain how it undermines prophetic intermediary in matters of report (al-umūr al-khabariyya).

Core Idea
When personal unveiling becomes the judge of revelation, prophethood becomes optional.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes aim at al-Ghazali, a towering figure in Islamic thought, for what he sees as a dangerous prioritization of personal spiritual experience (kashf) over the reports brought by the prophets. This critique is not merely about Sufi practice; it strikes at the very foundation of how Muslims should receive and interpret divine revelation. Ibn Taymiyya traces this error back to the principles of the philosophers, linking Ghazali's method to a broader threat to prophetic authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target and the charge
Read the opening: 'كلام في الغزالي قادح فيه.' Ibn Taymiyya is directly attacking al-Ghazali. The charge is that Ghazali nullifies the intermediary role of prophets in 'al-umūr al-khabariyya'—matters known only through prophetic reports.
The term 'قادح فيه' indicates a severe criticism, not a minor disagreement.
2
Understand the mechanism of kashf
Ibn Taymiyya explains Ghazali's method: through spiritual exercise (الرياضة), realities are unveiled to the individual. Whatever agrees with one's unveiling is accepted; whatever disagrees is interpreted metaphorically (تأوّل). This makes the prophet's message dependent on personal experience.
This reverses the proper order: revelation should judge experience, not vice versa.
3
Grasp the consequence for faith
The text reports that Muslims said harsh things about Ghazali because of this, stating 'كلامه يقدح في الإيمان بالأنبياء'—his speech detracts from faith in the prophets. Why? Because it makes the truth of prophecy relative to individual unveiling.
Faith in prophets requires accepting their reports unconditionally, not conditional on one's own spiritual state.
4
Trace the source of the error
Ibn Taymiyya concludes by saying this is taken from the principles of the philosophers (أصول هؤلاء الفلاسفة). This links Ghazali's error to the Hellenistic philosophical tradition that Ibn Taymiyya critiques throughout his work.
This is a recurring theme: Greek philosophy is the root of many deviations in Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلام في الغزالي قادح فيه. وأبو حامد يكثر ذكر هذا. وهو مما أنكره عليه المسلمون، وقالوا فيه أقوالاً غليظة بهذا السبب الذي أسقط فيه توسط الأنبياء في الأمور الخبرية، وجعل ما جاء به الرسول بالأنبياء وما لا يتأوّل؛ لكن إذا ارتاض الإنسان انكشفت له الحقائق فما وافق كشفه أقره وما لم يوافقه تأوّله ولهذا قالوا كلامه يقدح في الإيمان بالأنبياء وذلك أن هذا مأخوذ من أصول هؤلاء الفلاسفة.
A speech about Ghazali criticizing him. And Abu Hamid frequently mentions this. And it is something that the Muslims denounced against him, and they said harsh things about him because of this reason, by which he nullified the intermediary of the prophets in matters of reports (al-umūr al-khabariyya), and made what the Messenger brought [dependent] on the prophets and what is not interpretable; but if a person exercises spiritually, realities are unveiled to him, so what agrees with his unveiling he affirms, and what does not agree he interprets metaphorically. For this reason they said his speech detracts from faith in the prophets, and that is because this is taken from the principles of these philosophers.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a direct critique of al-Ghazali. Ibn Taymiyya states that Ghazali frequently promoted the idea that spiritual exercise can unveil realities, effectively nullifying the need for prophetic intermediary in matters of reports (al-umūr al-khabariyya—things known only through revelation). Ghazali is said to have made the Prophet's message subject to personal unveiling: what matches one's unveiling is accepted, and what does not is interpreted metaphorically (ta'wīl). Ibn Taymiyya reports that Muslims harshly condemned Ghazali for this, saying his speech detracts from faith in the prophets. Ibn Taymiyya traces this error to the principles of the philosophers (uṣūl hā'ulā' al-falāsifa), reinforcing his earlier connection to Hellenistic thought.

Key Terms

كشف
تأوّل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It strengthens faith in prophets
B) It detracts from faith in prophets
C) It is a valid method of interpretation
D) It is a minor issue

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that Ghazali's prioritization of kashf over prophetic reports effectively nullifies the intermediary role of prophets and undermines faith in their message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Ghazali's Philosophical Influence
Author contrasts mutakallimun and philosophers, criticizing Ghazali's philosophical influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's key arguments distinguishing theologians from philosophers and explain his critique of al-Ghazali's philosophical leanings.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya argues that Ghazali was corrupted by Ibn Sina's philosophy, leading to heretical claims rejected by Sunni consensus.

This passage is part of Ibn Taymiyya's larger project to critique Greek logic and philosophy. Here, he contrasts the methods of the mutakallimun (theologians) with those of the philosophers, accusing al-Ghazali of being influenced by Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa' to the point of making claims that contradict the teachings of the Prophet. Ibn Taymiyya cites verses from Ibn al-Arabi and points to Ghazali's 'Mishkat al-Anwar' and 'Kimiya' al-Sa'ada' as containing philosophical doctrines. He then notes that all major Sunni scholars—including the four imams, verified Sufis, and the theologians of Ahl al-Sunna—rejected such claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main contrast
Read the opening sentence: 'The difference between the methods of the theologians and the methods of the philosophers.' This sets up the core dichotomy. Note that Ibn Taymiyya is not opposing all reason, but specific philosophical methods that he sees as corrupting revelation.
Mutakallimun here refers to those who use dialectical reasoning within an Islamic framework.
2
Locate the accusation against Ghazali
Find the phrase 'Abu Hamid was made ill by al-Shifa'. This is a direct criticism: Ghazali was negatively influenced by Ibn Sina's encyclopedia of philosophy. Ibn Taymiyya uses this to argue that Ghazali deviated from the theologians' method.
Al-Shifa is Ibn Sina's major philosophical work.
3
Analyze the poetic evidence
Ibn Taymiyya quotes Ibn al-Arabi's verses that condemn those who follow Aristotle ('the religion of Aristotle') in contrast to the Prophet ('the religion of the Chosen One'). This reinforces the idea that Ghazali's influence led him away from orthodoxy.
The poem emphasizes the gravity of the corruption.
4
Identify the specific philosophical claim
Ibn Taymiyya points to Ghazali's works 'Mishkat al-Anwar' and 'Kimiya' al-Sa'ada' where he claims that a spiritual ascetic can hear God's speech like Moses. This is presented as a philosophical error that exceeds proper revelational boundaries.
This claim challenges the Sunni belief that prophetic experience is unique.
5
Observe the unanimous rejection
Ibn Taymiyya enumerates groups that rejected Ghazali's views: followers of the four madhhabs, verified Sufis, and Ahl al-Hadith. This shows that the critique is not sectarian but based on consensus of Sunni scholarship.
The 'verified Sufis' are those who adhere to the Sharia.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : الفرق بين طرق المتكلمين وطرق الفلاسفة. تأثر الغزالي. ولهذا كانوا يقولون: أبو حامد أمرضه الشَّفاء (١). وأنشد فيه ابن العربي الأبياتِ المعروفة عنه حيث قال:
من كتاب «الشفا»
011/

فماتوا على دين رِسْطالِس وعشنا على مِلَّة المُصطَفَى (٣)
على الغزالي
وكلامه في مشكاة الأنوار) وفي كيمياء السعادة هو قول هؤلاء. ولهذا يذكر أن إنكار العلماء صاحب الرياضة قد يَسْمَعُ كلامَ الله كما سمعه موسى بن عمران عليه السلام»، وأمثال هذه الأقاويل التي أنكرها علماء المسلمين العارفين بما جاء به الرسول من الكتاب والسنة من الطوائف كلها - من أصحاب الشافعي ومالك وأبي حنيفة وأحمد بن حنبل، والصوفية المحققين المتَّبعين للرسول وأهل الحديث، ونُظَّارِ أهل السنة .
The Fourth Station - the Fourteenth Aspect: The difference between the methods of the theologians (mutakallimun) and the methods of the philosophers. The influence of al-Ghazali. And for this reason they used to say: 'Abu Hamid was made ill by al-Shifa'. And Ibn al-Arabi recited about him the well-known verses:
From the book 'al-Shifa':
We absolve ourselves before God from a people who have a disease from the book 'al-Shifa'
... and often I said: 'O people! You are ... we return to God until God suffices'
When they belittled my warnings, they died upon the religion of Aristotle, and we live upon the religion of the Chosen One (the Prophet) - upon Ghazali.
And his words in Mishkat al-Anwar and in Kimiya' al-Sa'ada are the words of these (philosophers). And for this reason he mentions that the deniers of the scholars, the people of spiritual exercise, may hear the speech of God as Moses ibn Imran, peace be upon him, heard it. And similar sayings which the Muslim scholars who know what the Messenger brought from the Book and the Sunnah from all groups - from the followers of al-Shafi'i, Malik, Abu Hanifa, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and the verified Sufis who follow the Messenger and the people of Hadith, and the theologians of Ahl al-Sunna - have rejected.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is a critique of Ghazali's philosophical leanings, framed as the fourth station (maqām) and fourteenth aspect (wajh) of a larger argument distinguishing the methods of theologians (mutakallimūn) from those of philosophers. Ibn Taymiyya accuses Ghazali of being influenced by Ibn Sina's 'al-Shifa' (The Cure), to the point that people said 'Abu Hamid was made ill by al-Shifa'. He cites verses from Ibn al-Arabi (likely the Qadi Abu Bakr ibn al-Arabi) that condemn those who follow Aristotle due to this influence. Ibn Taymiyya then points to Ghazali's works 'Mishkat al-Anwar' and 'Kimiya' al-Sa'ada' as containing the philosophers' ideas, including the claim that a spiritual ascetic (ṣāḥib al-riyāḍa) can hear God's speech as Moses did. Such claims were rejected by all mainstream Muslim scholars: the four madhhab imams, verified Sufis who follow the Prophet, and the theologians of Ahl al-Sunna.

Key Terms
المتكلمين
الشفاء
الصوفية المحققين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes the method of theologians from philosophers by critiquing Ghazali's borrowing of Ibn Sina's ideas, which he argues led to claims rejected by the Sunni scholarly consensus.

Balancing Purification and Revelation in Knowledge
Author defends al-Ghazali on purification but subordinates it to revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of two opposing positions and articulate his epistemological principle that purification aids knowledge only when subordinated to the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Purification aids knowledge, but revelation is the ultimate criterion.

Ibn Taymiyya enters a debate between those who deny any role for spiritual purification in knowledge and those who elevate personal unveiling above revelation. He steers a middle path: piety and heart-purification are powerful aids, but they are wholly dependent on the Quran and Sunnah. Without this anchor, even purified souls risk deception by the devil. This lesson unpacks his epistemological balancing act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rejected positions
First, note the group that denies purification affects knowledge (the rationalists). Second, note the group that elevates kashf and qiyas above the Prophet's words (some Sufis/philosophers). Ibn Taymiyya rejects both extremes.
He defends al-Ghazali against the first group, but also warns against the second.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's own thesis
He asserts that piety and purification are among the greatest means for knowledge. But he immediately qualifies: 'But it is necessary to hold fast to the Book and Sunnah in knowledge and action.' This is his core principle.
Notice the word 'but' signals a crucial qualification.
3
Analyze his critique of kashf and qiyas
He declares that the Prophet's words clarify truth by themselves; no one's unveiling or analogy can be a criterion over them. Anything called 'kashf' or 'qiyas' contradicting the Prophet is corrupt.
He labels such claims as 'philosophical analogy and Sufi imagination'.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
He quotes two verses: one warns that turning from the Remembrance (Quran) results in a devil becoming a companion; the other promises that following Allah's guidance prevents misguidance. These prove the necessity of revelation for protection.
The devil can cast things even into a purified soul without revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انتصار المصنف للغزالي في الحق لا يمكن أحدا بنفسه وقد أنكر عليه طائفة من أهل الكلام والرأى كثيراً مما قاله من الحق، وزعموا أن طريقة الرياضة وتصفية القلب لا تؤثر في حصول العلم وأخطأوا أيضاً في هذا النفي، بل الحق أن التقوى وتصفية القلب من أعظم الأسباب على نيل العلم . لكن لا بد من الاعتصام بالكتاب والسنة في العلم والعمل، ولا يمكن أن أحداً بعد معرفة الغيب الرسول يعلم ما أخبر به الرسول من الغيب بنفسه بلا واسطة الرسول، ولا يستغني أحدٌ في معرفة الغيب عما جاء به الرسولُ . وكلام الرسول مبين للحق بنفسه، ليس كشف أحد ولا قياسه عِياراً عليه . فما وافق كشف الإنسان وقياسه وافقه وما لم يكن كذلك خالفه . بل ما يسمى «كشفاً» و «قياساً» هو مخالف للرسول. فهذا قياس فاسد وخيال فاسد وهو الذي يقال فيه نعوذ بالله من قياس فلسفي وخيال صوفي . والإنسان قد يصفّي نفسَه ويُلقي الشيطان في نفسه أشياء، فإن لم يعتصم بالذكر المنزّل وإلا اقترن به الشيطان، كما قال تعالى : ( وَمَن يَعْشُ عَن ذِكْرِ الرَّحْمَنِ نُفَيْضٌ لَهُ شَيْطَانَا فَهُوَ لَهُ قَرِينُ ﴾ [سورة الزخرف : ٣٦]. وقوله: ﴿فَمَنِ اتَّبَعَ هُدَايَ فَلَا يَضِلُّ وَلَا يَسْقَى﴾
The author's defense of al-Ghazali regarding the truth: No one can [attain knowledge] by himself. And a group from the people of kalam and opinion have denied much of what he said of the truth, and they claimed that the method of spiritual exercise and purification of the heart does not affect the attainment of knowledge, and they also erred in this negation. Rather, the truth is that piety and purification of the heart are among the greatest means for attaining knowledge. But it is necessary to hold fast to the Book and the Sunnah in knowledge and action, and it is impossible for anyone after knowing the unseen of the Messenger to know what the Messenger informed of the unseen by himself without the mediation of the Messenger, nor is anyone independent in knowing the unseen from what the Messenger brought. And the speech of the Messenger clarifies the truth by itself; no one's unveiling or analogy is a criterion over it. So whatever agrees with a person's unveiling and analogy agrees with it, and whatever is not so contradicts it. Rather, what is called 'unveiling' and 'analogy' is contradictory to the Messenger. So this is a corrupt analogy and a corrupt imagination, and it is said about it: we seek refuge with Allah from philosophical analogy and Sufi imagination. And a person may purify his soul, and the devil casts things into him; if he does not hold fast to the revealed remembrance, the devil will accompany him, as Allah said: 'And whoever turns away from the remembrance of the Most Gracious, We appoint for him a devil, so he becomes his companion' [Surat al-Zukhruf: 36]. And His saying: 'So whoever follows My guidance, he will not go astray nor be wretched' [Surat Taha: 123].
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a defense of al-Ghazali's position on the role of spiritual purification in acquiring knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya begins by stating that a group of theologians and rationalists denied al-Ghazali's claim that spiritual exercise and purification of the heart affect the attainment of knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya asserts that they erred in this denial; rather, piety and purification are among the greatest means for knowledge. However, he immediately qualifies this by emphasizing the necessity of adhering to the Book and Sunnah. No one can independently know the unseen that the Prophet reported without his mediation. The Prophet's words are self-evident in clarifying truth; neither personal unveiling nor analogical reasoning can override them. Anything that calls itself 'unveiling' or 'analogy' that contradicts the Prophet is corrupt. Finally, Ibn Taymiyya warns that even when a person purifies himself, the devil can whisper to him, and only by holding to the revealed remembrance (the Quran) can he be protected. He cites two Quranic verses as evidence. The overall message is that true knowledge requires both inner purification and strict fidelity to revelation.

Key Terms
تصفية القلب
الكتاب والسنة
كشف

B) Purification is useless for knowledge
C) Purification is a great means but requires adherence to the Book and Sunnah
D) Purification is only for spiritual experiences, not knowledge

Key Takeaway
True knowledge requires both inner purification and unwavering fidelity to revelation; neither is sufficient alone.

?

Distinction Between Theologians and Philosophers
Author refutes the accusation of methodological similarity between theologians and philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key doctrinal differences between Islamic theologians and logician-philosophers as presented by Ibn Taymiyya, and evaluate his critique of the philosophical reduction of prophethood.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the claim that theologians and philosophers share the same method, exposing the philosophers' reduction of prophethood to mere human achievement.

This passage is Ibn Taymiyya's response to an objection: 'The logicians' enumeration of the means of knowledge is also found in the speech of the Muslim theologians.' He gives two decisive answers. First, not everything theologians say is true — only what the Messenger brought is true. Second, the theologians do not follow the philosophers' path at all, especially regarding prophecy. Ibn Taymiyya then lists several doctrines that the theologians unanimously reject, which the philosophers uphold, showing a fundamental divergence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection being answered
Find the objection stated at the beginning: the logicians' means of knowledge are also found in the theologians' words. Notice the author's initial setup.
2
Extract the two answers given by the author
The author gives two aspects (وجهين). Read each one carefully. The first concerns the nature of truth and the Salaf's censure of kalam that contradicts revelation. The second is the core difference: theologians do not confine prophecy within a human method.
3
List the doctrines that theologians reject but philosophers uphold
Scan the passage for phrases like 'ليس فيهم من يقول' (there is none among them who says). These are points of consensus among theologians, e.g., denying God's knowledge of particulars, eternity of spheres, etc.
4
Analyze the author's critique of the 'First Intellect' hadith
The author refutes the philosophers' use of a fabricated hadith. Note how he rejects the identification of the First Intellect with the Pen, and shows the hadith is actually against them.
The hadith is fabricated per hadith experts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرق بين طرق متكلمي الإسلام وطرق المناطقة الفلاسفة فإن قيل : ما ذكره أهل المنطق من حصر طرق العلم يوجد نحو منه في كلام متكلمي المسلمين، بل منهم من يذكره بعينه إما بعباراتهم وإما بتغيير العبارة، قيل: الجواب من وجهين . أحدهما أن ليس كل ما يقوله المتكلمون حقاً بل كل ما جاء به الرسول فهو حق، وما قاله المتكلمون وغيرهم مما يخالف ذلك فهو باطل . وقد عُرف ذم السلف والأئمة لأهل الكلام المحدّث المشتمل على الباطل المخالف للكتاب والسنة. وقد بسط الكلام عليهم في غير هذا الموضع ومرّ أن الكلام المذموم الذي ذمه السلفُ الطيب - أتباعُ الصحابة والتابعين لهم بإحسان ـ هو الكلام الباطل، وهو المخالف لما جاء به الرسول . وهذان وصفان ملازمان فكل ما خالف ما جاء به الرسول فهو باطل، وكل كلام قاعدة كلية لمعرفة الباطل في الدين باطل فهو مخالف لما جاء به الرسول. وبطلان ذلك قد يُعلم بالأدلة العقلية مع دلالة الشرع على بطلانه ودلالة الشرع تكون تارة بالإخبار عن الحق والباطل، وتارةً بالإرشاد والهداية إلى الأدلة التي بها يُعرف الحق، وينظر العاقل في تلك الأدلة التي أرشد الرسول إليها ودَلَّ عليها . الثاني أن يقال : متكلموا الإسلام لم يسلكوا طريق هؤلاء الفلاسفة فإنه ليس فيهم بيان ما خالف فيه المتكلمون أحد يَحْصُر طرقَ العلم حصراً يَدْخُل فيه الأنبياء كما فعل هؤلاء حيث جعلوا ما علمه الأنبياء داخلاً في طريقهم، فجعلوا النبوة من جنس ما يكون لبعض الناس إذا كان فيه ذكاء وزهد بل المتكلمون متفقون على أن النبي يُعلمه الله بما لا يُعلم به غيره بمشيئة الرب وقدرته فإنهم متفقون على أن الله يفعل بمشيئته وقدرته، وأنه يرسل ملكاً إلى النبي، وهو يعلم الملك، ويعلم ما يقول وما يقوله للنبي . ليس فيهم من يقول إن الله لا يعلم الجزئيات، ولا أن الله ليس بقادر مختار، ولا أن الأفلاك قديمة أزلية، ولا من ينكر معاد الأبدان، ولا من يقول إن ملائكة الله مجرّدُ ما يُتَخَيَّل في النفوس كما يُتَخَيَّل للنائم، ولا كلام الله مجرّد ما يتخيل في النفوس من الأصوات، ولا من يقول إن ما يَعْلَمه الأنبياء من الغيب إنما يفيض على نفوسهم من النفس الفلكية، ولا يجعل أحدهم اللوح المحفوظ» هو النفس الفلكية. ولا يقول أحد منهم إن شيئاً غير الله أبدع ما سواه كما يقوله هؤلاء : إن «العقل الأول أبدع كل ما سواه من الممكنات، ويسمّيه من ينتسب إلى الإسلام منهم «القلم». ويظنون أن الحديث المروي «أن أول ما خلق الله العقل قال له: «أَقْبل» فأقبل ، ثم قال له : «أَدْبر) فأدبر ، هو هذا العقل. والحديث لفظه حجة عليهم، لا لهم. هذا فلو كان حجة لهم لم يَجُز التمسك به لأنه موضوع باتفاق أهل المعرفة بالحديث، كما ذكر ذلك الدارقطني، وابن حبان، وأبو الفرج ابن الجوزي،
The difference between the methods of the Muslim theologians and the methods of the logician-philosophers. For if it is said: 'What the people of logic mentioned of enumerating the means of knowledge is found similarly in the speech of the Muslim theologians; indeed, some of them mention it exactly, either in their expressions or with a change of expression.' It is said: The answer is from two aspects. The first is that not everything the theologians say is truth; rather, everything the Messenger brought is truth, and what the theologians and others say that contradicts that is false. And the censure of the Salaf and the Imams for the modern kalam that contains falsehood contradictory to the Book and Sunnah is well known. And the discussion about them has been expanded elsewhere, and it was mentioned that the blameworthy kalam which the good Salaf—the followers of the Companions and the Successors in goodness—censured is the false kalam, which contradicts what the Messenger brought. And these two descriptions are inseparable: so whatever contradicts what the Messenger brought is false, and every false kalam is a universal principle for knowing falsehood in the religion is contradictory to what the Messenger brought. And its falsehood may be known by rational proofs along with the evidence of the Sharia on its falsehood, and the evidence of the Sharia is sometimes by informing about truth and falsehood, and sometimes by guiding and directing to the proofs by which the truth is known, and the rational person looks into those proofs to which the Messenger guided and indicated. The second [aspect] is that the Muslim theologians did not follow the path of these philosophers, for there is not among them one who enumerates the means of knowledge in a way that includes the prophets as these did, for they made what the prophets knew part of their path, so they made prophethood of the same kind as what is possible for some people if they possess intelligence and asceticism. Rather, the theologians agree that God teaches the prophet by what He does not teach anyone else, by the will and power of the Lord, for they agree that God acts by His will and power, and that He sends an angel to the prophet, and the prophet knows the angel, and knows what he says and what the angel says to him. There is none among them who says that God does not know particulars, nor that God is not capable and choosing, nor that the celestial spheres are eternal, nor one who denies the resurrection of bodies, nor one who says that the angels of God are merely what is imagined in souls as in a dream, nor the speech of God is merely what is imagined in souls of sounds, nor one who says that what the prophets know of the unseen only emanates onto their souls from the celestial soul, nor does any of them make 'the Preserved Tablet' the celestial soul. And none of them says that something other than God originated everything else, as these say: 'the First Intellect originated everything else of possibilities,' and they call it, among those who attribute themselves to Islam, 'the Pen.' And they think that the hadith: 'The first thing God created was the intellect; He said to it: "Come forward," so it came forward; then He said: "Go back," so it went back,' is this intellect. But the hadith is an argument against them, not for them. [And] even if it were an argument for them, it would not be permissible to cling to it because it is fabricated by the agreement of the experts in hadith, as mentioned by al-Daraqutni, Ibn Hibban, and Abu al-Faraj Ibn al-Jawzi.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Taymiyya's response to an objection that Islamic theologians also enumerate the means of knowledge similarly to the logician-philosophers. He gives two answers. First, he asserts that not all speech of theologians is truth; only what the Messenger brought is truth. He notes that the Salaf criticized kalam that contradicts revelation. He then establishes a universal principle: anything that contradicts the Messenger is false, and knowing falsehood in religion is based on this. He adds that Sharia evidence includes both explicit information and guidance to rational proofs. Second, he argues that Islamic theologians do not follow the philosophers' path because the philosophers arbitrarily confine the means of knowledge to include the prophets, reducing prophecy to something achievable by any intelligent ascetic. In contrast, the theologians affirm that God teaches the prophet uniquely, by His will and power, through an angel. Then Ibn Taymiyya lists several doctrines that Islamic theologians unanimously reject, which the philosophers uphold: denying God's knowledge of particulars, denying God's ability and free choice, believing in the eternity of the celestial spheres, denying bodily resurrection, reducing angels and God's speech to mental imaginings, and claiming that prophetic knowledge emanates from a celestial soul. Finally, he refutes the philosophers' identification of the 'First Intellect' with the 'Pen' mentioned in a hadith, noting the hadith is fabricated. This passage is a comprehensive refutation of philosophical encroachment on Islamic theology.

Key Terms
الكلام المذموم
النفس الفلكية
العقل الأول
اللوح المحفوظ
القلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Philosophers reduce prophethood to a human achievement attainable by intelligence and asceticism
C) Theologians believe God does not know particulars
D) Philosophers affirm bodily resurrection

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya establishes that the Islamic theological method is fundamentally distinct from the philosophical method: prophecy is a unique divine gift, not a natural human attainment, and theologians reject core philosophical doctrines like emanation and the eternity of the world.

Criterion of Sainthood: Adherence to Book and Sunnah
Author argues that true sainthood requires complete adherence to revealed law, not inspiration alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's criterion for sainthood and distinguish between the ranks of al-Siddiq and al-muhaddath based on their relationship to revelation.

Core Idea
True sainthood is measured by adherence to Sharia, not mystical experiences.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya cuts to the heart of a major debate: what makes someone a true friend of God (wali)? He argues that sainthood is not about extraordinary inspirations or miracles, but about complete conformity to the Prophet's message. He contrasts two exemplary figures—Abu Bakr (al-Siddiq) and Umar (al-muhaddath)—to show that even divinely inspired insights must submit to the Book and Sunnah. The lesson will guide you through his evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Contrast al-Siddiq and al-muhaddath
Identify the two figures: Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, who perfected his affirmation of the Prophet and received only from him, and Umar al-muhaddath, who received inspiration but tested it against revelation.
Note that al-Siddiq is superior because he does not rely on his own heart, only on the infallible Prophet.
2
Extract the criterion of sainthood
Ibn Taymiyya states that the criterion (mi'yār) of sainthood according to the true gnostics is luzūm al-kitāb wa al-sunnah (adherence to the Book and Sunnah).
This is not just external compliance but a constant checking of inner states against revealed texts.
3
Analyze the evidence from the shaykhs
Review the quotations from Junayd, al-Darani, al-Naysaburi, and others. They all insist that any mystical insight must have 'two witnesses' from the Qur'an and Hadith.
Notice the strong language: 'If you see a man flying in the air, do not be deceived until you see his standing at the commands and prohibitions.'
4
Interpret the story of Abu Yazid al-Bistami
Examine why al-Bistami rejected the visiting shaykh who spat toward the qibla. He concluded that if the man could not be trusted with outward adab, he could not be trusted with inner secrets.
This story illustrates that disregard for even minor aspects of Sharia disqualifies claim to high spiritual rank.
5
Synthesize the hierarchy of saints
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the best saints are those who most perfectly follow the prophets, and Abu Bakr is the foremost saint after the prophets because of his complete emulation (mutāba'a).
This directly refutes any notion that saints can surpass the prophets or that inspiration alone defines sainthood.

Source Text

المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : كون معيار الولاية لزوم الكتاب والسنة

بين الصديق والمحدّث: كنا نتحدث أن السكينة تنطق على لسان عمر. وفي الترمذي وغيره: لو لم أبعث فيكم لبعث فيكم عمر، ولو كان بعدي نبي يُنتَظَر لكان عمر. هذا فالصديق أكمل منه. فإن الصديق كمل في تصديقه للنبي، فلا يتلقى إلا الموازنة ومع عن النبي، والنبي معصوم. والمحدَّث - كعمر - يأخذ أحياناً عن قلبه ما يُلْهَمَه ويُحدّث والمحدَّث به، لكن قلبه ليس معصوماً. فعليه أن يَعْرِض ما أُلقى عليه على ما جاء به الرسول، فإن وافقه قبله، وإن خالفه ردّه. ولهذا قد رجع عمر عن أشياء، وكان الصحابة يناظرونه ويحتجون عليه، فإذا بينت له الحجةُ من الكتاب والسنة رَجَع إليها وتَرَك ما رآه. والصديق إنما يَتَلقَّى عن الرسول، لا عن قلبه. فهو أكمل من المحدث. وليس بعد أبي بكر صديق أفضل منه، ولا بعد عمر محدَّثٌ أفضل منه.

كون معيار الولايات عند العارفين هو لزوم الكتاب والسنة

ولهذا كان الشيوخ العارفون المستقيمون من مشايخ التصوف وغيرهم يأمرون أهل القلوب ـ أرباب الزهد والعبادة والمعرفة، والمكاشفة - بلزوم الكتاب والسنة. قال الجنيد بن محمد: «عِلمنا هذا مقيد بالكتاب والسنة. فمن لم يقرأ القرآن ويكتب الكتاب الحديث لا يَصْلُح له أن يتكلم بعلمنا». وقال الشيخ أبو سليمان الداراني: «إنه لتمرُّ عليّ نكت من القوم فلا أقبلها إلا بشاهِدَين - الكتاب والسنة». وقال أيضاً «ليس لمن أُلهِم شيئاً من الخير أن يفعله حتى يسمع فيه بأثر». وقال أبو عثمان النيسابوري: من أمر السُنَّةَ على نفسه قولاً وفعلا نطق بالحكمة، ومن أمر الهوى على نفسه نطق بالبدعة. فإن الله يقول: ﴿وَإِن تُطِيعُوهُ تَهْتَدُوا﴾. وقال آخر: «من لم يتهم خَوَاطره في كل حال فلا تَعُدَّه في ديوان الرجال».

قصة البسطامي وقيل لأبي يزيد البسطامي: قد قَدِمَ شيخ من أصحابك. فذهب ليزوره، فرآه قد بصق في القبلة، فقال: «ارجعوا بنا! هذا رجل لم يأتمنه الله على أدب من آداب الشريعة فكيف يأتمنه على سِرِّه»؟ وهذا الذي فعله أبو يزيد يُسْتَدَلُّ عليه بما في السنن - أن رجلاً كان إماماً في مسجد من مساجد الأنصار - فجاء النبي فرأى بُصاقاً في القبلة، فقال: من فعل هذا؟ فذكرا الإمام، أن يُصَلُّوا خلفه. فلما جاء ليؤمهم منعوه وقالوا: إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهانا أن نصلي خلفك. فجاء إليه، فذكر ذلك له. فقال: صَدَقُوا. إنك آذيت الله ورسوله. وقال غير واحد من الشيوخ والعلماء: لو رأيتم الرجل يطير في الهواء ويمشي على الماء فلا تغتروا به حتى تنظروا وقوفه عند الأمر والنهي. ومثل هذا كثير في كلام المشايخ والعارفين وأئمة الهدى. وأفضلُ أولياء الله عندهم أكملهم متابعة للأنبياء. ولهذا كان الصديق أفضل الأولياء بعد النبيين. فما طَلَعَتْ شَمْسُ ولا غَرَبت على أحد بعد النبيين والمرسلين أفضل من أبي بكر لكمال متابعته. وهم كلهم متفقون على أنه لا
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: That the criterion of sainthood is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah.

Between al-Siddiq [Abu Bakr] and al-Muhaddath [the inspired one]: We used to say that tranquility speaks upon the tongue of Umar. And in al-Tirmidhi and others: Had I not been sent among you, Umar would have been sent among you; and if there were to be a prophet after me, it would be Umar. This [shows] that al-Siddiq is more perfect than him. For al-Siddiq perfected his affirming of the Prophet, so he only receives the balanced [truth] from the Prophet, and the Prophet is infallible. As for al-Muhaddath – like Umar – he sometimes takes from his heart what is inspired to him, and he is spoken to, but his heart is not infallible. So he must present what is cast to him against what the Messenger brought; if it agrees, he accepts it, and if it contradicts, he rejects it. For this reason, Umar retracted from many things, and the Companions would argue with him and present proofs against him; when the proof from the Book and the Sunnah was made clear to him, he would return to it and abandon his own opinion. As for al-Siddiq, he only receives from the Messenger, not from his own heart. So he is more perfect than the muhaddath. And there is no one after Abu Bakr better than him as a siddiq, nor after Umar better than him as a muhaddath.

That the criterion of [true] spiritual authorities according to the gnostics is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah.

For this reason, the upright gnostic shaykhs – from the masters of tasawwuf and others – command the people of hearts – those of asceticism, worship, knowledge, and unveiling – to adhere to the Book and the Sunnah. Al-Junayd ibn Muhammad said: 'Our knowledge is restricted by the Book and the Sunnah. Whoever does not recite the Qur'an and write the hadith is not fit to speak about our knowledge.' And Shaykh Abu Sulayman al-Darani said: 'Indeed, subtle points from the folk pass by me, but I do not accept them except with two witnesses – the Book and the Sunnah.' He also said: 'It is not for one who is inspired with something good to do it until he hears a [confirming] tradition about it.' And Abu Uthman al-Naysaburi said: 'Whoever puts the Sunnah in charge of his soul, in word and deed, speaks with wisdom; and whoever puts his whims in charge of his soul, speaks with innovation. For Allah says: 'If you obey him, you will be guided.' And another said: 'Whoever does not suspect his inner thoughts in every state, do not count him among the men.'

The story of al-Bistami: It was said to Abu Yazid al-Bistami: 'A shaykh among your companions has arrived.' So he went to visit him, and saw him spit towards the qibla. He said: 'Take us back! This is a man whom Allah has not entrusted with the etiquette of the Sacred Law, so how could He entrust him with His secret?' And what Abu Yazid did is supported by what is in the Sunan – that a man was an imam in a mosque of the Ansar – so the Prophet came and saw spittle towards the qibla. He said: 'Who did this?' They mentioned the imam. [The Prophet said:] 'Do not pray behind him.' When he came to lead them, they prevented him and said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah has forbidden us from praying behind you.' So he went to him and told him that. He said: 'They spoke the truth. You have harmed Allah and His Messenger.' And more than one of the shaykhs and scholars said: 'If you see a man flying in the air and walking on water, do not be deceived by him until you see his standing at the commands and prohibitions.' And such examples are many in the speech of the shaykhs, gnostics, and imams of guidance. The best of Allah's saints according to them are those most perfect in following the prophets. And for this reason, al-Siddiq was the best of the saints after the prophets. No sun has risen nor set upon anyone after the prophets and messengers better than Abu Bakr because of the perfection of his following. And they all agree that there is no...
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument by Ibn Taymiyya, defining the true criterion for sainthood (wilaya) as complete adherence to the Qur'an and Sunnah. He begins by contrasting two types of exemplary figures: al-Siddiq (Abu Bakr) and al-Muhaddath (Umar). Abu Bakr is called 'al-Siddiq' because of his perfect affirmation of the Prophet; he receives knowledge only from the Prophet, who is infallible. Umar is described as 'al-Muhaddath' – one who receives inspiration (hadith) directly into his heart. However, Umar's heart is not infallible, so he must test every inspiration against the revealed law. Ibn Taymiyya notes that Umar would retract his opinions when presented with evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah, showing that even the most inspired companion submits to the textual sources. Hence, Abu Bakr is more perfect because he does not rely on his own heart but solely on the Prophet.

Then Ibn Taymiyya generalizes: the true gnostic shaykhs (al-‘arifun) command the spiritual seekers to adhere to the Book and Sunnah. He quotes Junayd, Abu Sulayman al-Darani, Abu Uthman al-Naysaburi, and others emphasizing that any mystical insight must be verified by the revealed texts. He provides the story of Abu Yazid al-Bistami, who refused to venerate a visiting shaykh because the man spat towards the qibla – a clear violation of proper adab. Abu Yazid concluded that if the man could not be trusted with outward etiquette, he could not be trusted with inward secrets. Ibn Taymiyya supports this with a hadith where the Prophet himself forbade praying behind an imam who had spat toward the qibla.

The passage concludes by stating the consensus of the shaykhs: the best saints are those who most perfectly follow the prophets, and Abu Bakr is the foremost saint after the prophets because of his complete emulation. This entire argument refutes any claim that sainthood can be achieved through inner experiences divorced from the external law. The message is clear: no matter how miraculous the state, one must always measure it by the standard of the sharia.

Key Terms
الصديق
المحدَّث
الولاية
المتابعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the shaykh was from a different Sufi order.
B) Because the shaykh spat towards the qibla, violating a clear rule of adab.
C) Because the shaykh claimed to have visions that contradicted the Qur'an.
D) Because the shaykh did not pray behind an imam.

Key Takeaway
The true measure of sainthood is complete adherence to the Book and Sunnah, not the intensity of mystical inspiration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

True Sainthood: Sharia Over Miracles
Narrative illustrating that true sainthood requires Sharia adherence, not miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract from the story of Abu Yazid the criterion for distinguishing true sainthood from false claims, and apply it to evaluate claims of spiritual authority.

Core Idea
Sharia adherence is the true measure of sainthood, not miraculous feats.

Abu Yazid al-Bistami, a renowned saint, once visited a companion who displayed no miracles but committed a simple Sharia violation. His reaction teaches us a fundamental principle: the commands and prohibitions of the Law are the yardstick for spiritual rank. This lesson uses this narrative to help you parse the Islamic criterion for sainthood, a tool essential for evaluating claims in Tasawwuf and 'Aqida.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering incident
what action of the visiting sheikh caused Abu Yazid to turn back? Locate the specific violation he observed.
It is spitting towards the qibla.
2
Understand Abu Yazid's reasoning
why does Abu Yazid conclude that the sheikh cannot be entrusted with divine secrets? He links failure in Sharia etiquette with lack of divine trust.
He says: 'This man did not entrust God with the etiquette of the Sharia, so how can He entrust him with His secret?'
3
Connect to the Prophetic hadith
how does the hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud reinforce the same principle? The Prophet removed an imam for spitting towards the qibla, showing that even leadership in prayer is contingent on Sharia respect.
The imam was barred from leading prayer.
4
Extract the general principle
what is the overarching rule stated by the scholars? They say: 'If you see a man flying in the air and walking on water, do not be deceived until you see his standing at the command and prohibition.'
Miraculous acts are not indicators of sainthood; Sharia compliance is.

قصة البسطامي وقيل لأبي يزيد البسطامي : قد قَدِمَ شيخ من أصحابك. فذهب ليزوره، فرآه قد بصق في القبلة، فقال: ارجعوا بنا! هذا رجل لم يأتمنه الله على أدب من آداب الشريعة فكيف يأتمنه على سِرِّه؟ وهذا الذي فعله أبو يزيد يُسْتَدَلُّ عليه بما في السنن - سنن أبي داود وغيره - أن رجلاً كان إماماً في مسجد من مساجد الأنصار - فإن كل قبيلة كان لها مسجد ـ فجاء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فرأى بُصاقاً في القبلة، فقال: من فعل هذا؟ فذكروا الإمام، فَنَهَاهُمْ أن يُصَلُّوا خلفه . فلما جاء ليؤمهم منعوه وقالوا : إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهانا أن نصلي خلفك. فجاء إليه، فذكر ذلك له . فقال : صَدَقُوا . إنك آذيت الله ورسوله. وقال غير واحد من الشيوخ والعلماء : لو رأيتم الرجل يطير في الهواء ويمشي على الماء فلا تغتروا به حتى تنظروا وقوفه عند الأمر والنهي.
The story of al-Bistami: It was said to Abu Yazid al-Bistami: 'A sheikh of your companions has arrived.' So he went to visit him, and saw him spitting towards the qibla. He said: 'Take us back! This man did not entrust God with the etiquette of the Sharia, so how can He entrust him with His secret?' And this action of Abu Yazid is supported by what is in the Sunan - Sunan Abi Dawud and others - that a man was an imam in one of the mosques of the Ansar - for every tribe had a mosque - and the Prophet (peace be upon him) came and saw spittle towards the qibla. He said: 'Who did this?' They mentioned the imam, and he forbade them from praying behind him. When he came to lead them, they prevented him and said: 'Verily, the Messenger of God forbade us from praying behind you.' So he went to him and mentioned that. He said: 'They told the truth. You have annoyed God and His Messenger.' And more than one of the sheikhs and scholars said: 'If you see a man flying in the air and walking on water, do not be deceived by him until you see his standing at the command and prohibition.'
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a critical illustration of the criterion for true sainthood in Islam. It presents a narrative about Abu Yazid al-Bistami, a famous Sufi, who judged a visiting sheikh not by his spiritual rank but by his lack of respect for the qibla (a rule of Sharia). The lesson is that external miraculous acts (like flying or walking on water) are not signs of sainthood if the person violates the sacred law. The passage then reinforces this with a hadith about an imam who spat towards the qibla and was removed from his position by the Prophet's command. The conclusion is that adherence to Sharia (al-amr wa al-nahy) is the true measure, not extraordinary abilities.

Key Terms
الوقوف عند الأمر والنهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His ability to perform miracles
B) His knowledge of divine secrets
C) His adherence to Sharia etiquette
D) His spiritual rank among Sufis

Key Takeaway
True sainthood is measured by standing at the commands and prohibitions of Sharia, not by performing miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Task 2: Research one other historical example where a scholar or saint was rejected despite extraordinary abilities due to a Sharia violation. Write a short paragraph comparing it to the story of Abu Yazid.

The Exclusive Path to God: Following the Prophet
Critique of those who claim alternative paths to God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the exclusive role of the Prophet as the only intermediary to God and refute claims of alternative paths using Ibn Taymiyya's reasoning.

Core Idea
No path to God without following the Prophet

Ibn Taymiyya makes a decisive assertion: the only way for servants to reach God is through the intermediary, the Prophet Muhammad. He then censures those who think that saints can bypass this path or are superior to the Prophet. This lesson examines the central claim and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
Find Ibn Taymiyya's statement that the path to God is only through following the intermediary, the Prophet. What is the role of the wasita?
Look for the Arabic term 'الواسطة'.
2
Recognize the deviations criticized
List the false beliefs Ibn Taymiyya attacks: claiming a path without following the Prophet, elevating saints above the Prophet, etc.
These are mentioned after 'مثل من يظن'.
3
Understand the basis of critique
Why does Ibn Taymiyya reject these deviations? He grounds his argument in revelation and the finality of prophethood.
His authority is the Quran and Sunnah.
4
Apply the critique
Use Ibn Taymiyya's reasoning to evaluate any claim that offers a path to God independent of prophetic guidance.
Consider modern parallels in Sufi or spiritual movements.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طريق للعباد إلى الله إلا باتباع الواسطة الذي بينهم وبين الله. وهو الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم. ولكن دخل في طريقهم أقوام ببدع وفسوق وإلحاد. وهؤلاء مذمومون عند الله وعند رسوله وعند أولياء الله المتقين وهم صالحوا عباده مثل من يظن أن لبعض الأولياء طريقاً إلى الله بدون اتباع الرسول، أو يظن أن من الأولياء من يكون مثل النبي، أو أفضل منه، أو أنه يكون من هو خاتم الأولياء أفضل من السابقين الأولين، أو أعلم بالله من خاتم الأنبياء وأمثال هذه المقالات التي تقولها من دخل فيهم من الملاحدة الضالين. ومن هذا الوجه صار قوم يتصوفون يتفلسفون. وتكلم ابن سينا في إشاراته على مقامات العارفين. وقال الرازي في كلام ابن سينا على مقامات شرحه: هذا الباب أجل ما في الكتاب فإنه رتب علم الصوفية ترتيباً ما سبقه إليه من العارفين قبله ولا يلحقه من بعده. وهذا الذي قاله الرازي قاله بحسب معرفته، فإنه لم يكن عارفاً بطريق الصوفية العارفين المتبعين للكتاب والسنة. ولعله قد رأى من صوفية وقته وفيه من الجهالات والضلالات ما رأى أن هذا الكلام أحسن ما يرتب عليه طريقهم. وقد ذكر في مقامات العارفين أمر النبوة التي يثبتونها.
The path for servants to God is only through following the intermediary between them and God, who is the Messenger (peace be upon him). But some people have entered into their path with innovations, immorality, and heresy. These are blameworthy before God and His Messenger and the righteous awliya. Such as one who thinks that some awliya have a path to God without following the Messenger, or thinks that some awliya are like the Prophet or better than him, or that the Seal of the Awliya is better than the early predecessors, or more knowledgeable of God than the Seal of the Prophets, and similar statements uttered by those among them who are misguided atheists. On this account, some who become Sufis also philosophize. Ibn Sina in his 'Isharat' spoke about 'Maqamat al-'Arifin'. And al-Razi said regarding Ibn Sina's words on the stations in his commentary: 'This chapter is the greatest thing in the book, for he arranged the science of Sufism in an arrangement that no one before him preceded him in among the gnostics, and no one after him will catch up.' This statement of al-Razi he made according to his knowledge, for he was not a knower of the path of the Sufi gnostics who follow the Book and the Sunnah. Perhaps he saw among the Sufis of his time what he saw of ignorances and misguidance that made him think that this speech is the best upon which to arrange their path. And he mentioned in the 'Maqamat al-'Arifin' the matter of prophethood which they affirm.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a strong critique of certain Sufi groups who incorporate philosophical ideas and claim that some saints can reach God without following the Prophet. Ibn Taymiyya asserts unequivocally that the only path to God is through the Prophet as intermediary. He then criticizes Ibn Sina's philosophical treatment of Sufi stations in his 'Isharat' and al-Razi's praise of it. Ibn Taymiyya argues that al-Razi lacked true knowledge of the authentic Sufi path based on Quran and Sunnah, and that his approval stems from his exposure to misguided Sufis of his time. The passage highlights the danger of deviating from the prophetic model and the corruption that results when philosophical reasoning is mixed with spirituality.

Key Terms
الواسطة
مقامات العارفين

Key Takeaway
The Prophet is the exclusive intermediary; any claim of a path to God without following him is a deviation.

Critique of Philosophical Sufism: Ibn Sina and al-Razi
Critique of philosophical Sufism, focusing on Ibn Sina and al-Razi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze Ibn Taymiyya's critique of Ibn Sina's 'Maqamat al-'Arifin' and al-Razi's praise of it.

Core Idea
Ibn Sina's philosophical Sufism is a deviation, not an improvement.

In the second part of the passage, Ibn Taymiyya targets the fusion of philosophy with Sufism, specifically Ibn Sina's treatment of the 'stations of the gnostics' in his 'Isharat' and al-Razi's glowing commentary. Ibn Taymiyya argues that al-Razi's praise stems from ignorance of authentic prophetic Sufism.

Guided Path
1
Identify what Ibn Sina wrote
Locate the reference to Ibn Sina's 'Isharat' and his discussion of 'Maqamat al-'Arifin' (stations of the gnostics).
The passage says: 'وتكلم ابن سينا في إشاراته على مقامات العارفين'
2
Understand al-Razi's praise
Al-Razi called this chapter the greatest in the book and said Ibn Sina's arrangement was unprecedented and unsurpassed.
Look for: 'هذا الباب أجل ما في الكتاب'
3
Ibn Taymiyya's critique of al-Razi
Ibn Taymiyya says al-Razi spoke from ignorance, lacking true knowledge of prophetic Sufism, and was influenced by corrupted Sufis of his time.
Key phrase: 'لم يكن عارفاً بطريق الصوفية العارفين المتبعين للكتاب والسنة'
4
Connect philosophy and deviation
Ibn Taymiyya ties the philosophical Sufism of Ibn Sina to the earlier deviations he condemned, showing it is a symptom of the same problem.
The passage begins with 'ومن هذا الوجه صار قوم يتصوفون يتفلسفون'

طريق للعباد إلى الله إلا باتباع الواسطة الذي بينهم وبين الله. وهو الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم. ولكن دخل في طريقهم أقوام ببدع وفسوق وإلحاد. وهؤلاء مذمومون عند الله وعند رسوله وعند أولياء الله المتقين وهم صالحوا عباده مثل من يظن أن لبعض الأولياء طريقاً إلى الله بدون اتباع الرسول، أو يظن أن من الأولياء من يكون مثل النبي، أو أفضل منه، أو أنه يكون من هو خاتم الأولياء أفضل من السابقين الأولين، أو أعلم بالله من خاتم الأنبياء وأمثال هذه المقالات التي تقولها من دخل فيهم من الملاحدة الضالين. ومن هذا الوجه صار قوم يتصوفون يتفلسفون. وتكلم ابن سينا في إشاراته على مقامات العارفين. وقال الرازي في كلام ابن سينا على مقامات شرحه: هذا الباب أجل ما في الكتاب فإنه رتب علم الصوفية ترتيباً ما سبقه إليه من العارفين قبله ولا يلحقه من بعده. وهذا الذي قاله الرازي قاله بحسب معرفته، فإنه لم يكن عارفاً بطريق الصوفية العارفين المتبعين للكتاب والسنة. ولعله قد رأى من صوفية وقته وفيه من الجهالات والضلالات ما رأى أن هذا الكلام أحسن ما يرتب عليه طريقهم. وقد ذكر في مقامات العارفين أمر النبوة التي يثبتونها.
The path for servants to God is only through following the intermediary between them and God, who is the Messenger (peace be upon him). But some people have entered into their path with innovations, immorality, and heresy. These are blameworthy before God and His Messenger and the righteous awliya. Such as one who thinks that some awliya have a path to God without following the Messenger, or thinks that some awliya are like the Prophet or better than him, or that the Seal of the Awliya is better than the early predecessors, or more knowledgeable of God than the Seal of the Prophets, and similar statements uttered by those among them who are misguided atheists. On this account, some who become Sufis also philosophize. Ibn Sina in his 'Isharat' spoke about 'Maqamat al-'Arifin'. And al-Razi said regarding Ibn Sina's words on the stations in his commentary: 'This chapter is the greatest thing in the book, for he arranged the science of Sufism in an arrangement that no one before him preceded him in among the gnostics, and no one after him will catch up.' This statement of al-Razi he made according to his knowledge, for he was not a knower of the path of the Sufi gnostics who follow the Book and the Sunnah. Perhaps he saw among the Sufis of his time what he saw of ignorances and misguidance that made him think that this speech is the best upon which to arrange their path. And he mentioned in the 'Maqamat al-'Arifin' the matter of prophethood which they affirm.
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a strong critique of certain Sufi groups who incorporate philosophical ideas and claim that some saints can reach God without following the Prophet. Ibn Taymiyya asserts unequivocally that the only path to God is through the Prophet as intermediary. He then criticizes Ibn Sina's philosophical treatment of Sufi stations in his 'Isharat' and al-Razi's praise of it. Ibn Taymiyya argues that al-Razi lacked true knowledge of the authentic Sufi path based on Quran and Sunnah, and that his approval stems from his exposure to misguided Sufis of his time. The passage highlights the danger of deviating from the prophetic model and the corruption that results when philosophical reasoning is mixed with spirituality.

Ibn Taymiyya's Redefinition of Fana': True Monotheism vs. Pantheism
Ibn Taymiyya defines true fana' and refutes pantheistic and abstract-essence views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Ibn Taymiyya's definition of praiseworthy fana' from the pantheistic and abstract-essence misconceptions, and identify his critique of each.

Core Idea
True fana' is annihilation of devotion to other than Allah, not annihilation of creation itself.

Ibn Taymiyya takes a term central to Sufi spirituality—fana'—and strips it of its metaphysical extremes. He rescues it from pantheism and from the abstraction of a bare essence, grounding it instead in the concrete monotheism of Ibrahim. In this passage, he lays out the true perfection: not losing awareness of creation, but purifying one's heart of any love or fear that rivals Allah.

Guided Path
1
Locate Ibn Taymiyya's positive definition of fana'
Find where he defines true fana' as hanifiyya and sincerity (ikhlāṣ). He lists specific acts: worship, love, obedience, fear, love/hate for Allah's sake. Note that these involve 'annihilation from' other-than-Allah, not annihilation of the perception of creation.
The definition is operational: it is about redirecting all spiritual and practical orientations exclusively to Allah.
2
Identify the two erroneous views he criticises
First, the pantheistic claim that one does not witness other-than-Allah at all (waḥdat al-wujūd). Second, the view that the highest station is witnessing the essence stripped of attributes (al-dhāt al-mujarrada 'an al-ṣifāt).
Both views distort the proper relationship between Creator and creation.
3
Examine his refutation of each
For pantheism, he calls it heresy (qawl al-mulāḥida). For abstract essence, he argues that such an essence has no external reality and is not the true Lord. The refutation is both theological (based on revelation) and logical (based on the nature of existence).
He uses the example of Ibrahim to show that true perfection requires action, not just contemplation.
4
Summarise his alternative: the perfection of Ibrahim
Ibrahim was commanded to sacrifice his son as a test to remove any lingering love for other-than-Allah. This shows that true fana' is achieved through obedience and trial, not through metaphysical absorption.
Ibn Taymiyya equates this perfection with the religion of Ibrahim (ḥanīfiyya).
5
Assess his criteria for valid spiritual experience
True knowledge of Allah requires action ('amal) and adherence to revealed law. Mere inner states or abstract contemplation are insufficient and can lead to error.
Ibn Taymiyya consistently links spiritual states with practical devotion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحقيقة هذا الفناء هو تحقيق الحنيفية، وهو إخلاص الدين الله . وهو أن يفنى بعبادة الله عن عبادة ما سواه وبمحبته عن محبة ما سواه وبطاعته عن طاعة ما سواه، و بخشيته عن خشية ما سواه، وبالحب فيه والبغض فيه عن الحبّ فيما سواه والبغض فيه فلا يكون لمخلوق من المخلوقين - لا لنفسه ولا لغير نفسه ـ على قلبه شِرْكَةٌ مع الله تعالى. ولهذا أمر إبراهيم الخليل بذبح ابنه، فإنه كان قد سأل الله أن يَهَبه إياه، ولم يكن له ابن غيره . والمقصود هنا أن الله أمر الخليل بذبح ابنه - بِكْرِهِ - امتحاناً له وابتلاء ليُخْرِج مجرد شهود قلبه محبة ما سوى الله ليتمّ كونه خليلاً بذلك. فهذا هو الكمال. وأما مجرد شهوده الحقَّ من غير فعل ما يحبه ويرضاه فهذا ليس بإيمان يُنجي من الله عذاب الله، فضلاً عن أن يكون هذا غاية العارفين . ثم الذي لا يشهد السِّوَى مطلقاً إن شَهِدَه عين السوى فهذا قول الملاحدة القائلين بوحدة الوجود. وإن كان ذلك لغيبيته وإعراضه عن شهود السوى فمن شهد ما سواه مجرد الذات مخلوقاً له ـ آية له - وشهد ما فيه من آياته كان أكمل ممن لم يشهد هذا . وهؤلاء قد يبلغ بهم الأمر إلى أن يروا أن شهود الذات مجرّدةً عن الصفات أعلى مقامات الشهود وهذا من جهلهم. فإن الذات المجردة عن الصفات لا حقيقة لها في الخارج، وليس ذاك ربُّ العالمين. ولكن هم في أنفسهم جردوها عن الصفات وشهدوا مجرّد الذات، كما يشهد الإنسانُ تارةً علم الربّ وتارة قدرته. فهؤلاء شهدوا مجرّد ذات مجردة فهذا في غاية النقص في معرفة الله والإيمان به. فكيف يكون هذا غاية؟
The reality of this annihilation is the realization of pure monotheism (hanifiyya), which is sincerity of religion to Allah. It is that one is annihilated by worship of Allah from worship of other than Him, by love of Him from love of other than Him, by obedience to Him from obedience to other than Him, by fear of Him from fear of other than Him, by love for His sake and hatred for His sake from love for other than Him and hatred for other than Him, so that no creature—neither himself nor others—has any partnership in his heart with Allah Almighty. For this reason He commanded Abraham the intimate friend to sacrifice his son, for he had asked Allah to grant him a son, and he had no other son. The intended meaning here is that Allah commanded the intimate friend to sacrifice his son—his firstborn—as a test and trial for him, to remove from his heart the mere witnessing of love for anything other than Allah, so that he might become an intimate friend by that. This is perfection. As for mere witnessing of the Truth without doing what He loves and is pleased with, this is not a faith that saves from Allah's punishment, let alone being the goal of the knowers. Then, whoever does not witness other-than-Allah at all—if he witnesses it as the essence of other-than-Allah, that is the statement of the heretics who affirm the unity of existence. If that is due to his absent-mindedness and turning away from witnessing other-than-Allah, then whoever witnesses other-than-Allah as a mere essence created for Him—a sign of His—and witnesses the signs within it is more perfect than one who does not witness this. These people may go so far as to consider that witnessing the essence stripped of attributes is the highest station of witnessing, and this is due to their ignorance. For the essence stripped of attributes has no reality in the external world, and that is not the Lord of the worlds. Rather, they in themselves strip it of attributes and witness a mere essence, just as a person sometimes witnesses the knowledge of the Lord and sometimes His power. These have witnessed a mere stripped essence, and that is the utmost deficiency in knowledge of Allah and belief in Him. So how can this be the goal?
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya clarifying the correct meaning of fana' (annihilation) in the Sufi tradition and refuting two erroneous conceptions: first, the pantheistic notion of annihilation in the unity of existence (wahdat al-wujud), and second, the idea that contemplating the divine essence stripped of attributes is the highest spiritual achievement. Ibn Taymiyya begins by defining the praiseworthy fana' as the complete purification of one's inner and outer devotion for Allah alone. It is not the obliteration of awareness of creation, but rather the reorientation of love, fear, obedience, and worship exclusively toward Allah, with no trace of shirk (association) in the heart. He illustrates this with the example of Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham), who was commanded to sacrifice his son as a test to uproot any lingering attachment to the created, thus perfecting his status as an intimate friend (khalil) of Allah. This, Ibn Taymiyya asserts, is the true perfection. He then warns that mere intellectual contemplation or witnessing of the Truth without actual obedience does not constitute saving faith. Next, he attacks the pantheistic position that denies any independent reality to creation, considering it a heresy. He also critiques those who elevate the contemplation of a bare essence—divorced from attributes—to the highest rank. Ibn Taymiyya argues that such a bare essence does not exist externally; it is a mental abstraction, not the true Lord. To worship or seek closeness to such an abstraction is actually a profound deficiency, not a pinnacle of knowledge. Thus, the true goal is not metaphysical monism or abstract contemplation, but steadfast monotheism lived through devotion and action.

الحنيفية
شهود
وحدة الوجود
الذات المجردة عن الصفات

Ibn Taymiyya redefines fana' as exclusive devotion to Allah, rejecting both pantheistic unity and abstract essence as distortions of true monotheism.
