Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Monistic Fana'
Ibn Taymiyya explains the hadith qudsi on nawafil and distinguishes divine love from human desire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the praiseworthy fana' (al-fana' al-mahmud) and the monistic interpretation, using Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the hadith of nawafil and the divine prophetic distinction.

Core Idea
Praiseworthy fana' is not union but realizing 'la ilaha illallah' by witnessing that only God is creator and worthy of worship.

In this passage from his refutation of the logicians, Ibn Taymiyya tackles a key mystical concept: fana' (annihilation). He warns against its monistic interpretation, which he traces to Pharaoh and the philosophers like Ibn Sina. Instead, he recasts fana' as the very essence of tawhid—the realization that no creature shares in divinity, and that true worship requires obedience to the Prophet. This lesson walks you through his critical argument and its reliance on prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of critique
Find the opening phrase where Ibn Taymiyya says the reality of certain people's statement is the reality of Pharaoh's statement. This marks the monistic interpretation as his target.
The term 'حقيقة قولهم' refers to those who claim unity with God (e.g., wahdat al-wujud).
2
Extract the hadith and its orthodox meaning
Read the hadith qudsi about nawafil. Notice that Ibn Taymiyya accepts the hadith but rejects the interpretation that God literally becomes human faculties. Instead, he views it as an expression of divine love and guidance.
The hadith is sound; the dispute is over its meaning.
3
Analyze the distinction between predestinarian and prophetic distinction
Ibn Taymiyya contrasts the one who looks only at qadr (predestination) with the divine prophetic distinction (al-farq al-ilahi al-nabawi). The former loses the moral difference between commanded and prohibited.
This distinction is the essence of 'la ilaha illallah'—affirming that God alone is worthy of worship and obedience.
4
Identify the critique of Ibn Sina's system
Ibn Taymiyya accuses Ibn Sina of combining the monistic claim with heresies: negating attributes, eternity of orbs, denying bodily resurrection, and making prophethood accessible via acquisition.
This shows the danger of philosophical monism—it leads out of Islam.
5
Synthesize the alternative: praiseworthy fana' as tawhid
The praiseworthy fana' is the realization of the testimony of tawhid: witnessing that no creature has any divinity, that only God is creator and only He deserves worship. This is embodied in the verse 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' and requires obedience to the messenger.
This definition anchors fana' in orthodox Islamic theology, not mystical union.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقام الرابع - الوجه الرابع عشر : حقيقة قولهم هي حقيقة قول فرعون بالنوافل حتى أحبَّه . فإذا أحببته كنت سمعه الذي يسمع به، وبصره الذي يُبصر به، ويده التي يبطش بها ورجله التي يمشي بها. فبي يسمع، وبي يبصر، وبي يبطش، وبي يمشي. ولئن سألني لأعطينه ولئن استعاذني لأعذته وما ترددتُ عن شيء أنا فاعله ترددي عن قبض نفس عبدي المؤمن - يكره الموت وأكره مساءته، ولا بد له منه . فالناظر إلى القدر فقط لا يفرق بين مأمور ومحظور سواء كان فرضاً أو الفرق الإلهي هذا لا بد لنفسه أن تميل إلى شيء وتنفر عن شيء، فإن خلو الحي عن النفساني محال . وهو مع الإرادة مطلقاً محال فإن لم يحب ما يحبه الله ويبغض ما يبغضه أحبَّ ما تحبه نفسه . وأبغض ما تبغضه نفسه. فيخرج عن الفرق الإلهي النبوي - الذي هو حقيقة قول «لا إله إلا الله وحقيقة دين الإسلام - إلى الفرق النفساني الشيطاني . والفرق كون عدم التفريق إلحاداً . ثم هؤلاء صاروا فِرَقاً. أما ابن سينا وأمثاله من الملاحدة فإنهم يأمرون بهذا مع سائر إلحادهم من نفي الصفات، وقدم الأفلاك، وإنكار معاد الأبدان، وجعل النبوة تُنال بالكسب كالذكاء والزهد وإنما يفيض عليها فيضُ من العقل الفعال. فيخرج من دين المسلمين واليهود والنصارى . بل الفناء المحمود عند العارفين هو تحقيق شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله . فلا يشهد لمخلوق شيئاً من الإلهية . فيشهد أنه لا خالق غيره، ويشهد أنه لا يستحق العبادة غيره، نعبد وإياك نستعين . ويتحقق بحقيقة قوله: ﴿ إِيَّاكَ نَعْبُدُ وَإِيَّاكَ نَسْتَعِينُ ﴾ . وقوله : فَأَعْبُدُهُ وَتَوَكَّلْ عَلَيْهِ . وإلا فإذا شهدت أنه المستحق للعبادة مع رؤيتك نفسَك لم تشهد حقيقة إياك نستعين، وإذا شهدت حقيقة أنه الفاعل لكل شيء ولم تشهد أنه المستحق للعبادة دون ما سواه وأن عبادته إنما تكون بطاعة رسوله لم تشهد حقيقة إياك نعبد». وإذا تحققت بقوله إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين» تحققت بالفناء في التوحيد الذي بعث الله به رُسله وأنزل به كتبه .
The fourth station - the fourteenth aspect: The reality of their statement is the reality of the statement of Pharaoh. [He said] 'By the supererogatory acts until I love him. When I love him, I become his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his hand with which he strikes, and his foot with which he walks. By Me he hears, by Me he sees, by Me he strikes, and by Me he walks. If he asks Me, I will surely give him; if he seeks refuge with Me, I will surely grant him refuge. I have not hesitated about anything I am doing as I hesitated about taking the soul of My believing servant - he hates death and I hate to displease him, but it is inevitable for him.' So the one who looks only at predestination does not distinguish between commanded and prohibited, whether obligatory or the divine distinction. This self inevitably inclines to something and recoils from something, for the living being to be devoid of the psychic is impossible. And it is absolutely impossible with will. For if he does not love what God loves and hate what God hates, he loves what his self loves and hates what his self hates. Thus he departs from the divine prophetic distinction – which is the reality of the statement 'There is no god but Allah' and the reality of the religion of Islam – to the psychic satanic distinction. And the distinction is that not making a distinction is heresy. Then these people became sects. As for Ibn Sina and his likes among the atheists, they command this along with all their atheism, such as negating the attributes, the eternity of the orbs, denying the resurrection of bodies, and making prophethood attainable through acquisition like intelligence and asceticism, and that it only emanates upon them an emanation from the Active Intellect. So he leaves the religion of Muslims, Jews, and Christians. Rather, the praiseworthy annihilation according to the knowers is the realization of the testimony that there is no god but Allah. So he does not witness for any creature anything of divinity. So he witnesses that there is no creator other than Him, and he witnesses that none deserves worship other than Him. [He says] 'You alone we worship and You alone we seek help.' And it is realized by the reality of His saying: 'You alone we worship and You alone we seek help' [Al-Fatiha:5] and His saying: 'So worship Him and rely upon Him' [Hud:123]. Otherwise, if you witness that He alone deserves worship while seeing yourself, you have not witnessed the reality of 'You alone we seek help'; and if you witness the reality that He is the doer of everything but do not witness that He alone deserves worship and that His worship is only through obedience to His messenger, you have not witnessed the reality of 'You alone we worship.' And if you realize His saying 'You alone we worship and You alone we seek help,' you realize annihilation in the tawhid with which Allah sent His messengers and revealed His books.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya on the true meaning of fana' (annihilation) in Islamic mysticism, contrasting it with false claims. He begins by stating that the reality of certain people's claim (the monists) is the same as Pharaoh's statement. He then quotes a hadith qudsi about the servant drawing near through supererogatory acts (nawafil) until God loves him, and then God becomes his faculties. Ibn Taymiyya explains that the one who looks only at divine predestination (qadr) loses the distinction between commanded and prohibited. The human soul naturally inclines and recoils; if it does not align with God's love and hate, it follows its own desires, leading to a satanic distinction instead of the divine prophetic distinction. This is the reality of la ilaha illallah. He then identifies the sects that fall into this: Ibn Sina and the philosophers who combine this with atheistic beliefs like negating attributes and rejecting bodily resurrection. He clarifies that the praiseworthy fana' is the realization of tawhid: witnessing that no creature shares in divinity, that only God is the creator and only He deserves worship. This is embodied in the verse 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in'. He warns that if one sees God as the only true agent but still sees oneself, one has not truly witnessed 'Iyyaka nasta'in'; if one sees God as the only object of worship but does not follow His messenger, one has not witnessed 'Iyyaka na'budu'. True fana' is to realize both, which is the monotheism of the prophets.

Key Terms
الفناء المحمود
الفرق الإلهي النبوي

D) Following one's spiritual master without question

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya redefines fana' as the realization of tawhid through witnessing that only God is creator and worthy of worship, and warns against the monistic and philosophical distortions.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Wahdat al-Wujud: The Pharaoh Analogy
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud and equates it with Pharaoh's denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's analogical argument equating wahdat al-wujud with Pharaoh's denial and evaluate its validity.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya argues that wahdat al-wujud is not spiritual excellence but a repetition of Pharaoh's denial of a distinct Creator.

Ibn Taymiyya does not merely reject the monistic doctrine of wahdat al-wujud; he diagnoses it as a reincarnation of Pharaoh's denial. In this passage, he dissects the claims of Ibn Arabi and Ibn Sab'in and exposes their logical and theological error by drawing a powerful analogy with the archetypal tyrant. By understanding this critique, you will see how Ibn Taymiyya uses the logical tool of analogical reasoning (qiyas tamthili) in theological polemics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases compared
Find the two positions Ibn Taymiyya is comparing: the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud (followers of Ibn Arabi and Ibn Sab'in) and the statement of Pharaoh. He explicitly says 'So its reality is the statement of Pharaoh.'
2
Extract the common feature ('illa)
What is the shared characteristic? Both deny a Creator distinct from His creation. For Pharaoh, he denied a separate God above the world; for the monists, they assert that creatures' existence is identical to God's existence, thus eliminating distinction.
Ibn Taymiyya writes: 'Pharaoh denied that this existence has a Creator distinct from it.'
3
Check the similarity and differences
Note a difference: Pharaoh knew his claim was false, while the monists are ignorant. Does this affect the analogy? Ibn Taymiyya uses this to emphasize their error, not to weaken it.
Ibn Taymiyya says: 'Pharaoh was inwardly aware that what he said was false... but these are ignorant, misguided.'
4
Evaluate the conclusion
Ibn Taymiyya concludes that the monists' doctrine is essentially the statement of Pharaoh, thus a form of denial. Determine if the analogy proves the doctrine false or just associates it with disbelief.
The analogy functions as a reductio ad absurdum: if monists claim to affirm God, they are actually repeating Pharaoh.
5
Assess the analogical argument's strength
For the analogy to be strong, the 'illa must be truly shared. Here, the core issue is the denial of a distinct Creator. The difference in self-awareness may affect moral culpability but not the logical structure.
Ibn Taymiyya's argument is valid in showing that the logical consequence of wahdat al-wujud is identical to Pharaoh's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا لما سلك ابن عربي وابن سبعين وغيرهما هذه الطريق الفاسدة أورثهم ذلك «الفناء عن وجود السوى». فجعلوا الموجود واحداً ووجود كل مخلوق هو عين وجود الحق. وحقيقة «الفناء» عندهم أن لا يرى إلا الحق، وهو الرائي والمرئي، والعابد والمعبود، والذاكر والمذكور، والناكح والمنكوح والأمرُ الخالق هو الأمر المخلوق. وهو المتصف بكل ما يوصف [به] الوجود من مدح وذم وعُبَّاد الأصنام ما عبدوا غيره، وما ثَمَّ موجود مُغاير له البتة عندهم . وهذا منتهى سلوك هؤلاء الملحدين . فحقيقته قول ،فرعون لأن فرعون كان في الباطن عالماً بأن ما يقوله باطل، وكان قول فرعون جاحداً مُريداً للعلو والفساد. ولهذا جحد وجود الصانع بالكلية. وأما هؤلاء فجُهّال ضلال يحسبون أن ما يقولونه هو حقيقة إثبات الربّ ،وتعظيمه، وهو في الحقيقة قول فرعون . فإن فرعون ما كان ينكر وجود هذا العالم، ولا ينكر أن الموجودات تشترك في مسمى «الوجود» ، وإنما كان ينكر أن لهذا الوجود خالقاً مبايناً له. ولهذا أمر ببناء الصَّرْح ليكذب موسى بزعمه أن للعالم إلها فوقه .
For this reason, when Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and others followed this corrupt path, it caused them to have 'annihilation from the existence of the other'. So they made existence one, and the existence of every creature is the very existence of the Truth. And the reality of 'annihilation' according to them is that one sees only the Truth, and He is the seer and the seen, the worshiper and the worshiped, the rememberer and the remembered, the copulator and the copulated, and the command of the creator is the created thing. And He is described with every description of existence, whether praise or blame, and the worshipers of idols worshiped none but Him, and there is no existence other than Him at all according to them. This is the ultimate conduct of these atheists. So its reality is the statement of Pharaoh, because Pharaoh was inwardly aware that what he said was false, and the statement of Pharaoh was denier, desiring elevation and corruption. For this reason he denied the existence of the Creator entirely. But these are ignorant, misguided who think that what they say is the reality of affirming the Lord and magnifying Him, while in fact it is the statement of Pharaoh. For Pharaoh did not deny the existence of this world, nor did he deny that existents share in the meaning of 'existence', but he denied that this existence has a Creator distinct from it. For this reason he ordered the building of a tower to deny Moses in his claim that the world has a God above it.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud (unity of existence) as advocated by Ibn Arabi and Ibn Sab'in. He explains that their concept of 'fana'' leads them to assert that all existence is one and that the existence of every creature is identical to the existence of God. According to them, annihilation means seeing only the Truth, and they conflate the Creator with the creation, even going so far as to say that idol worshippers worshipped none but God. Ibn Taymiyya condemns this as the ultimate atheism. He then draws an analogy with Pharaoh: Pharaoh inwardly knew his claims were false, but he denied a Creator distinct from the world out of arrogance and desire for corruption. The monists, however, are ignorant and misguided, thinking they are affirming God, but in reality they are repeating Pharaoh's statement. Pharaoh did not deny the existence of the world or that existents share in existence; he denied that there is a Creator separate from the universe. Thus, the monists' denial of a distinct Creator is fundamentally the same as Pharaoh's denial, albeit cloaked in pseudo-spiritual language.

Key Terms
وحدة الوجود
الفناء عن وجود السوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, in what way is the doctrine of wahdat al-wujud similar to the statement of Pharaoh?
A) Both claim that there is no god at all
B) Both deny the existence of the world
C) Both deny that the Creator is distinct from His creation
D) Both worship idols

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's analogical reasoning exposes the logical core of wahdat al-wujud as a denial of the Creator's distinctness, equating it with Pharaoh's archetypal disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify another 'new' doctrine that could be compared to a known falsehood via a shared 'illa. For example, compare the doctrine that 'the Quran is created' with the Mu'tazilite position. Construct an analogical argument similar to Ibn Taymiyya's.
?
In the passage, Ibn Taymiyya claims the monists are like Pharaoh because both deny a distinct Creator. However, Pharaoh knew he was wrong while the monists are ignorant. Does this difference weaken the analogy? Write a brief assessment.

The Monist Concept of Fana' and Ibn Taymiyya's Critique
Ibn Taymiyya describes and refutes the monist concept of fana'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the core claim of the monist doctrine of wahdat al-wujud as critiqued by Ibn Taymiyya and explain why he considers it tantamount to atheism.

Core Idea
Monist fana' erases the distinction between Creator and creature, paving the way to outright atheism.

In this passage from his Radd ala al-Mantiqiyyin, Ibn Taymiyya exposes the dangerous implications of the monist reinterpretation of fana'. He describes how Ibn Arabi and his followers came to believe that all existence is one, and that there is no real difference between the worshiper and the worshipped. This lesson will guide you through that critique.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of fana'
Find the lines where Ibn Taymiyya describes what the monists mean by fana'. What are the pairs of opposites that become identical?
Look for 'وهو الرائي والمرئي' and similar contrasts.
2
Identify the consequences
Once distinctions are erased, the worshiper of idols becomes a worshiper of the Real. What does this imply about idol worship according to the monists?
3
Extract the verdict
Ibn Taymiyya calls this 'the ultimate conduct of these atheists.' What is the basis for that verdict?
The word 'الملحدين' is key.
4
Compare with classical Sufi fana'
Contrast the monist view with the traditional view that fana' is annihilation of ego, not of ontological distinction.
Optional step for advanced students.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فناء أهل ولهذا لما سلك ابن عربي وابن سبعين وغيرهما هذه الطريق الفاسدة أورثهم ذلك «الفناء عن وجود السوى». فجعلوا الموجود واحداً ووجود كل مخلوق هو عين وجود الحق. وحقيقة «الفناء» عندهم أن لا يرى إلا الحق، وهو الرائي والمرئي، والعابد والمعبود، والذاكر والمذكور، والناكح والمنكوح والأمرُ الخالق هو الأمر المخلوق. وهو المتصف بكل ما يوصف به الوجود من مدح وذم وعُبَّاد الأصنام ما عبدوا غيره، وما ثَمَّ موجود مُغاير له البتة عندهم . وهذا منتهى سلوك هؤلاء الملحدين .

حقيقة قولهم فحقيقته قول فرعون لأن فرعون كان في الباطن عالماً بأن ما يقوله باطل، وكان قول فرعون جاحداً مُريداً للعلو والفساد. ولهذا جحد وجود الصانع بالكلية. وأما هؤلاء فجُهّال ضلال يحسبون أن ما يقولونه هو حقيقة إثبات الرب، وتعميمه، وهو في الحقيقة قول فرعون . فإن فرعون ما كان ينكر وجود هذا العالم، ولا ينكر أن الموجودات تشترك في مسمى «الوجود» ، وإنما كان ينكر أن لهذا الوجود خالقاً مبايناً له. ولهذا أمر ببناء الصَّرْح ليكذب موسى بزعمه أن للعالم إلها فوقه . قال تعالى : ( وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَنهَمَنُ ابْنِ لِي صَرْحًا لَعَلَى أَبْلُغُ الأَسْبَبَ أَسْبَابَ السَّمَوَاتِ فَأَطَّلِعَ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّه كَذِبًا وَكَذَلِكَ زُيِّنَ لِفِرْعَوْنَ سُوهُ عَمَلِهِ، وَصُدَّ عَنِ السَّبِيلِ وَمَا كَيْدُ فِرْعَوْنَ إِلَّا فِي تَبَابِ ﴾ [سورة غافر : ٣٦ - ٣٧] . وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَتَأَيُّهَا الْمَلَأُ مَا عَلِمْتُ لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرِي فَأَوْقِدْ لِي يَهَمَنُ عَلَى الطِينِ فَاجْعَل فِي صَرْحًا لَعَلَّى أَطَّلِعُ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّهُ مِنَ الْكَذِبِينَ ) وَاسْتَكْبَرَ هُوَ وَجُنُودُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ وَظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا يُرْجَعُونَ ) فَأَخَذْنَهُ وَجُنُودَهُ فَنَبَذْنَهُمْ فِي الْبَرِّ فَانظُرْ كَيْفَ كَانَ عَقِبَةُ الظَّالِمِينَ ( وَجَعَلْتَهُمْ أَبِمَّةٌ يَدْعُونَ إِلَى النَّارِ وَيَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ لَا يُنصَرُونَ الله وأتبعنَهُمْ فِي هَذِهِ الدُّنْيَا لَعَنَةً وَيَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ هُم مِن الْمَقْبُوحِينَ ﴾ [سورة القصص : ٣٨ - ٤٢] .

وأكثر هؤلاء الملاحدة القائلين بوحدة الوجود يقولون إن فرعون أكمل من موسى، وإن فرعون صادق في قوله «أنا ربكم الأعلى» ، لأن الوجود فاضل ومفضول، والفاضل يستحق أن يكون ربَّ المفضول. ومنهم من يقول : مات مؤمناً، وإن تغريقه كان ليغتسل غُسل الإسلام فإنهم مع قولهم بأن الوجود واحد قد يقولون إما بقول بعضهم: إن الثبوت غيرُ الوجود، وإن ماهيات الممكنات ثابتة، وإن وجود الحق قاض عليها، كما يقول ذلك ابن عربي وغيره ؛ وإما أن يفرق بين المطلق والمعين، كما يقوله صاحبه القُونَوي ؛ وابنُ سبعين قوله قريب من هذا وقد بسط الكلام عليهم في غير هذا الموضع، وإنما ذُكروا هنا لأن هؤلاء هم آخر مراتب فلاسفة الصوفية الذين يقولون إنهم أهل التحقيق والعرفان وكل من سواهم عندهم ناقص بالنسبة إليهم. وقد رأيتُ من هؤلاء غير واحد .

وهم يرتبون الناس طبقات، أدناها عندهم الفقيه، ثم المتكلم، ثم الفيلسوف، ثم الصوفي - أي صوفي الفلاسفة ثم المحقق ويجعلون ابن سينا وأمثاله من الفلاسفة في الطبقة الثانية، وأبا حامد وأمثاله من الصوفية من العشرة، ويجعلون المحقق هو الواحد .

ولهذا ذكر ابن عربي في الفتوحات له أربع عقائد الأول: عقيدة أبي المعالي وأمثاله مجردة عن الحجة، ثم هذه العقيدة بحجتها، ثم عقيدة الفلاسفة، ثم عقيدة المحققين . وذلك أن الفيلسوف يفرّق بين الوجود والممكن، والواجب، وهؤلاء يقولون «الوجود واحد». والصوفي الذي يعظمه هؤلاء هو الصوفي الذي عظمه ابن سينا. وبعده المحقق .

وهؤلاء ليسوا مسلمين ولا يهوداً ولا نصارى بل كثير من المشركين أحسن منهم . حالهم اشتراكهم مع أهل البدع والأهواء وهؤلاء أئمة النظار المتفلسفة وصوفيتهم وشيعتهم كان من أسباب تسلطهم
The annihilation of the people - that is why when Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and others followed this corrupt path, it bequeathed to them 'annihilation from the existence of other'. So they made existence one, and the existence of every creature is the very existence of the Real. The reality of 'annihilation' according to them is that one sees only the Real, and He is the seer and the seen, the worshiper and the worshipped, the rememberer and the remembered, the copulator and the copulated, and the commanding Creator is the commanded creation. He is described with every attribute of existence, praise and blame, and the worshipers of idols worshiped none other than Him, and there is no existent distinct from Him at all according to them. This is the ultimate conduct of these atheists.

The reality of their statement - its reality is the statement of Pharaoh, because Pharaoh inwardly knew that what he said was false, and Pharaoh's statement was denial intending dominance and corruption. Therefore he denied the existence of the Creator entirely. As for these, they are ignorant misled people who think that what they say is the reality of affirming the Lord and magnifying Him, but it is in reality the statement of Pharaoh. For Pharaoh did not deny the existence of this world, nor did he deny that existent things share in the meaning of 'existence', but he denied that this existence has a distinct Creator above it. Therefore he ordered the building of a tower to give the lie to Moses, claiming that the world has a god above him. Allah said: 'And Pharaoh said: O Haman, build for me a tower that I may reach the ways - the ways of the heavens - and look upon the god of Moses; but indeed I think he is a liar.' And thus were made fair-seeming to Pharaoh the evil of his deed, and he was turned away from the way; and the plot of Pharaoh was not but in ruin. And Allah said: 'And Pharaoh said: O eminent ones, I have not known for you a god other than me. So kindle for me, O Haman, upon the fire of clay, and make for me a tower that I may look upon the god of Moses; and indeed I think he is of the liars.' And he and his soldiers were arrogant in the land without right and thought that they would not be returned to Us. So We seized him and his soldiers and cast them into the sea. So see how was the end of the wrongdoers. And We made them leaders inviting to the Fire, and on the Day of Resurrection they will not be helped. And We followed them in this world with a curse, and on the Day of Resurrection they will be of the abhorred.'

Most of these atheists who affirm the unity of existence say that Pharaoh is more perfect than Moses, and that Pharaoh was truthful in his statement 'I am your highest lord', because existence is excellent and inferior, and the excellent deserves to be the lord of the inferior. And among them are those who say: he died as a believer, and his drowning was for him to perform the bath of Islam. For along with their statement that existence is one, they may either say the saying of some of them: that affirmation is other than existence, and that the quiddities of possibles are fixed, and that the existence of the Real dominates them, as Ibn Arabi and others say; or they distinguish between the absolute and the determined, as his associate al-Qunawi says; and Ibn Sab'in's statement is close to this. He has expanded discussion on them elsewhere; they are only mentioned here because these are the last ranks of the philosopher Sufis who claim to be people of verification and gnosis, and everyone else is deficient compared to them. I have seen more than one of these.

They rank people into levels: the lowest according to them is the jurist, then the theologian, then the philosopher, then the Sufi - i.e., the Sufi of the philosophers, then the verifier. They place Ibn Sina and his likes among the philosophers in the second level, and Abu Hamid and his likes among the Sufis in the tenth, and they make the verifier the one.

Therefore Ibn Arabi mentioned in al-Futuhat four creeds: first, the creed of Abu al-Ma'ali and his likes stripped of evidence; then this creed with its evidence; then the creed of the philosophers; then the creed of the verifiers. That is because the philosopher distinguishes between existence, the possible, and the necessary, while these say 'existence is one'. The Sufi whom these venerate is the Sufi whom Ibn Sina venerated; afterwards is the verifier.

These are not Muslims, nor Jews, nor Christians; rather many of the polytheists are better than them. Their situation is their association with the people of innovation and desires. These are the leaders of the speculative philosopher-sufis and their followers, and they were among the causes of their dominance.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the monist doctrine (wahdat al-wujud) as espoused by Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and their followers. Ibn Taymiyya begins by describing the concept of 'fana' (annihilation) as they understand it: not seeing anything but Allah, to the point where all distinctions between Creator and creation, worshiper and worshiped, are abolished. This, he argues, leads to outright atheism (ilhad). He then draws a powerful analogical argument: their statement is essentially the same as Pharaoh's claim 'I am your highest lord'. He explains that Pharaoh did not deny the existence of the world or that things share in existence; he denied a distinct Creator above the world. Similarly, the monists affirm existence but deny any real distinction between the Necessary Being and contingent beings. Ibn Taymiyya then notes that these monists go so far as to praise Pharaoh, claiming he was more perfect than Moses and died a believer. He highlights their diverse internal views: some (like Ibn Arabi) distinguish between 'thubut' (fixity) and 'wujud' (existence), others (like al-Qunawi) distinguish between the absolute and the determined. Yet all ultimately deny the distinct reality of the Creator. Ibn Taymiyya then presents their hierarchical ranking of people: jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi (of the philosophers), and finally the 'verifier' (muhaqqiq) — a rank reserved for the monist elite. He cites Ibn Arabi's classification of four creeds, showing that the monists place themselves above all others, including mainstream Ash'ari theologians and philosophers like Ibn Sina. Finally, Ibn Taymiyya condemns them as outside the pale of Islam, worse than polytheists, and associates them with ahl al-bid'a wa al-ahwa' (people of innovation and desires). The argument is structured as a sustained critique: first exposing the dangerous implication of their core doctrine, then comparing it to the archetypal rejection of the Creator (Pharaoh), then documenting their internal absurdities and arrogant rankings, and finally issuing a decisive verdict on their religious status.

وحدة الوجود
فناء
المحقق

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya refutes monist fana' by showing that it collapses the Creator-creature distinction, leading logically to atheism.

Ibn Taymiyya's Analogical Argument: Monists and Pharaoh
Ibn Taymiyya draws an analogical argument between the monist doctrine and Pharaoh's rejection of a distinct Creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's analogical argument linking the monist doctrine to the statement of Pharaoh, and evaluate its rhetorical and logical strength.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya exposes monist 'unity of existence' as a repackaged version of Pharaoh's denial of a distinct Creator.

Ibn Taymiyya does not merely describe the monist error; he compares it directly to the archetype of kufr: Pharaoh. He argues that both Pharaoh and the monists affirm existence but deny a distinct Creator above it. This lesson unpacks that comparison.

Guided Path
1
Identify the comparison terms
What exactly does Ibn Taymiyya compare? (monist doctrine vs Pharaoh's statement)
2
Understand the common element
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what did Pharaoh affirm about existence? What did he deny?
Pharaoh did not deny the existence of the world or the shared meaning of existence; he denied a distinct Creator above.
3
Map the analogy
The monists affirm existence is one; Pharaoh also did not deny existence of the world. Both deny a distinct Creator above.
4
Note the difference
Pharaoh knew he was wrong; the monists are ignorant and think they are affirming the Lord.
Ibn Taymiyya mentions this to show the monists are even more misguided.
5
Assess the strength of the analogy
Does Ibn Taymiyya's comparison hold? Why is it effective?
The analogy is strong because it cuts to the core theological error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فناء أهل ولهذا لما سلك ابن عربي وابن سبعين وغيرهما هذه الطريق الفاسدة أورثهم ذلك «الفناء عن وجود السوى». فجعلوا الموجود واحداً ووجود كل مخلوق هو عين وجود الحق. وحقيقة «الفناء» عندهم أن لا يرى إلا الحق، وهو الرائي والمرئي، والعابد والمعبود، والذاكر والمذكور، والناكح والمنكوح والأمرُ الخالق هو الأمر المخلوق. وهو المتصف بكل ما يوصف به الوجود من مدح وذم وعُبَّاد الأصنام ما عبدوا غيره، وما ثَمَّ موجود مُغاير له البتة عندهم . وهذا منتهى سلوك هؤلاء الملحدين .

حقيقة قولهم فحقيقته قول فرعون لأن فرعون كان في الباطن عالماً بأن ما يقوله باطل، وكان قول فرعون جاحداً مُريداً للعلو والفساد. ولهذا جحد وجود الصانع بالكلية. وأما هؤلاء فجُهّال ضلال يحسبون أن ما يقولونه هو حقيقة إثبات الرب، وتعميمه، وهو في الحقيقة قول فرعون . فإن فرعون ما كان ينكر وجود هذا العالم، ولا ينكر أن الموجودات تشترك في مسمى «الوجود» ، وإنما كان ينكر أن لهذا الوجود خالقاً مبايناً له. ولهذا أمر ببناء الصَّرْح ليكذب موسى بزعمه أن للعالم إلها فوقه . قال تعالى : ( وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَنهَمَنُ ابْنِ لِي صَرْحًا لَعَلَى أَبْلُغُ الأَسْبَبَ أَسْبَابَ السَّمَوَاتِ فَأَطَّلِعَ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّه كَذِبًا وَكَذَلِكَ زُيِّنَ لِفِرْعَوْنَ سُوهُ عَمَلِهِ، وَصُدَّ عَنِ السَّبِيلِ وَمَا كَيْدُ فِرْعَوْنَ إِلَّا فِي تَبَابِ ﴾ [سورة غافر : ٣٦ - ٣٧] . وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَتَأَيُّهَا الْمَلَأُ مَا عَلِمْتُ لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرِي فَأَوْقِدْ لِي يَهَمَنُ عَلَى الطِينِ فَاجْعَل فِي صَرْحًا لَعَلَّى أَطَّلِعُ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّهُ مِنَ الْكَذِبِينَ ) وَاسْتَكْبَرَ هُوَ وَجُنُودُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ وَظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا يُرْجَعُونَ ) فَأَخَذْنَهُ وَجُنُودَهُ فَنَبَذْنَهُمْ فِي الْبَرِّ فَانظُرْ كَيْفَ كَانَ عَقِبَةُ الظَّالِمِينَ ( وَجَعَلْتَهُمْ أَبِمَّةٌ يَدْعُونَ إِلَى النَّارِ وَيَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ لَا يُنصَرُونَ الله وأتبعنَهُمْ فِي هَذِهِ الدُّنْيَا لَعَنَةً وَيَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ هُم مِن الْمَقْبُوحِينَ ﴾ [سورة القصص : ٣٨ - ٤٢] .

وأكثر هؤلاء الملاحدة القائلين بوحدة الوجود يقولون إن فرعون أكمل من موسى، وإن فرعون صادق في قوله «أنا ربكم الأعلى» ، لأن الوجود فاضل ومفضول، والفاضل يستحق أن يكون ربَّ المفضول. ومنهم من يقول : مات مؤمناً، وإن تغريقه كان ليغتسل غُسل الإسلام فإنهم مع قولهم بأن الوجود واحد قد يقولون إما بقول بعضهم: إن الثبوت غيرُ الوجود، وإن ماهيات الممكنات ثابتة، وإن وجود الحق قاض عليها، كما يقول ذلك ابن عربي وغيره ؛ وإما أن يفرق بين المطلق والمعين، كما يقوله صاحبه القُونَوي ؛ وابنُ سبعين قوله قريب من هذا وقد بسط الكلام عليهم في غير هذا الموضع، وإنما ذُكروا هنا لأن هؤلاء هم آخر مراتب فلاسفة الصوفية الذين يقولون إنهم أهل التحقيق والعرفان وكل من سواهم عندهم ناقص بالنسبة إليهم. وقد رأيتُ من هؤلاء غير واحد .

وهم يرتبون الناس طبقات، أدناها عندهم الفقيه، ثم المتكلم، ثم الفيلسوف، ثم الصوفي - أي صوفي الفلاسفة ثم المحقق ويجعلون ابن سينا وأمثاله من الفلاسفة في الطبقة الثانية، وأبا حامد وأمثاله من الصوفية من العشرة، ويجعلون المحقق هو الواحد .

ولهذا ذكر ابن عربي في الفتوحات له أربع عقائد الأول: عقيدة أبي المعالي وأمثاله مجردة عن الحجة، ثم هذه العقيدة بحجتها، ثم عقيدة الفلاسفة، ثم عقيدة المحققين . وذلك أن الفيلسوف يفرّق بين الوجود والممكن، والواجب، وهؤلاء يقولون «الوجود واحد». والصوفي الذي يعظمه هؤلاء هو الصوفي الذي عظمه ابن سينا. وبعده المحقق .

وهؤلاء ليسوا مسلمين ولا يهوداً ولا نصارى بل كثير من المشركين أحسن منهم . حالهم اشتراكهم مع أهل البدع والأهواء وهؤلاء أئمة النظار المتفلسفة وصوفيتهم وشيعتهم كان من أسباب تسلطهم
The annihilation of the people - that is why when Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and others followed this corrupt path, it bequeathed to them 'annihilation from the existence of other'. So they made existence one, and the existence of every creature is the very existence of the Real. The reality of 'annihilation' according to them is that one sees only the Real, and He is the seer and the seen, the worshiper and the worshipped, the rememberer and the remembered, the copulator and the copulated, and the commanding Creator is the commanded creation. He is described with every attribute of existence, praise and blame, and the worshipers of idols worshiped none other than Him, and there is no existent distinct from Him at all according to them. This is the ultimate conduct of these atheists.

The reality of their statement - its reality is the statement of Pharaoh, because Pharaoh inwardly knew that what he said was false, and Pharaoh's statement was denial intending dominance and corruption. Therefore he denied the existence of the Creator entirely. As for these, they are ignorant misled people who think that what they say is the reality of affirming the Lord and magnifying Him, but it is in reality the statement of Pharaoh. For Pharaoh did not deny the existence of this world, nor did he deny that existent things share in the meaning of 'existence', but he denied that this existence has a distinct Creator above it. Therefore he ordered the building of a tower to give the lie to Moses, claiming that the world has a god above him. Allah said: 'And Pharaoh said: O Haman, build for me a tower that I may reach the ways - the ways of the heavens - and look upon the god of Moses; but indeed I think he is a liar.' And thus were made fair-seeming to Pharaoh the evil of his deed, and he was turned away from the way; and the plot of Pharaoh was not but in ruin. And Allah said: 'And Pharaoh said: O eminent ones, I have not known for you a god other than me. So kindle for me, O Haman, upon the fire of clay, and make for me a tower that I may look upon the god of Moses; and indeed I think he is of the liars.' And he and his soldiers were arrogant in the land without right and thought that they would not be returned to Us. So We seized him and his soldiers and cast them into the sea. So see how was the end of the wrongdoers. And We made them leaders inviting to the Fire, and on the Day of Resurrection they will not be helped. And We followed them in this world with a curse, and on the Day of Resurrection they will be of the abhorred.'

Most of these atheists who affirm the unity of existence say that Pharaoh is more perfect than Moses, and that Pharaoh was truthful in his statement 'I am your highest lord', because existence is excellent and inferior, and the excellent deserves to be the lord of the inferior. And among them are those who say: he died as a believer, and his drowning was for him to perform the bath of Islam. For along with their statement that existence is one, they may either say the saying of some of them: that affirmation is other than existence, and that the quiddities of possibles are fixed, and that the existence of the Real dominates them, as Ibn Arabi and others say; or they distinguish between the absolute and the determined, as his associate al-Qunawi says; and Ibn Sab'in's statement is close to this. He has expanded discussion on them elsewhere; they are only mentioned here because these are the last ranks of the philosopher Sufis who claim to be people of verification and gnosis, and everyone else is deficient compared to them. I have seen more than one of these.

They rank people into levels: the lowest according to them is the jurist, then the theologian, then the philosopher, then the Sufi - i.e., the Sufi of the philosophers, then the verifier. They place Ibn Sina and his likes among the philosophers in the second level, and Abu Hamid and his likes among the Sufis in the tenth, and they make the verifier the one.

Therefore Ibn Arabi mentioned in al-Futuhat four creeds: first, the creed of Abu al-Ma'ali and his likes stripped of evidence; then this creed with its evidence; then the creed of the philosophers; then the creed of the verifiers. That is because the philosopher distinguishes between existence, the possible, and the necessary, while these say 'existence is one'. The Sufi whom these venerate is the Sufi whom Ibn Sina venerated; afterwards is the verifier.

These are not Muslims, nor Jews, nor Christians; rather many of the polytheists are better than them. Their situation is their association with the people of innovation and desires. These are the leaders of the speculative philosopher-sufis and their followers, and they were among the causes of their dominance.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the monist doctrine (wahdat al-wujud) as espoused by Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and their followers. Ibn Taymiyya begins by describing the concept of 'fana' (annihilation) as they understand it: not seeing anything but Allah, to the point where all distinctions between Creator and creation, worshiper and worshiped, are abolished. This, he argues, leads to outright atheism (ilhad). He then draws a powerful analogical argument: their statement is essentially the same as Pharaoh's claim 'I am your highest lord'. He explains that Pharaoh did not deny the existence of the world or that things share in existence; he denied a distinct Creator above the world. Similarly, the monists affirm existence but deny any real distinction between the Necessary Being and contingent beings. Ibn Taymiyya then notes that these monists go so far as to praise Pharaoh, claiming he was more perfect than Moses and died a believer. He highlights their diverse internal views: some (like Ibn Arabi) distinguish between 'thubut' (fixity) and 'wujud' (existence), others (like al-Qunawi) distinguish between the absolute and the determined. Yet all ultimately deny the distinct reality of the Creator. Ibn Taymiyya then presents their hierarchical ranking of people: jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi (of the philosophers), and finally the 'verifier' (muhaqqiq) — a rank reserved for the monist elite. He cites Ibn Arabi's classification of four creeds, showing that the monists place themselves above all others, including mainstream Ash'ari theologians and philosophers like Ibn Sina. Finally, Ibn Taymiyya condemns them as outside the pale of Islam, worse than polytheists, and associates them with ahl al-bid'a wa al-ahwa' (people of innovation and desires). The argument is structured as a sustained critique: first exposing the dangerous implication of their core doctrine, then comparing it to the archetypal rejection of the Creator (Pharaoh), then documenting their internal absurdities and arrogant rankings, and finally issuing a decisive verdict on their religious status.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Pharaoh deny that the monists also deny?
A) The existence of the world
B) The existence of a distinct Creator above the world
C) The existence of a soul
D) The reality of good and evil

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's analogical argument shows that the monist doctrine is functionally equivalent to Pharaoh's faith denial, despite its claims to affirm the Lord.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's analogical argument in your own words, identifying the asl, hukm, illa, and fara.
?
Find another example in Islamic theology where an analogical argument is used to refute a heretical position (e.g., the Jahmiyya). Write down the comparison.

The Monist Hierarchy and Ibn Taymiyya's Verdict of Kufr
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the monist hierarchy and declares them outside the pale of Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the monist hierarchy of knowledge (jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi, verifier) and explain Ibn Taymiyya's verdict that they are outside of Islam.

Core Idea
The monists rank themselves above all Muslims, but Ibn Taymiyya exposes their claims as self-serving and their status as worse than polytheists.

Ibn Taymiyya reports how the monists organize people into layers: the jurist, theologian, philosopher, the Sufi of the philosophers, and finally the 'verifier' (muhaqqiq) – themselves. He then delivers a decisive judgment: they are not Muslims, Jews, or Christians; indeed many polytheists are better than them. This lesson examines that judgment.

Guided Path
1
List the hierarchy
What are the five ranks the monists recognize? (jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi of the philosophers, verifier)
2
Identify the position of mainstream scholars
Where do they place Ibn Sina and Abu Hamid al-Ghazali? What does that show?
Ibn Sina is in the second level, al-Ghazali in the tenth. This shows their disdain for mainstream scholarship.
3
Understand the classification of creeds
What four creeds does Ibn Arabi list in al-Futuhat? Where do the monists place themselves?
The fourth creed is that of the verifiers, i.e., themselves.
4
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's verdict
What specific wording does he use to declare them outside Islam? (e.g., 'ليسوا مسلمين ولا يهوداً ولا نصارى')
5
Evaluate the basis for his verdict
Why does he consider them worse than polytheists? Because they associate themselves with ahl al-bid'a wa al-ahwa'.

فناء أهل ولهذا لما سلك ابن عربي وابن سبعين وغيرهما هذه الطريق الفاسدة أورثهم ذلك «الفناء عن وجود السوى». فجعلوا الموجود واحداً ووجود كل مخلوق هو عين وجود الحق. وحقيقة «الفناء» عندهم أن لا يرى إلا الحق، وهو الرائي والمرئي، والعابد والمعبود، والذاكر والمذكور، والناكح والمنكوح والأمرُ الخالق هو الأمر المخلوق. وهو المتصف بكل ما يوصف به الوجود من مدح وذم وعُبَّاد الأصنام ما عبدوا غيره، وما ثَمَّ موجود مُغاير له البتة عندهم . وهذا منتهى سلوك هؤلاء الملحدين .

حقيقة قولهم فحقيقته قول فرعون لأن فرعون كان في الباطن عالماً بأن ما يقوله باطل، وكان قول فرعون جاحداً مُريداً للعلو والفساد. ولهذا جحد وجود الصانع بالكلية. وأما هؤلاء فجُهّال ضلال يحسبون أن ما يقولونه هو حقيقة إثبات الرب، وتعميمه، وهو في الحقيقة قول فرعون . فإن فرعون ما كان ينكر وجود هذا العالم، ولا ينكر أن الموجودات تشترك في مسمى «الوجود» ، وإنما كان ينكر أن لهذا الوجود خالقاً مبايناً له. ولهذا أمر ببناء الصَّرْح ليكذب موسى بزعمه أن للعالم إلها فوقه . قال تعالى : ( وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَنهَمَنُ ابْنِ لِي صَرْحًا لَعَلَى أَبْلُغُ الأَسْبَبَ أَسْبَابَ السَّمَوَاتِ فَأَطَّلِعَ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّه كَذِبًا وَكَذَلِكَ زُيِّنَ لِفِرْعَوْنَ سُوهُ عَمَلِهِ، وَصُدَّ عَنِ السَّبِيلِ وَمَا كَيْدُ فِرْعَوْنَ إِلَّا فِي تَبَابِ ﴾ [سورة غافر : ٣٦ - ٣٧] . وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَقَالَ فِرْعَوْنُ يَتَأَيُّهَا الْمَلَأُ مَا عَلِمْتُ لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرِي فَأَوْقِدْ لِي يَهَمَنُ عَلَى الطِينِ فَاجْعَل فِي صَرْحًا لَعَلَّى أَطَّلِعُ إِلَى إِلَهِ مُوسَى وَإِنِّي لَأَظُنُّهُ مِنَ الْكَذِبِينَ ) وَاسْتَكْبَرَ هُوَ وَجُنُودُهُ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ وَظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ إِلَيْنَا لَا يُرْجَعُونَ ) فَأَخَذْنَهُ وَجُنُودَهُ فَنَبَذْنَهُمْ فِي الْبَرِّ فَانظُرْ كَيْفَ كَانَ عَقِبَةُ الظَّالِمِينَ ( وَجَعَلْتَهُمْ أَبِمَّةٌ يَدْعُونَ إِلَى النَّارِ وَيَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ لَا يُنصَرُونَ الله وأتبعنَهُمْ فِي هَذِهِ الدُّنْيَا لَعَنَةً وَيَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ هُم مِن الْمَقْبُوحِينَ ﴾ [سورة القصص : ٣٨ - ٤٢] .

وأكثر هؤلاء الملاحدة القائلين بوحدة الوجود يقولون إن فرعون أكمل من موسى، وإن فرعون صادق في قوله «أنا ربكم الأعلى» ، لأن الوجود فاضل ومفضول، والفاضل يستحق أن يكون ربَّ المفضول. ومنهم من يقول : مات مؤمناً، وإن تغريقه كان ليغتسل غُسل الإسلام فإنهم مع قولهم بأن الوجود واحد قد يقولون إما بقول بعضهم: إن الثبوت غيرُ الوجود، وإن ماهيات الممكنات ثابتة، وإن وجود الحق قاض عليها، كما يقول ذلك ابن عربي وغيره ؛ وإما أن يفرق بين المطلق والمعين، كما يقوله صاحبه القُونَوي ؛ وابنُ سبعين قوله قريب من هذا وقد بسط الكلام عليهم في غير هذا الموضع، وإنما ذُكروا هنا لأن هؤلاء هم آخر مراتب فلاسفة الصوفية الذين يقولون إنهم أهل التحقيق والعرفان وكل من سواهم عندهم ناقص بالنسبة إليهم. وقد رأيتُ من هؤلاء غير واحد .

وهم يرتبون الناس طبقات، أدناها عندهم الفقيه، ثم المتكلم، ثم الفيلسوف، ثم الصوفي - أي صوفي الفلاسفة ثم المحقق ويجعلون ابن سينا وأمثاله من الفلاسفة في الطبقة الثانية، وأبا حامد وأمثاله من الصوفية من العشرة، ويجعلون المحقق هو الواحد .

ولهذا ذكر ابن عربي في الفتوحات له أربع عقائد الأول: عقيدة أبي المعالي وأمثاله مجردة عن الحجة، ثم هذه العقيدة بحجتها، ثم عقيدة الفلاسفة، ثم عقيدة المحققين . وذلك أن الفيلسوف يفرّق بين الوجود والممكن، والواجب، وهؤلاء يقولون «الوجود واحد». والصوفي الذي يعظمه هؤلاء هو الصوفي الذي عظمه ابن سينا. وبعده المحقق .

وهؤلاء ليسوا مسلمين ولا يهوداً ولا نصارى بل كثير من المشركين أحسن منهم . حالهم اشتراكهم مع أهل البدع والأهواء وهؤلاء أئمة النظار المتفلسفة وصوفيتهم وشيعتهم كان من أسباب تسلطهم
The annihilation of the people - that is why when Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and others followed this corrupt path, it bequeathed to them 'annihilation from the existence of other'. So they made existence one, and the existence of every creature is the very existence of the Real. The reality of 'annihilation' according to them is that one sees only the Real, and He is the seer and the seen, the worshiper and the worshipped, the rememberer and the remembered, the copulator and the copulated, and the commanding Creator is the commanded creation. He is described with every attribute of existence, praise and blame, and the worshipers of idols worshiped none other than Him, and there is no existent distinct from Him at all according to them. This is the ultimate conduct of these atheists.

The reality of their statement - its reality is the statement of Pharaoh, because Pharaoh inwardly knew that what he said was false, and Pharaoh's statement was denial intending dominance and corruption. Therefore he denied the existence of the Creator entirely. As for these, they are ignorant misled people who think that what they say is the reality of affirming the Lord and magnifying Him, but it is in reality the statement of Pharaoh. For Pharaoh did not deny the existence of this world, nor did he deny that existent things share in the meaning of 'existence', but he denied that this existence has a distinct Creator above it. Therefore he ordered the building of a tower to give the lie to Moses, claiming that the world has a god above him. Allah said: 'And Pharaoh said: O Haman, build for me a tower that I may reach the ways - the ways of the heavens - and look upon the god of Moses; but indeed I think he is a liar.' And thus were made fair-seeming to Pharaoh the evil of his deed, and he was turned away from the way; and the plot of Pharaoh was not but in ruin. And Allah said: 'And Pharaoh said: O eminent ones, I have not known for you a god other than me. So kindle for me, O Haman, upon the fire of clay, and make for me a tower that I may look upon the god of Moses; and indeed I think he is of the liars.' And he and his soldiers were arrogant in the land without right and thought that they would not be returned to Us. So We seized him and his soldiers and cast them into the sea. So see how was the end of the wrongdoers. And We made them leaders inviting to the Fire, and on the Day of Resurrection they will not be helped. And We followed them in this world with a curse, and on the Day of Resurrection they will be of the abhorred.'

Most of these atheists who affirm the unity of existence say that Pharaoh is more perfect than Moses, and that Pharaoh was truthful in his statement 'I am your highest lord', because existence is excellent and inferior, and the excellent deserves to be the lord of the inferior. And among them are those who say: he died as a believer, and his drowning was for him to perform the bath of Islam. For along with their statement that existence is one, they may either say the saying of some of them: that affirmation is other than existence, and that the quiddities of possibles are fixed, and that the existence of the Real dominates them, as Ibn Arabi and others say; or they distinguish between the absolute and the determined, as his associate al-Qunawi says; and Ibn Sab'in's statement is close to this. He has expanded discussion on them elsewhere; they are only mentioned here because these are the last ranks of the philosopher Sufis who claim to be people of verification and gnosis, and everyone else is deficient compared to them. I have seen more than one of these.

They rank people into levels: the lowest according to them is the jurist, then the theologian, then the philosopher, then the Sufi - i.e., the Sufi of the philosophers, then the verifier. They place Ibn Sina and his likes among the philosophers in the second level, and Abu Hamid and his likes among the Sufis in the tenth, and they make the verifier the one.

Therefore Ibn Arabi mentioned in al-Futuhat four creeds: first, the creed of Abu al-Ma'ali and his likes stripped of evidence; then this creed with its evidence; then the creed of the philosophers; then the creed of the verifiers. That is because the philosopher distinguishes between existence, the possible, and the necessary, while these say 'existence is one'. The Sufi whom these venerate is the Sufi whom Ibn Sina venerated; afterwards is the verifier.

These are not Muslims, nor Jews, nor Christians; rather many of the polytheists are better than them. Their situation is their association with the people of innovation and desires. These are the leaders of the speculative philosopher-sufis and their followers, and they were among the causes of their dominance.
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the monist doctrine (wahdat al-wujud) as espoused by Ibn Arabi, Ibn Sab'in, and their followers. Ibn Taymiyya begins by describing the concept of 'fana' (annihilation) as they understand it: not seeing anything but Allah, to the point where all distinctions between Creator and creation, worshiper and worshiped, are abolished. This, he argues, leads to outright atheism (ilhad). He then draws a powerful analogical argument: their statement is essentially the same as Pharaoh's claim 'I am your highest lord'. He explains that Pharaoh did not deny the existence of the world or that things share in existence; he denied a distinct Creator above the world. Similarly, the monists affirm existence but deny any real distinction between the Necessary Being and contingent beings. Ibn Taymiyya then notes that these monists go so far as to praise Pharaoh, claiming he was more perfect than Moses and died a believer. He highlights their diverse internal views: some (like Ibn Arabi) distinguish between 'thubut' (fixity) and 'wujud' (existence), others (like al-Qunawi) distinguish between the absolute and the determined. Yet all ultimately deny the distinct reality of the Creator. Ibn Taymiyya then presents their hierarchical ranking of people: jurist, theologian, philosopher, Sufi (of the philosophers), and finally the 'verifier' (muhaqqiq) — a rank reserved for the monist elite. He cites Ibn Arabi's classification of four creeds, showing that the monists place themselves above all others, including mainstream Ash'ari theologians and philosophers like Ibn Sina. Finally, Ibn Taymiyya condemns them as outside the pale of Islam, worse than polytheists, and associates them with ahl al-bid'a wa al-ahwa' (people of innovation and desires). The argument is structured as a sustained critique: first exposing the dangerous implication of their core doctrine, then comparing it to the archetypal rejection of the Creator (Pharaoh), then documenting their internal absurdities and arrogant rankings, and finally issuing a decisive verdict on their religious status.

Key Terms
المحقق
طبقات الناس
الفلاسفة
الصوفية
الفقيه
المتكلم

B) The theologian
C) The philosopher

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya decisively excludes the monist verifiers from Islam, showing that their self-exaltation masks their fundamental departure from tawhid.

Why Denying God's Will and Power Is Worse
Author argues philosophers' denial of God's will/power is worse than denial of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's comparative argument that denying God's will and power is a graver error than denying His knowledge, and assess his use of historical evidence.

Core Idea
Denying God's will and power places philosophers below even polytheists in correct belief about God.

Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' denial of God's power and will is more severe than their denial of His knowledge of particulars. He supports this by showing that even those ignorant of God's exhaustive knowledge, like the three men in the hadith, affirmed His creative power. Furthermore, the polytheistic Arabs, despite their shirk, acknowledged God as Creator. This makes the philosophers worse than polytheists in this regard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two denials
Note that Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes two types of errors: denial of God's knowledge of particulars and denial of God's power and will. He claims the latter is worse.
This is a comparative critique; the target is the philosophers who deny God's voluntary action.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith of the three men at the Ka'ba. They doubted whether God hears hidden speech, but they had no doubt that God created the universe by His will and power. Their ignorance was only about the scope of God's knowledge.
The Quranic verse rebukes them for assuming God does not know, but they still affirmed His creative power.
3
Assess the polytheist comparison
Ibn Taymiyya points out that even the polytheistic Arabs, who worshipped idols, affirmed that God created the heavens and the earth by His will and power. Thus, the philosophers are in a worse state than these polytheists because they deny what even polytheists affirm.
This is a striking argument: the philosophers fall below the baseline of pagan Arabs in this aspect of theology.
4
Evaluate the argument's force
Consider whether the comparison holds. If even those who associate partners with God still acknowledge His creative power, then denying that power is a more fundamental rejection of divine attributes.
Ibn Taymiyya uses empirical observation of common belief as a yardstick to measure the gravity of error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنكارهم لقدرة الله ومشيئته أعظمُ من إنكارهم لعلمه بالجزئيات. فإن كثيراً من الناس كان لا يعرف ذلك ولكن يعلم أن الله قادر خلق الأشياء بمشيئته، كما في الصحيحين عن ابن مسعود قال : اجتمع عند البيت ثلثة نفر ـ قُرَشِيّان وثَقَفي، أو ثقفيان وقرشي - كثير شحم بطونهم قليل فقه قلوبهم . فقال أحدهم : أترون الله يسمع ما نقول؟ فقال الثاني : يسمع إن جَهَرنا ولا يسمع إن أخفينا. فقال الثالث: «إن كان إذا جهرنا سمعنا فهو إذا أخفينا». فأنزل الله : ﴿وَمَا كُنتُمْ تَسْتَتِرُونَ أَن يَشْهَدَ عَلَيْكُمْ سمعكُمْ وَلَا أَبْصَرُكُمْ وَلَا جُلُودُكُمْ وَلَكِن ظَنَنتُمْ أَنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَعْلَمُ كَثِيرًا مِمَّا تَعْمَلُونَ وَذَلِكُمْ ظَنُّكُمُ الَّذِي ظَنَنتُم بِرَبِّكُمْ أَرْدَنَكُمْ فَأَصْبَحْتُم مِّنَ الْخَسِرِينَ﴾. وهؤلاء كانوا يقرون بأن الله خلق السموات والأرض بمشيئته وقدرته. وكذلك كان بعض أحداث المسلمين قد يجهل هذه المسئلة فيقول : يا رسول الله مهما يكتم الناس يعلمه الله؟ فيقول له النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «نعم». ولم يكن هؤلاء يجهلون أن الله خلق كل شيء بمشيئته وقدرته بل كان هذا من أظهر الأمور وأعرفها عند عامة المسلمين، بل وعامة المشركين الذين كانوا يعبدون الأصنام، وهم كفار وهم مشركون وهم الذين قاتلهم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهم أول من يتناوله ذمّ القرآن للمشركين. ومع هذا فكانوا مُقرّين بأن الله خلق السموات والأرض وما بينهما، وخلق كل شيء بقدرته ومشيئته. فكانوا أحسن حالاً من هؤلاء الفلاسفة في الإقرار بأن الله خالق كل شيء وربه ومليكه، وأنه خلق الأشياء بمشيئته وقدرته.
Indeed, their denial of God's power and will is greater than their denial of His knowledge of particulars. For many people did not know that, but they knew that God is powerful and created things by His will. As in the Two Sahihs from Ibn Mas'ud who said: Three men gathered at the Ka'ba — two Quraysh and one Thaqafi, or two Thaqafi and one Quraysh — with much fat in their bellies and little understanding in their hearts. One said: 'Do you think God hears what we say?' The second said: 'He hears if we speak aloud, but does not hear if we hide.' The third said: 'If when we speak aloud He hears us, then also when we hide.' So Allah revealed: 'And you did not cover yourselves lest your ears, eyes and skins testify against you, but you thought that Allah does not know much of what you do, and that is your thought which you thought about your Lord; it has ruined you, and you have become among the losers.' [Fussilat 41:22-23] And these people affirmed that God created the heavens and the earth by His will and power. Similarly, some young Muslims might be ignorant of this issue and say: 'O Messenger of Allah, whatever people hide, does God know it?' The Prophet said: 'Yes.' And these people were not ignorant that God created everything by His will and power; rather, this was among the most apparent and well-known matters among the common Muslims, and even among the polytheists who worshipped idols, who are disbelievers and polytheists, whom the Prophet fought, and who are the first to be addressed by the Quran's blame of the polytheists. Yet with all this, they affirmed that God created the heavens and the earth and what is between them, and created everything by His power and will. So they were in a better state than these philosophers in affirming that God is the Creator of everything, its Lord and Owner, and that He created things by His will and power.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' denial of God's power and will is an even greater error than their denial of His knowledge of particulars. He supports this by noting that even those who were ignorant of God's exhaustive knowledge, like the three men in the hadith, still affirmed that God creates by His will and power. The story highlights that the men were uncertain about God's hearing of hidden speech, but they had no doubt about God's power to create. Ibn Taymiyya then compares the philosophers unfavorably with Arab polytheists, who, despite their shirk, acknowledged God as Creator. Thus, the philosophers are worse than the polytheists in this regard.

Key Terms
قدرة الله ومشيئته
إنكار
فلاسفة
مشركون

A) That God hears all speech
B) That God created the heavens and earth by His will
C) That God knows all secrets
D) That God punishes sins

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that denying God's will and power is a more serious error than denying His knowledge, because even polytheists acknowledged God's creative power, making the philosophers' denial unprecedented.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of the Philosophers' Heaven Doctrine
Author refutes philosophers' claim that the heavens move by choice without a creator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the philosophers' view of the heavens is worse than the Qadariyya's, and evaluate its logical force.

Core Idea
The philosophers' heaven is self-moving and uncaused, a denial of creation worse than the Qadariyya's.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya levels a devastating critique against the philosophers' (falasifa) conception of the heavens. He compares their position with that of the Qadariyya, a sect already rejected by mainstream Islam, to show that the philosophers are even more misguided. Understanding this critique helps you see how Islamic theology defends the absolute creatorship and sovereignty of Allah against philosophical emanationism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' claim
Locate in the Arabic where the philosophers say the heaven is 'possible' (mumkin) with an 'originator' (mubdi'), moves by choice, and has a celestial soul. Note that they deny any creator above it.
This claim is the target of Ibn Taymiyya's refutation.
2
Understand the Qadariyya position as a foil
Ibn Taymiyya cites the Qadariyya, who believe Allah creates animals and gives them power, allowing them to originate their own actions. This is considered a flawed view by Ahl al-Sunnah.
The Qadariyya at least affirm Allah's creative act, unlike the philosophers.
3
Compare the two views
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' view is 'worse' because they do not treat the heaven as truly created (makhluq), even if they call it 'caused' (ma'lul). Their heaven is self-sufficient in motion, with no external agent.
The comparison is the core of the critique.
4
Evaluate the rational argument
Ibn Taymiyya adds a rational point: a simple, unchanging being (the First) cannot produce diverse, changing events. The philosophers' claim that motion emanates from the First is baseless.
This is a logical objection from the nature of causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولهم أنه شرط في وجود الممكنات لا مبدع لها ولا فاعل. فإنهم لا يثبتون للحوادث محدثاً أصلاً في نفس الأمر، إذ الفلك عندهم ممكن له مبدع، وهو متحرك باختیاره كما يتحرك الإنسان باختياره، وله نفس فلكية كما للإنسان نفس. وليس عندهم فوقه شيء يَحْدُث عنه شيء. القول بأن وإن قالوا: إنه «معلول» فقولهم في الفلك أقبح من قول القدرية في أفعال الحيوان. فإن القدرية يقولون: إن الله خلق الحيوان بقدرته ومشيئته، فجعل له قدرة تصلح للضدين، فهو يحدث إرادته وأفعاله بقدرته ومشيئته. وهؤلاء لا يجعلون الفلك مخلوقاً في الحقيقة وإن قالوا هو معلول. ولو جعلوه مخلوقاً فعندهم هو متحرك حركة اختيارية نفسانية بمشيئة وقوة فيه، وليس فوقه شيء يحدث هذه الحركة ولا يفعلها. وإنما الفلك متحرك للتشبه بالأول لاستخراج أيونته [؟] وأوضاعه، إذ هي غاية كماله. وإن قالوا: إن حركته تصدر عن الأول فكلام لا حقيقة له. فإنهم وكل عاقل يعلم أن الشيء البسيط الذي هو على حال واحدة أزلاً وأبداً لا يحدث عنه شيء، فضلاً عن حوادث مختلفة. ويعلمون أن المتغيرات لا تصدر عن بسيط ألبتة. وهذا كله مبسوط في غير هذا الموضع.
Their saying that [the First] is a condition for the existence of contingent things, not a creator or agent for them. For they do not establish for events any originator at all in reality, since according to them the heaven is contingent having an originator, and it moves by its choice as man moves by his choice, and it has a celestial soul as man has a soul. And according to them there is nothing above it from which something occurs. The saying that even if they say it is 'caused', their saying about the heaven is worse than the Qadariyya's saying about the actions of animals. For the Qadariyya say that Allah created the animal with His power and will, then gave it a power suitable for opposites, so it originates its will and actions by its power and will. But these [philosophers] do not consider the heaven as created in reality, even if they say it is 'caused'. And if they considered it created, according to them it moves with a psychic voluntary motion by will and power within it, and there is nothing above it that originates this motion or does it. Rather, the heaven moves to imitate the First in order to extract its [؟] and its states, for that is its perfection. And if they say its motion emanates from the First, it is speech with no reality. For they and every rational person know that a simple thing that is in one state eternally and everlastingly does not produce anything, let alone diverse events. And they know that changing things do not emanate from a simple thing at all. All of this is elaborated elsewhere.
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of the philosophers' (falasifa) doctrine regarding the heavens. The author (Ibn Taymiyya) begins by summarizing the philosophers' claim: they say the First (al-Awwal) is a condition for existence but not a creator or agent. They do not actually establish a creator for events; rather, they say the heaven (al-falak) is contingent with an originator (mubdi'), but it moves by its own choice, like a human, and has a celestial soul. According to them, there is no being above the heaven that produces events from it. The author then makes a comparison: this view is worse than the Qadariyya's position on animal actions. The Qadariyya (a sect that affirmed human free will) at least say Allah creates the animal with power and will, then gives it a power for opposites, so it originates its own acts. But the philosophers do not truly consider the heaven as created, even if they call it 'caused'. If they did consider it created, they still say it moves voluntarily by its own will and power, with no external agent causing its motion. The only reason they give for its motion is to imitate the First and extract its perfect states. If they claim the motion emanates from the First, it is baseless: a simple, unchanging being cannot produce differing events. The author notes that this argument is elaborated elsewhere, indicating the complexity of the refutation. The passage uses the Islamic science example of the Qadariyya to show inconsistency, and it belongs to the field of kalam and philosophy critique.

Key Terms
معلول
مبدع
قدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn Taymiyya say the philosophers' view on the heaven is worse than the Qadariyya's view on animal actions?
A) The philosophers deny any cause for the heaven's motion.
B) The Qadariyya affirm a creator for the animal's power, but the philosophers deny a creator for the heaven.
C) The philosophers say the heaven moves by force, while the Qadariyya say animals move by will.
D) Ibn Taymiyya actually agrees with the Qadariyya.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique reveals that the philosophical concept of emanation is fundamentally inferior to Islamic creation because it denies Allah's direct creative agency over the heavens.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Compare the philosophers' view of the heaven as a self-moving 'caused' being with the Qadariyya's view of animal actions. In two sentences, explain why Ibn Taymiyya considers the former worse.
?
Construct a simple kalam argument: 'A simple unchanging being cannot produce diverse changing events. The heaven exhibits diverse motions. Therefore, the heaven's motions cannot emanate from a simple unchanging First.' Then identify whether this argument is deductive or inductive.
